201 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Palmer


Docket No. 74935


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


162 Ill. 2d 465; 643 N.E.2d 797; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 143; 205 Ill. Dec. 506



October 20, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied December 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Mason County, the Hon. Thomas L. Brownfield, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Mason County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of felony murder, home invasion, and residential burglary and sentenced defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged an order which convicted him of felony murder, home invasion, and residential burglary and sentenced him to death. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that trial counsel's failure to pursue a plea was a matter of his professional judgment or strategy. Even though counsel's strategy for avoiding the death penalty was unsuccessful, his decision to pursue that particular strategy was not incompetent. The court found no unfairness in the trial court's sentencing considerations because the sentence was noticeably well considered, with the proper focus given to the nature of the offenses and the character of this defendant, as well as his rehabilitative potential.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence of death for the crimes of felony murder, home invasion, and residential burglary because counsel's failure to pursue a plea bargain was a matter of professional judgment or strategy. Although this strategy was unsuccessful, the decision was not incompetent.

 

202 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Enis


Docket No. 72742


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


163 Ill. 2d 367; 645 N.E.2d 856; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 124; 206 Ill. Dec. 604



September 29, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, 01/30/1995
Writ of certiorari denied Enis v. Illinois, 516 U.S. 827, 116 S. Ct. 94, 133 L. Ed. 2d 50, 1995 U.S. LEXIS 5572 (1995)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Without prejudice, Motion denied by, As moot Enis v. Butler, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 167624 (S.D. Ill., Dec. 5, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. Christopher C. Starck, Judge, presiding.
People v. Enis, 139 Ill. 2d 264, 564 N.E.2d 1155, 1990 Ill. LEXIS 135, 151 Ill. Dec. 493 (1990)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which found defendant guilty of murder and which imposed the death sentence following a sentencing hearing.


OVERVIEW: Shortly before defendant was to be tried for the sexual assault of a nurse, the nurse was murdered. Defendant was convicted for her murder and sentenced to death, but the court reversed and remanded for retrial. Defendant was again convicted and sentenced to death, and the court affirmed the trial court's rulings. There was no error in the trial court's denial of reconsideration of its ruling denying defendant's motions to quash and suppress evidence in the absence of new evidence, as defendant did not raise the issues at his first appeal. Admission of the sexual assault was admissible to show defendant's motive. The arrest was proper, as defendant was not immediately and improperly arrested as he contended, but rather he had agreed to go to the station with officers, and his counsel was told that defendant was not under arrest at that time. Eyewitness testimony was independently reliable to overcome a suggestive photo showing because of the witness's independent recollection, their opportunity to see defendant, and their certainty. There was ample evidence from which a jury could have reasonably found defendant guilty based on eyewitness testimony and defendant's motive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction and sentence, as the sexual assault was admissible to show defendant's motive. Where defendant's counsel was told that defendant was not under arrest at the time defendant contended, the arrest was proper. A suggestive photo showing was overcome by independently reliable eyewitness testimony due to the witness's independent recollection, their opportunity to see defendant, and their certainty.

 

203 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Novak


Docket No. 75279


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


163 Ill. 2d 93; 643 N.E.2d 762; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 113; 205 Ill. Dec. 471



September 22, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied December 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First Distrct; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Paul T. Foxgrover, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the Appellate Court for the First District of Illinois, which convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual assault and sentenced him to a prison term of 11 years, followed by a mandatory supervised release period of three years.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated criminal sexual assault and sentenced to a prison term of 11 years, followed by a mandatory supervised release of three years. The court allowed appellant's petition for leave to appeal. Appellant contended that he did not receive a fair trial because the trial judge erroneously allowed lay opinion witnesses to testify to matters beyond the scope of their personal knowledge; erroneously refused appellant's tendered jury instruction on aggravated criminal sexual abuse as a lesser included offense of aggravated criminal sexual assault; and used erroneous Illinois Pattern Jury Instructions concerning other-crimes and out-of-court statements by the child-victim to his mother. The court initially concluded that the testimony of the individuals in this case went beyond the scope of lay witness opinion testimony and their testimony was admissible as expert testimony. Through education, training, experience, or a combination of each, the witnesses possessed knowledge that was not common to the average citizen. Further, this knowledge aided the jury in reaching this conclusion. The court could not say that the trial court abused its discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court, which convicted appellant of aggravated criminal sexual assault. The court held that the testimony of certain witnesses was admissible as expert testimony because the witnesses possessed knowledge that was not common to the average citizen.

 

204 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. Gainer


Docket No. 75806


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


162 Ill. 2d 15; 642 N.E.2d 114; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 114; 204 Ill. Dec. 652



September 22, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Johnson County, the Hon. James R. Williamson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Johnson County (Illinois) which granted appellee inmate declaratory and injunctive relief in his action against appellant state officials alleging that 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-4-3(a)(3), (c), requiring prisoners previously convicted of sexual offenses to submit a specimen of blood for genetic marker indexing prior to their release, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: An inmate was serving an indeterminate sentence for sexual offense convictions that predated the enactment of 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-4-3(a)(3), (c). The inmate was eligible for parole, but refused to provide a specimen of blood required under the statute for genetic marker indexing. The inmate filed an action for declaratory and injunctive relief under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and Ill. Code Civ. P., 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-701 (1992). The trial court ruled that the sections were unconstitutional because they were retroactive and violated the Ex Post Facto and Due Process clauses of the United States and Illinois Constitutions. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-4-3(c) was a timing provision rather than an enforcement mechanism. The statute provided only that the inmate was required to provide a specimen of his blood at a certain time, that being prior to his release. The state could forcibly seize a specimen of the inmate's blood. Thus, nothing prevented the blood sample from being taken prior to the inmate's release from prison and the requirement did not impose a delay on an inmate's release.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court which granted declaratory and injunctive relief to the inmate on his action against state officials seeking a ruling that a statute requiring him to provide a specimen of blood for genetic marker indexing before his release from prison was unconstitutional.

 

205 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Williams


Docket No. 71994


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


164 Ill. 2d 1; 645 N.E.2d 844; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 121; 206 Ill. Dec. 592



September 22, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Shelvin Singer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted her of first-degree murder in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a)(1) and robbery in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 18-1(a), denied her post-trial motions for a new trial and judgment non obstante verdicto, and sentenced her to death pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(b)(6).


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of first-degree murder and robbery and after considering mitigating and aggravating factors pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(c), sentenced defendant to death, finding no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude the imposition of the death sentence. Defendant appealed, raising several issues and the court affirmed. The court found that the circuit court's determination that defendant was not arrested at the time in question was not manifestly erroneous, because defendant went to and stayed at the police station for questioning voluntarily. The record contained no evidence whatsoever that if the initial officer entertained the belief that defendant was not free to leave, it was communicated to defendant in any way. The court's review of the record in no way suggested that the conduct of the trial court impeded the selection of an impartial jury. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting it into evidence hearsay testimony that defendant had committed three robberies. Having already determined Illinois's death penalty statute was not unconstitutional, the court declined to reconsider the question.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for first-degree murder and robbery was affirmed, along with the resulting sentence of death. The court determined that defendant had not been subject to unreasonable search and seizure, had not been deprived of a fair trial, and that the trial court had properly considered both aggravating and mitigating factors in the imposition of the death sentence.

Chicago Bar Ass'n v. Illinois State Bd. of Elections


Docket Nos. 77405, 77566 cons.c


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


161 Ill. 2d 502; 641 N.E.2d 525; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 109; 204 Ill. Dec. 301



September 7, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Nos. 77405, 77566 -- Original action for mandamus in the Illinois Supreme Court, consolidated with an appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Dorothy Kinnaird, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 77405 - Petition dismissed. No. 77566 - Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant election boards brought an action for mandamus consolidated with an appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, (Illinois) to review a judgment preventing various public officials from placing the proposed amendment on the general election ballot.


OVERVIEW: Appellant election boards brought an action in mandamus and consolidated an appeal from the trial court regarding the proposed amendment on the general election ballot. The Proponents seek to impose a limit on the number of years a State legislator may serve in the General Assembly. The Proponents obtained more than the required number of voters' signatures and filed the petition with appellant. Appellee bar association brought two legal proceedings. In the mandamus proceeding, the court allowed appellee's motion or leave to file its petition for the writ. In the taxpayer action, the trial court entered an order in favor of the appellee. On appeal, the court dismissed the mandamus proceeding. Further, the court found that it was clear that the proposed amendment did not meet the structural and procedural requirement of Ill. Const. art. XIV, § 3. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the mandamus proceeding and affirmed the trial court's judgment because it was clear that the proposed amendment did not meet the structural and procedural requirement of the constitution.

 

207 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Adams


Docket Nos. 75111, 75654 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


161 Ill. 2d 333; 641 N.E.2d 514; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 102; 204 Ill. Dec. 290



August 4, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 3, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 75111. Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Michael P. Toomin, Judge, presiding.

No. 75654. Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Mary Maxwell Thomas, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed decisions from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed the separate convictions of defendants for possession of a stolen vehicle and possession of controlled substances, contending it was error to conclude that the state failed to meet its burden of establishing venue beyond a reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were separately convicted of possession of a stolen motor vehicle and possession of controlled substances. On appeal, the convictions were reversed based upon findings that the state failed to establish venue in each case beyond a reasonable doubt. The state sought review and the court reversed the judgments, finding that venue was a material allegation of each offense that had to be proved by the state beyond a reasonable doubt, along with the other elements of the charged offenses. The court found that such burden was met by the state. The court concluded that the wrong standard was used below in reviewing the convictions because the guilty verdicts could not be reversed unless the evidence, viewed in the light most favorable to the state, was so palpably contrary to the verdict, and was so unreasonable, improbable, or unsatisfactory as to create a reasonable doubt of defendants' guilt. The court found that, in reviewing the evidence, the state established beyond a reasonable doubt that the offenses occurred within the charging jurisdictions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments overturning defendants' convictions and remanded the causes for consideration of the remaining issues raised by the parties but not yet considered.

Doe v. Calumet City


Docket No. 75347


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


161 Ill. 2d 374; 641 N.E.2d 498; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 107; 204 Ill. Dec. 274



August 4, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 3, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Dean Sodaro, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother and children filed an action against appellee city and police for negligence, intentional infliction of emotional distress, and liability for gender discrimination under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 (1982). The circuit court granted defendants' motion to dismiss and the Appellate Court for the First District affirmed. The mother and children challenged the order dismissing their complaint.


OVERVIEW: The mother and children were attacked at night while they slept. One of the children was raped and the mother was beaten. On appeal the court held that the children's negligence action was properly dismissed, because the police were protected by immunity granted under the Tort Immunity Act (Act). The court found that the children had not established a "special relationship" in order to fall within an exception to the Act. The court reasoned that the children had not shown that they were under the direct and immediate control of the police when the injuries occurred. The court also found that the mother had stated a cause of action for emotional distress. The court reasoned that the police disregarded a high probability that his conduct would cause severe emotional distress. The facts indicated that the officer ignored pleas of the mother to help her children. Finally, the court found that the children had stated a cause of action under the "wilful and wanton" exception to the Act. The court reasoned that this exception did not require the children to prove a special relationship.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the order that dismissed the children's action for negligence and reversed the part of the order that dismissed the other causes of action. The cause was remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

Forest Preserve Dist. v. West Suburban Bank


Docket No. 76143


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


161 Ill. 2d 448; 641 N.E.2d 493; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 104; 204 Ill. Dec. 269



August 4, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing October 3, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. William E. Black, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a forest preservation district, obtained an injunction against defendant landowners in the trial court, which prohibited the landowners from building a parking lot while a condemnation proceeding was pending. The Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois) reversed the trial court's order granting the injunction and the preservation district appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowners claimed that the forest preservation district had taken their land without compensation by obtaining the injunction in violation of Ill. Const. art. I, § 15 (1970), U.S. Const. amend. V. The forest preservation district claimed that it did not take the landowners' property without just compensation, because the injunction allowed the landowners to continue using their land for farming. The court reversed the appellate court decision that had reversed the trial court's order granting the injunction and remanded to the appellate court to consider other matters regarding the injunction, holding that the injunction obtained by the district did not deprive the landowners of the title to their land or the economic benefits from the land. The court further held that under Ill. Const. art. I, § 15 (1970) the taking of property by the state was not improper, but the taking of property without compensating the owners was improper, which was not the case in so far as the landowners were concerned.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision and remanded to the appellate court to consider other matters raised by the landowners regarding the injunction.

 

210 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


National Marine v. Illinois EPA


Docket No. 74270


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


159 Ill. 2d 381; 639 N.E.2d 571; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 93; 203 Ill. Dec. 251



July 28, 1994, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court reversed in part and affirmed in part; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner brought suit against defendant Illinois Environmental Protection Agency (agency), seeking declaratory and injunctive relief and the issuance of a writ of certiorari, in response to the agency's liability notice. The Illinois Appellate Court affirmed the circuit court's dismissal of the count for declaratory relief and reversed the circuit court's dismissal of the count praying for the writ of certiorari. The agency appealed.


OVERVIEW: The agency issued a notice to the landowner, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1004(q) (1991), informing the landowner of its potential liability for a release of a hazardous substance on its property. The landowner brought suit against the agency, seeking declaratory relief of the unconstitutionality of para. 1004(q), and issuance of a writ of certiorari to review the agency's record and to quash the notice. The circuit court granted the agency's motion to dismiss the landowner's complaint entirely. The intermediate court reversed as to the count praying for the writ of certiorari. The agency appealed. On appeal, the court held that the circuit court properly dismissed the entire complaint because the claim was premature and not ripe for judicial resolution, and because allowing the landowner judicial review at this preliminary stage in the administrative process would have thwarted the legislative intent and statutory scheme. Pre-enforcement review of the issuance of a para. 1004(q) notice was not available to a notice recipient, regardless of the form of relief sought. The landowner's claim was not a controversy "ripe" for judicial resolution.


OUTCOME: The portion of the judgment affirming the dismissal of the count for declaratory relief was affirmed. The portion of the judgment reversing the dismissal of the count for a writ of certiorari was reversed. The circuit court judgment dismissing the landowner's entire complaint was affirmed.

 

211 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Sklodowski v. State


Docket Nos. 73485, 74181


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


162 Ill. 2d 117; 642 N.E.2d 1180; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 87; 205 Ill. Dec. 63



June 16, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing November 15, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Lester D. Foreman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 73485-Appeal dismissed. No. 74181-Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, beneficiaries of five state retirement funds, filed motions seeking a temporary restraining order (TRO) to prevent defendant state officials from transferring money from the funds to the state's general revenue fund and an order disqualifying the state attorney general from representing three of the funds. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied the motions. The beneficiaries appealed.


OVERVIEW: The TRO request was ancillary to a separate mandamus action to restore money to the funds. On appeal, the court held that, despite the conflict between the officials' attempt to divert pension money to balance the budget and the retirement funds' need to regain financial stability, the attorney general's representation of the officials and three of the funds did not prejudice the parties. The beneficiaries could continue their advocacy unaffected by the attorney general's representation of three funds. Whether the circuit court should have issued the TRO was rendered moot when the money was transferred. The court declined to apply the public interest exception to the mootness doctrine and refused to render an advisory opinion because a supreme court opinion on the constitutional issues might influence or foreclose the circuit court from deciding similar issues in the pending mandamus action. The constitutional challenges to the transfer of money first had to be resolved by the circuit court. The circuit court's denial of temporary injunctive relief did not mean it could not reach a final adjudication of the merits of the pending mandamus action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court denying the motion to disqualify the attorney general and dismissed the appeal from the denial of the TRO.

 

212 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Thompkins


Docket No. 72827


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


161 Ill. 2d 148; 641 N.E.2d 371; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 77; 204 Ill. Dec. 147



May 26, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 3, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Will E. Gierach, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissing, without an evidentiary hearing, defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and, in a post-conviction proceeding in the lower court, the defendant filed a petition alleging 33 separate grounds for relief. The lower court denied the petition on the grounds of res judicata, waiver, and lack of merit. The court affirmed the lower court's decision on 32 counts but reversed on the issue of whether the defendant was denied the effective assistance of counsel because counsel failed to adequately investigate and present evidence in mitigation. The court noted that the material submitted by defendant in support of this issue was not part of the record in the original proceedings and represented new evidence and, thus, the issue could not have been raised on direct appeal. The court further held that the affidavits did not duplicate the letters introduced by defense counsel at the sentencing hearing and the persons who submitted affidavits in the post-conviction proceeding were defendant's parents, siblings, children, and friends. The court held that, as a constitutional matter, a capital sentencing hearing requires an individualized assessment of the offense and the offender.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court on 32 of the 33 allegations of error. The court reversed for an evidentiary hearing on defendant's claim that he was denied effective assistance of counsel because the counsel failed to adequately investigate and present evidence in mitigation.

 

213 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Banks


Docket No. 72752


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


161 Ill. 2d 119; 641 N.E.2d 331; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 66; 204 Ill. Dec. 107



May 19, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, 10/03/1994
Writ of certiorari denied Banks v. Illinois, 513 U.S. 1177, 115 S. Ct. 1160, 130 L. Ed. 2d 1116, 1995 U.S. LEXIS 1437 (1995)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Banks, 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 616 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Barbara J. Disko, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a)(1) (1985) and sentenced him to death based on the statutory aggravating factors of murder of an individual under 12 years of age that resulted from exceptionally brutal or heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(b)(7) (1985).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced to death for the murder of a 16-month-old child with whom he lived but was not related. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed. The argument that defendant had no legal duty to act was rejected because defendant's overt acts of starvation, exposure to subfreezing temperature, and interference with the mother's efforts to aid her children resulted in the death. The abuse of the other children was properly admitted to establish defendant's presence, intent, motive, and design and not his propensity for criminal conduct. The interference with the right to represent himself based on law library access was meritless because he failed to complain prior to the trial, and any defect was harmless because of the overwhelming evidence of guilt. Defendant refused all offers of counsel. The State's comments at trial were not preserved as error and were insufficient to invoke the plain error rule. Defendant's conduct was sufficiently brutal and cruel to warrant the death penalty. Defendant failed to tender alternative jury instructions and, therefore, waived his right to appeal. Defendant's other arguments against the death penalty were meritless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction and death sentence.

In re C.E.


Docket No. 73605


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


161 Ill. 2d 200; 641 N.E.2d 345; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 67; 204 Ill. Dec. 121



May 19, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 3, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Marjan P. Staniec, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Attorney General, on behalf of the Department of Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Cook County (Illinois) which refused to authorize the involuntary administration of psychotropic medication to a person receiving mental health treatment.


OVERVIEW: A recipient of mental health services had been found by the circuit court to have been subjected to involuntary admission to a hospital for treatment and had ordered the appointment of appellee guardian for the recipient. The trial court's order further provided that the guardian could not authorize psychotropic medication until certain conditions were met. 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-107.1 permitted a trial court to authorize the involuntary administration of psychotropic medication when the court found by clear and convincing proof, following a full hearing, that the recipient of mental health services was incapable of making the drug-treatment decision on his own behalf and was suffering from one or more of the conditions specified in the statute. The circuit court had refused to do so, reasoning that § 2-107.1 was void as unconstitutional on its face. The court concluded that the statutory provision did not impermissibly overburden the free expression rights of mental health recipients who, while incapable to make a decision in their own behalf, had refused the administration of psychotropic substances.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed and the cause was remanded for further proceedings.

 

215 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Williams


Docket No. 70576


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


161 Ill. 2d 1; 641 N.E.2d 296; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 68; 204 Ill. Dec. 72



May 19, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 3, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. John W. Crilly, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed; death sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of conviction from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for first degree murder, conspiracy to commit murder, armed violence, and sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's judgments of conviction were affirmed, the death sentence was vacated, and remanded. The court held that the trial court's finding of exigent of circumstances was supported by the evidence. It was not unreasonable for the police to believe that swift action to apprehend defendant was necessary. Upon a review of the totality of the evidence, the court held that the trial court was correct in that the police had probable cause to arrest defendant and that exigent circumstances were present to justify making the arrest without a warrant. The evidence of defendant's conviction of voluntary manslaughter should not have been admitted at trial, but it was not so prejudicial as to have denied defendant a fair trial. The court vacated the death sentence because remarks by the prosecutor which were irrelevant to the issue of defendant's eligibility for the death penalty could have improperly distracted and influenced the jurors. The prosecutor's statement's in the closing were misrepresentations of the evidence and the law, were improper and inflammatory, and the court held that defendant was entitled to a new sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of convictions because the police had probable cause to arrest defendant and exigent circumstances were present to justify making the arrest without a warrant. The court vacated defendant's death sentence because the prosecutor's closing statement's were misrepresentations of the evidence and the law and he was entitled to a new sentencing hearing.

People v. Fate


Docket No. 75596


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


159 Ill. 2d 267; 636 N.E.2d 549; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 71; 201 Ill. Dec. 117



May 19, 1994, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of DuPage County (Illinois) that granted appellee's motion to dismiss one of the counts against him based on his alleged violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 951/2, para. 11-501(a)(5) because the statute was not a proper exercise of police power.

Stat. ch. 951/2, para. 11-501(a)(5) that prohibited the operation of a motor vehicle while there was any amount of a drug, substance, or compound in his urine resulting from the unlawful use or consumption of cannabis. The lower court granted appellee's motion to dismiss the charge but the court reversed and remanded. The court found the statute was not an improper or unconstitutional use of police power even though it was without regard to actual physical impairment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the lower court that granted appellee motion to dismiss one of the counts against him based on his alleged violation of a statute that barred the operation of a motor vehicle following the ingestion of any controlled substance because the statute was not a proper exercise of police power.

 

217 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Almgren v. Rush-Presbyterian-St. Luke's Medical Ctr.


Docket Nos. 74831, 74897 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


162 Ill. 2d 205; 642 N.E.2d 1264; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 72; 205 Ill. Dec. 147



May 19, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing November 15, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 74831.--Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Dean J. Sodaro, Judge, presiding.

No. 74897.--Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County, the Hon. Pamela Jensen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgments vacated; appeals dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two separate medical malpractice actions, appellant healthcare providers sought review of judgments entered by Illinois appellate courts, which denied the healthcare providers' pretrial discovery motions for authorization to conduct ex part interviews with appellee patients' treating physicians.


OVERVIEW: In two distinct cases, the patients sought to recover damages for personal injuries allegedly sustained during medical treatment by the healthcare providers. In one case, the trial court granted the healthcare provider's motion to conduct ex parte discovery, and the lower court reversed on appeal. In the other case, the trial court denied a similar motion, and the lower court affirmed on appeal. On appeal, the court held that the lower courts lacked jurisdiction to review the merits of the trial courts' orders. The court reasoned that pretrial discovery orders were subject to review only on appeal from the final judgment entered in a case. There was no right to appeal such interlocutory orders under Ill. Const. art. VI, § 6. Furthermore, pretrial discovery orders were not made appealable by Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 306, 307, 308, 73 Ill. 2d R. 306, 307, 308. The court held that to the extent that § 10(b) of the Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities Confidentiality Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91 1/2, para. 810(b) (1991), attempted to provide for appeals from less than final judgments, it was an unconstitutional infringement by the legislature upon the rulemaking power of the court.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the lower courts' judgments and dismissed the parties' appeals.

 

218 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Cutinello v. Whitley


Docket No. 75468


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


161 Ill. 2d 409; 641 N.E.2d 360; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 73; 204 Ill. Dec. 136



May 19, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 3, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant counties sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found that the County Motor Fuel Tax Law, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 34, para. 5-1035.1 (1991), was unconstitutional. Plaintiffs, purchasers and retailers, filed a cross-appeal to have defendants turn over the proceeds disbursed to defendants before the issuance of a preliminary injunction.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, purchasers and retailers, brought a class action against defendant counties to challenge the constitutionality of the County Motor Fuel Tax Law (Law), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 34, para. 5-1035.1 (1991). The trial court found the statute unconstitutional and defendants appealed. Plaintiffs filed a cross-appeal to have the proceeds disbursed to defendants before the issuance of a preliminary injunction turned over to plaintiffs. The court reversed the judgment against defendants and remanded the case for further proceedings. The court determined that the Law did not violate the special legislation proscription in Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13. The legislative action satisfied the rational basis test and plaintiffs failed to show that the legislative classification was unreasonable. The court also determined that the comprehensive transportation bill that included the Law did not violate the single-subject rule of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d) because its provisions had a natural and logical connection to the legislative purpose. The court concluded that, under the enrolled bill doctrine, the bill did not violate the three-readings requirement of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment against defendant counties and remanded the action brought by plaintiffs, purchasers and retailers, to the trial court for further proceedings. The County Motor Fuel Tax Law (Law) did not violate the special legislation proscription. The comprehensive transportation bill that included the Law did not violate the single-subject rule or the three-readings requirement.

Eagan v. Chicago Transit Auth.


Docket No. 75176


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


158 Ill. 2d 527; 634 N.E.2d 1093; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 60; 199 Ill. Dec. 739



April 21, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Willard J. Lassers and the Hon. Thomas E. Hoffman, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff personal injury claimant challenged the decision of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which found in favor of defendant transit authority, in the claimant's negligence action.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was a passenger on one of the transit authority's train when he observed an individual attempting to pick the pocket of another passenger. The claimant intervened and confronted the pickpocket, who then attacked the claimant and cut him with a razor. The claimant brought a negligence action against the transit authority. The transit authority filed a motion to dismiss the complaint pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-619 (1987). Following a hearing, the trial court granted the transit authority's motion and dismissed the complaint. The appellate court reversed and remanded the cause to proceed on the merits, and the transit authority sought review. On appeal the court reversed and reinstated the circuit court's dismissal. The court held that the allegations in the claimant's complaint fell within the scope of immunity that was conferred upon the transit authority by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 327 (1987), which provided immunity to the transit authority for failure to prevent the commission of crimes by fellow passengers or third persons where a security or police force had been provided for the passengers' protection.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court, which reversed the dismissal of the claimant's negligence action against the transit authority.

People v. Griffith


Docket No. 73451


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


158 Ill. 2d 476; 634 N.E.2d 1069; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 62; 199 Ill. Dec. 715



April 21, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied May 27, 1994.
Rehearing denied by, 05/27/1994
Writ of certiorari denied Griffith v. Illinois, 513 U.S. 952, 115 S. Ct. 370, 130 L. Ed. 2d 321, 1994 U.S. LEXIS 7441 (1994)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Griffith v. Gaetz, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 25794 (C.D. Ill., Mar. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Livingston County, the Hon. Charles E. Glennon, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant inmate sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois), which convicted him of the first-degree murder of another inmate and of unlawful possession of a weapon and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of the first-degree murder of another inmate and of unlawful possession of a weapon by a person in the custody of the department of corrections. He was sentenced to death on the murder conviction and to a consecutive 30-year prison term on the weapon conviction. On appeal, the court found that the inmate was fully informed by the trial judge about separate jury instructions for first and second-degree murder. With his attorney present, the inmate chose not to instruct the jury on second-degree murder. He wanted the jury to have but two alternatives: guilty of murder in the first degree or not guilty. It was clear from the record that his choice was voluntary, knowing, and intelligent. The court further found that the trial court properly considered the inmate's mitigation evidence, for whatever it was worth, and properly concluded that it was insufficient to preclude a sentence of death.


OUTCOME: The order convicting the inmate of first-degree murder and unlawful possession of a weapon was affirmed. The order sentencing the inmate to death was affirmed.

People v. Hobley


Docket No. 71184


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


159 Ill. 2d 272; 637 N.E.2d 992; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 42; 202 Ill. Dec. 256



March 31, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied May 27, 1994.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) his death sentence imposed after defendant was convicted by jury of felony murder, a violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a)(3) (1985), arson, a violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1(a) (1985), and aggravated arson, a violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1.1(a)(1), (a)(2) (1985). Defendant sought reversal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contested his death sentence imposed by the circuit court following defendant's jury convictions for felony murder in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a)(3) (1985), arson in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1(a) (1985), and aggravated arson in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1.1(a)(1), (a)(2) (1985). Defendant requested reversal based on alleged errors within the pretrial, guilt, and sentencing phases of the circuit court proceedings. The court affirmed defendant's judgment of convictions and death sentence. The circuit court correctly decided that defendant was not arrested until after he confessed because initially he was just helping the police investigation, was not handcuffed, was not involuntarily taken anywhere, and a reasonable person would have believed he was free to leave. The court decided that the police had probable cause to arrest defendant. The circuit court correctly found that defendant received sufficient Miranda warnings to have knowingly and voluntarily waived his constitutional rights before his polygraph examination and then again before his first interview, prior to confessing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the death sentence challenged by defendant from the circuit court following defendant's jury convictions for felony murder, a statutory violation, arson, a statutory violation, and aggravated arson, a statutory violation. The court declined to reverse because defendant's arrest occurred after he confessed and was based on probable cause obtained after adequate Miranda warnings were given.

 

222 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. O'Malley v. 6323 N. LaCrosse Ave.


Docket No. 75447


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


158 Ill. 2d 453; 634 N.E.2d 743; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 33; 199 Ill. Dec. 690



March 24, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Peter Bakakos, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) declaring that the provision of the Drug Asset Forfeiture Procedure Act, which denied a jury trial in forfeiture proceedings per Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1679(F) (1991), violated Ill. Const. art. I, § 13. The state filed a complaint for forfeiture of real property after claimant's husband was arrested for possession of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Claimant and her husband owned a home as joint tenants. The husband was arrested for the possession of cocaine resulting from a search of their home, and the state filed a complaint for forfeiture of the real property pursuant to the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1505 (act). Claimant then filed a claim for return of the real property and demanded a trial by jury. The state filed a motion to strike the jury demand on grounds that the act provided that the hearings with respect to all property subject to forfeiture had to be by the court without a jury. On appeal, the court held that the critical inquiry was whether jury trials were provided for in rem forfeiture proceedings at the time the Illinois Constitution was adopted in 1970. In affirming that the act unconstitutionally denied claimant the right to a trial by jury, the court held that the right to a jury trial, in civil proceedings in rem for the enforcement of statutory forfeitures, existed prior to adoption of the Illinois Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the holding of the lower court holding that the provision of the Drug Asset Forfeiture Procedure Act (act) denying the right to trial by jury in forfeiture actions violated the Illinois constitution. The court held, however, that because the remainder of the statute was capable of being independently executed, it would excise the invalid section and allow the balance of the act to stand.

People ex rel. Waller v. 1990 Ford Bronco


Docket No. 75810


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


158 Ill. 2d 460; 634 N.E.2d 747; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 34; 199 Ill. Dec. 694



March 24, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. John G. Radosevich, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which dismissed an action against defendant under § 1.25 of the Wildlife Code (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 61, para. 1.25 (1991) to obtain by forfeiture an automobile, a shotgun, and a handgun owned by defendant on the ground that use of the items were connected to the violations.


OVERVIEW: Officers of the Department of Conservation arrested defendant for violation of § 24-1(a)(4) of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-1(a)(4) (1991), for carrying a shotgun and a handgun in his automobile. The car and the weapons were seized. The state filed a complaint pursuant to § 1.25 to obtain by forfeiture the automobile, the shotgun, and the handgun because use of the items was connected to the violations. Defendant asked the court to declare § 1.25 of the Act unconstitutional. The court dismissed the action on the grounds that § 1.25 was unconstitutional and the state appealed. The court affirmed the dismissal, holding that the state never contended that the guns or the auto were used or operated illegally in taking, transporting, holding or conveying any wild bird or wild mammal contrary to the provisions of the Act and nothing in § 1.25 authorized the seizure or forfeiture of property for violation of any provision of the Criminal Code. In addition, nothing in the Criminal Code authorized the seizure or forfeiture of property by means of the procedures set forth in the Act. Accordingly, § 1.25 of the Act had no application to the facts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the action brought by the state for forfeiture of defendant's car and weapons following his arrest for carrying the weapons in his car.

 

224 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. R.L.


Docket Nos. 75081, 75082, 75083 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


158 Ill. 2d 432; 634 N.E.2d 733; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 37; 199 Ill. Dec. 680



March 24, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Michael B. Getty, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which ruled that § 5-4(7)(a) of the Juvenile Court Act of 1987, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 805-4(7)(a) (1991), as applied to 15-and 16-year-old minors charged with drug offenses committed within 1,000 feet of public housing, such as defendants, denied minors equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, who were juveniles, were charged with possessing illegal drugs on city housing authority property. Section 5-4(7)(a) contained a classification based on the location of the crime. A minor charged with committing a drug offense on a public way beyond 1,000 feet of public housing remained in the administration of the juvenile division. However, a minor charged with the same offense within 1,000 feet of public housing was automatically removed from the juvenile division and was treated as an adult. The trial court ruled that § 5-4(7)(a) denied defendants equal protection. On appeal, the court reversed the decision and held that under strict scrutiny, defendants failed to prove that the legislature purposely intended to racially discriminate in enacting the provision. The court held that a facially neutral and otherwise valid law did not violate the equal protection clause simply because the law affected a greater proportion of one race than of another. The court further concluded that a rational basis existed for the classification created by § 5-4(7)(a). The classification was based on the location of the charged offense, which was a permissible distinction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the case.

People v. Kitchen


Docket No. 71027


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


159 Ill. 2d 1; 636 N.E.2d 433; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 38; 201 Ill. Dec. 1



March 24, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied May 27, 1994.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of five counts of murder following a jury trial. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) found the defendant eligible for the death penalty based on the statutory aggravating factor of murder of two or more individuals and found insufficient mitigating factors to preclude imposition of the death sentence. Defendant's execution was stayed pending his direct appeal from his convictions and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused and convicted of participating in the murder of five people because of some drug money allegedly owed and then setting their bodies on fire. The trial court sentenced defendant to death. The court rejected defendant's contention that the state engaged in purposeful racial discrimination when exercising its peremptory challenges because 1) the court upheld prosecutor's challenges concerning the person's viewpoints toward the death penalty; 2) unemployment was a sufficiently race-neutral reason for excluding a venireperson; 3) the demeanor of a venireperson also constituted a legitimate race-neutral reason for the exercise of a peremptory challenge; and 4) sufficient evidence was produced at trial to support the jury's verdict. Regarding defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel the court held that because the record did not adequately set forth what defense counsel's testimony would have been it could not resolve this ineffectiveness claim in defendant's favor. Defendant also failed to meet the burden of demonstrating a reasonable probability that, but for counsel's errors, the result of the proceeding would have been different.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's convictions and death sentence.

People v. Fair


Docket No. 71231


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


159 Ill. 2d 51; 636 N.E.2d 455; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 39; 201 Ill. Dec. 23



March 24, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied May 27, 1994.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction and death sentence from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for murder on the grounds that the state engaged in purposeful discrimination when it exercised it peremptory challenges in an allegedly racially discriminatory manner.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. Appellant challenged his conviction and sentence claiming that the state discriminatorily used its peremptory challenges during voir dire to purposefully exclude black venirepersons from the jury, that the lower court erred in failing to require the state to explain the use of its seventh and final challenge, and that the state's explanation for the exercise of the prior challenges were neither clear nor reasonably specific. The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence. The court held that appellant failed to make a timely objection to the state's final challenge as appellant did not object at the time the juror was excluded and allowed both parties to proceed with opening arguments and three state witnesses to testify before sounding his complaint. The court held that the state met its burden of providing race-neutral explanations for its exclusion of jurors as exclusion on the basis of courtroom demeanor and apprehension as to the imposition of the death penalty were acceptable explanations.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for murder and death sentence were affirmed on the grounds that appellant failed to timely object to the state's challenge of a juror and that courtroom demeanor and a potential juror's attitude toward the death penalty were sufficient to carry the state's burden of proving race-neutral reasons for its challenges against black venirepersons.

Bonaguro v. County Officers Electoral Bd.


Docket No. 74907


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


158 Ill. 2d 391; 634 N.E.2d 712; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 28; 199 Ill. Dec. 659



March 18, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Francis Barth, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Republican candidate for judge filed objections to the Democratic party's nomination under 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7-61 (1992) of a candidate who had not run in the primary. The Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) affirmed the trial court, which confirmed defendant electoral board's order overruling the Republican's objections and placing the Democrat's name on the ballot for the general election. The Republican appealed.


OVERVIEW: No Democratic candidate ran in the primary, but the Democratic party subsequently nominated a candidate by party resolution, purportedly authorized by 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7-61 (1992). On appeal, the Republican contended that § 7-61 did not authorize a political party to fill a judicial vacancy in nomination by party resolution. The court agreed and reversed and held that § 7-61 applied to all vacancies in nomination except judicial vacancies. Sections 7-7 and 7-61 described only political districts for legislative and executive positions and did not refer to judicial committees for judicial vacancies in nomination. The absence of a reference to a nominating committee for judicial office in § 7-7 indicated the legislative intent that judicial vacancies in nomination could not be filled by party resolution. Moreover, the board of elections stated that where an established political party failed to nominate a candidate, a party committee could fill the vacancy, except for judicial office. 26 Ill. Adm. Code § 207.10 (1992). Also the Illinois attorney general had concluded that there was no method to fill judicial vacancies in nomination. 1972 Ill. Att'y Gen. Op. 99.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court.

 

228 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Knuckles


Docket No. 73616


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


1994 Ill. LEXIS 22



February 17, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Petition for Rehearing Allowed May 27, 1994.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the judgment of an Illinois appellate court, which affirmed an order sustaining defendant's motion to quash subpoenas for the testimony and memoranda of her non-testifying psychiatrist.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to slaying of her mother, and her counsel disclaimed an intention of raising an insanity defense. The plea was set aside, and the charges reinstated. The state issued two subpoenas for the testimony and written memoranda of a non-testifying psychiatrist who, at defense counsel's request, examined defendant two weeks after the killing. The appellate court affirmed the order sustaining defendant's motion to quash. The state appealed. The court held that the attorney-client privilege extended to communications between defendant and the psychiatrist to aid in preparation of the insanity defense. Defendant did not waive the privilege by asserting defenses that placed her mental condition in issue. The court concluded that the trial court erred in quashing the subpoenas because the privilege yielded under the peculiar facts of the case. The court held that the nine-year delay between the homicide and the trial was in no way attributable to the state and that barring discovery of the only expert whose inquiry into defendant's mental condition was contemporaneous with the occurrence of the crime obstructed the fundamental truth-seeking function of the trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order sustaining defendant's motion to quash the state's subpoenas.

People v. Fitzpatrick


Docket No. 74768


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


158 Ill. 2d 360; 633 N.E.2d 685; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 23; 198 Ill. Dec. 844



February 17, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied April 4, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Clinton County, the Hon. Harold H. Pennock III, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from a ruling of the Circuit Court of Clinton County (Illinois) issued in defendant's trial for aggravated criminal sexual assault. Upon defendant's motion, the circuit court declared that the Illinois Child Shield Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat., ch. 38, par. 106B-1 (1991), violated the confrontation clause of the Illinois constitution as set forth in Ill. Const. 1970, art. I, § 8.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with several counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault against his four minor grandchildren. The state filed a motion pursuant to the Child Shield Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat., ch. 38, par. 106B-1 (1991), to allow the grandchildren to testify outside of defendant's presence through closed circuit television. Defendant filed a motion to declare the Act unconstitutional pursuant to the confrontation clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. 1970, art. I, § 8. The circuit court held that the Act violated the Illinois Constitution. On appeal, the court affirmed the ruling of the circuit court. The court noted that it was not bound by the United States Supreme Court's interpretation of similar federal constitutional provisions when interpreting the Illinois Constitution. The court ruled that the confrontation clause of the Illinois Constitution, unlike its federal counterpart, clearly and unambiguously entitled a defendant to a face-to-face confrontation with a witness. Because the language of the confrontation clause was unambiguous, the court ruled that it was not free to disregard it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling of the circuit court that the Illinois Child Shield Act violated defendant's rights under the confrontation clause of the Illinois Constitution.

People v. Childress


Docket No. 72024


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


158 Ill. 2d 275; 633 N.E.2d 635; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 16; 198 Ill. Dec. 794



February 3, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied April 4, 1994. As Corrected April 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. James J. Heyda, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed in part and vacated in part; death sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions and sentences from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which convicted defendant of first degree murder, burglary, home invasion, and attempted aggravated criminal sexual assault and imposed sentences to run consecutively to the death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his convictions and sentences for first degree murder, burglary, home invasion, and attempted aggravated criminal sexual assault. Defendant alleged that there were various errors in the administration of the trial, that his burglary conviction was erroneous, that as a result, so was the death sentence, and that the statute was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the sentences and the convictions in part. The court reversed the burglary conviction, as defendant was guilty of residential burglary, not simple burglary and the court held that the sentences for the other crimes should have been ordered to run concurrent with the death sentence and modified the sentences accordingly. The court affirmed the other convictions, as the trial court did not abuse its discretion and any errors committed were harmless. Finally, the death sentence was proper, as the erroneous inclusion of burglary among the predicate felonies as aggravating circumstances in support of the sentence was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt and did not require a new hearing. The court also concluded that the sentence was proper, as the death penalty statute was constitutionally firm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions in part but reversed the burglary conviction, as defendant was guilty of residential burglary, not simple burglary and any errors were otherwise harmless. The court affirmed the death sentence, as the death penalty statute was constitutional and no errors entitled defendant to a new hearing.

People v. Coleman


Docket No. 72151


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


158 Ill. 2d 319; 633 N.E.2d 654; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 18; 198 Ill. Dec. 813



February 3, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied April 4, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. John N. Hourihane, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), convicting and sentencing him to death for capital murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts each of first degree murder, armed robbery, and home invasion. He was sentenced to death. The court affirmed defendant's convictions and death sentence. The court held that defendant's contentions that he was denied a fair trial based on the admission of different particular evidence was without basis because the evidence did not rise to the level of plain error, as it was harmless. The court further held that defendant was not denied the effective assistance of counsel. In addition, the court held that defendant was not eligible for resentencing and that he was not denied a fair capital sentence hearing. Moreover, the court declined to rule on defendant's claim on the constitutionality of the Illinois death penalty statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for first degree murder, armed robbery, and home invasion. The court held that he was not denied a fair trial based on the admission of different particular evidence because the evidence did not rise to the level of plain error, as it was harmless.

 

232 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Russell


Docket Nos. 73721, 74443 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


158 Ill. 2d 23; 630 N.E.2d 794; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 1; 196 Ill. Dec. 629



January 20, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 73721.- Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County, the Hon. James K. Donovan, Judge, presiding.

No. 74443.- Appeal from the Circuit of Coles County, the Hon. Ashton Waller, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of separate decisions from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County and the Circuit Court of Coles County (Illinois), which found Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-16.2(a)(1) (1989) (now 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-16.2(a)(1) (1992)) unconstitutional with regard to defendants, who were charged with being knowing carriers of HIV and transmitting the virus through intimate contact. The cases were consolidated on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Each defendant was charged with being a knowing carrier of the HIV virus and transmitting the virus through intimate contact with another person. One defendant had consensual sex and the other committed rape. In both cases the trial courts found that the criminal statute was unconstitutional and the state challenged the decision. On consolidated appeals, the court reversed and remanded for further proceedings. Neither of the trial courts explained why the statute was unconstitutional. The court found that free speech was not violated because the actions of defendants did not have any connection with free speech. Additionally, the statute was not overly broad or facially vague. Further, the statute did not infringe on the right to intimate association because no such right existed. The statute was sufficiently clear and explicit so that a person of ordinary intelligence need not have to guess at its meaning or application. Also, it provided sufficiently definite standards for law enforcement officers and triers of fact so that its application was not depend merely on their private conceptions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision that found the statute criminalizing the transmission of HIV by knowing carriers unconstitutional and remanded for further proceedings against the defendants.

People v. Janes


Docket No. 73235


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


158 Ill. 2d 27; 630 N.E.2d 790; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 4; 196 Ill. Dec. 625



January 20, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cumberland County, the Hon. Paul C. Komada, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court reversed in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered a guilty plea in the Circuit Court of Cumberland County (Illinois) to three counts of murder and was sentenced to death. Defendant challenged his conviction and his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that he was entitled to a new hearing on his motion to withdraw his guilty plea because his counsel failed to comply with the certificate requirements of Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(d), codified at 145 Ill. 2d R. 604(d). Defendant also challenged, on several grounds, the trial court's decision to sentence him to death. On appeal, the court held that defendant was entitled to a new hearing on his motion to withdraw his guilty plea, and, in view of that holding, declined to address the death sentence issues. In reaching its decision, the court concluded that because the record did not show strict compliance with the certificate requirement of Rule 604(d), reversal of that portion of the trial court's judgment denying defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea was warranted. The court rejected the state's argument that because defendant was not prejudiced by any violations of Rule 604(d), a remand for new proceedings served no purpose.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed in part, and the case was remanded.

 

234 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Zaremba


Docket No. 74221


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


158 Ill. 2d 36; 630 N.E.2d 797; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 6; 196 Ill. Dec. 632



January 20, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Peter J. Dockery, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which dismissed an indictment on the ground that § 16-1(a)(5) of the Illinois Theft Statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 16-1(a)(5) (1989), was unconstitutional on its face since it failed to require a culpable mental state. The indictment alleged that defendant knowingly received property explicitly represented as being stolen.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that because § 16-1(a)(5) of the Illinois theft statute did not require a culpable mental state, it could apply to innocent conduct. He asserted that § 16-1(a)(5) would criminalize the actions of a police evidence technician who took from a police officer for safekeeping the proceeds of a theft that the police officer had recovered and that the police officer gave to the evidence technician with the representation that the goods were stolen. Section 16-1(a)(5) did not bear a rational relationship to a legitimate state purpose; thus, it was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court agreed and affirmed the judgment of the circuit court. Section 16-1(a)(5) was not reasonably related to the purpose of enabling police officers to break up fencing operations because, as written, it subjected innocent persons to punishment. The court also found that the mental states stated in §§ 16-1(a)(A) through (a)(C) of the theft statute could not be implied in § (a)(5) because to do so would make §§ (a)(A) though (a)(C), as stated below §§ (a)(1) through (a)(4), "meaningless surplusage."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which found a section of the Illinois theft statute regarding fencing to be unconstitutional on its face because it failed to require a culpable mental state.

 

235 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Meyers


Docket Nos. 74710, 74711, 74712 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


158 Ill. 2d 46; 630 N.E.2d 811; 1994 Ill. LEXIS 5; 196 Ill. Dec. 646



January 20, 1994, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Ronald F. Bartkowicz, Judge, presiding.

Judgments reversed; causes remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed complaints against defendants, who had been charged with violation of § 235b of the Revenue Act of 1939, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 716d (1991), after they had participated in a tax sale of property, when they had interests in the property to be sold. The prosecution appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants claimed that § 235b of the Illinois Revenue Act of 1939, specifically at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 716d (1991), violated the equal protection clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, impaired their right to acquire property, violated equal protection, and claimed the complaints were vague and violated due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The state claimed that the complaints sufficiently tracked the language of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 716d (1991) to meet due process requirements. The court reversed the trial court dismissal and remanded, holding that defendants were the class of persons to which Para. 716d was addressed and that the complaints against defendants tracked the language of Para. 716d to meet due process requirements, which did not require specific property descriptions if the property was not an element of the offense, which it was not. The court further held that defendants had no right to acquire property from a tax sale and the owner and taxpayer had a right to redeem the property after the sale.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal, because defendants' rights of due process and equal protection were not violated by the prosecution and defendants were the class of citizens which was sought to be prosecuted under the statutory scheme, which prohibited persons that had an interest in property being sold at a tax sale from bidding at the sale.

238 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Messenger v. Edgar


Docket No. 75132


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


157 Ill. 2d 162; 623 N.E.2d 310; 1993 Ill. LEXIS 71; 191 Ill. Dec. 65



September 23, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied November 29, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, government officials, appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which declared unconstitutional that part of Ill. Comp. Stat. § 5/501 (1992) of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act that provided for a dissolution action stay and restrained the parties to the action from disposing of any property until further order of the court.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff wife filed for dissolution of marriage and an action for declaratory judgment alleging the unconstitutionality of Ill. Comp. Stat. § 5/501 (1992). The wife asserted that the challenged section deprived her of property without due process of law. The trial court found the challenged section unconstitutional and void. Initially, the court found the wife had standing to bring this action for declaratory judgment. Next, the court found that the effect of § 5/501.1(a)(1) was to restrain each party to an action for dissolution of marriage, in the absence of the consent of the other party or an order of the court, from disposing of any and all property, including that qualifying under the Act for the designation "non-marital property." The court held that the excessively broad sweep of this section to include a restraint affecting property that could not be considered in any way a marital asset, the means adopted by the legislature, was not a rational means of accomplishing its purpose and violated the guarantee of substantive due process. Hence, the wife sustained her burden of establishing the invalidity of the challenged portion of § 5/501.1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

 

239 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Nevitt v. Langfelder


Docket No. 74405


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


157 Ill. 2d 116; 623 N.E.2d 281; 1993 Ill. LEXIS 73; 191 Ill. Dec. 36



September 23, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied November 29, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. C. Joseph Cavanagh, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed from the decision of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which found that defendant city and officials were not bound to follow the Public Employee Disability Act, 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. 345/1 (1992), because it was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured while working as a fire fighter for the city, which was a home rule unit of government. The Disability Act required home rule units of government with populations smaller than one million to continue paying, for a period of one year, wages and benefits to fire fighters who were injured in the line of duty. The city refused the plaintiff's request for continued payment of those items. In response to the employee's request for a declaratory judgment of his rights, the trial court found that the classification of home rule units in the Disability Act violated the equal protection guarantees of the federal and state constitutions. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The Disability Act applies to certain divisions of state government, and hence it involved a power or function that was exercised or performed by the state. There were a number of rational reasons that the legislature chose to exclude from coverage home rule units larger than one million persons. As there was no violation of equal protection principles, the city and officials were required to comply with the terms of the Disability Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.
