People v. Towns


Docket No. 72708


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


157 Ill. 2d 90; 623 N.E.2d 269; 1993 Ill. LEXIS 79; 191 Ill. Dec. 24



September 23, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied November 29, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County, the Hon. James Donovan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) convicted the defendant of first-degree murder arising out of an armed robbery and shooting of a convenience store clerk, and imposed the death penalty. Defendant appealed, and his execution was stayed pending direct review by the court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant signed a statement that he was in the store while the clerk was counting the cash receipts. He took some of the money, and, when the clerk accused him of taking the money and threatened to call the police, defendant shot him twice in the head. He fled in the clerk's car, removed the stereo, and set the car on fire. Defendant verbalized the plan to his brother, who wrote it down, and the note was found in the brother's bedroom. The stereo was in his sister's house. The court held that (1) the Jury Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 78 (1991), was not violated and defendant was not deprived of a fair and impartial jury because a juror oath was not required prior to voir dire, and the jurors fairly and impartially rendered a verdict; (2) counsel was not ineffective in failing to timely object to preserve the issue of the juror oath, which was not required; and (3) admission of the note was proper because authentication was established by circumstantial evidence in that the note was found in the brother's bedroom and the note was entitled "Wednesday's plan," and the crime occurred on a Wednesday.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment of conviction and sentencing.

American Tel. & Tel. Co. v. Village of Arlington Heights


Docket No. 72315


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


156 Ill. 2d 399; 620 N.E.2d 1040; 1993 Ill. LEXIS 70; 189 Ill. Dec. 723; 73 Rad. Reg. 2d (P & F) 1330



August 26, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied October 4, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Robert L. Sklodowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant municipalities challenged an order of the Illinois Appellate Court for the First District. The court affirmed a judgment, which held that the municipalities could not impose toll charges or franchise fees on plaintiff telephone company for laying fiber optic cable underneath public ways.


OVERVIEW: The intermediate court affirmed a judgment, which held that defendant municipalities could not impose tolls or franchise fees on plaintiff telephone company for laying fiber optic cable under public ways. The court affirmed. Because no person or entity within any of the municipalities was connected to or had the use of plaintiff's fiber optic cable, the court found that plaintiff was not seeking what normally would have been considered a franchise: a business that sought protection, licensing, and special privileges for using city streets. The court also held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 8-11-2(4) (1987) was entirely regulatory and that it did not permit municipalities to tax the users of public streets or of the wires under the streets. The court further determined that the Telephone Company Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 134, para. 16.90 et seq., granted plaintiff eminent domain over private property and any public ground of the state that was needed to extend telephone poles, wires, cables, or other appliances. The court held that consent for the installation of telephone equipment along or under municipal streets could not be unreasonably withheld.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate judgment, which affirmed the trial court's decision that defendant municipalities could not impose tolls or franchise fees on plaintiff telephone company for laying fiber optic cable under public ways. The court held that plaintiff was not seeking special privileges for using city streets and that a regulatory statute did not allow taxing the user of public streets or wires under the streets.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court, sua sponte, recalled the order of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which affirmed the trial court's order finding petitioner candidate to be the winner of a contested primary but ordered that respondent candidate continue to serve as a judge until the general election in which petitioner candidate ran unopposed.


OVERVIEW: In the election contest pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 7-63 (1989), the court concluded that (1) the appellate court's order was unconstitutional and could not stand; (2) petitioner candidate won the primary election; (3) a proper recount was conducted; (4) petitioner candidate was properly placed on the general election ballot; (5) the election contest was not moot; (6) the voters' right of suffrage was not infringed; and (7) the doctrine of laches did not apply. The court explained that the appellate court's decision, which essentially allowed both candidates to fill a single judicial vacancy, was unconstitutional because it increased the number of judges in the county, usurped the court's power to appoint persons to fill judicial vacancies if viewed as an appointment, failed to place the proper constitutional limitations concerning judges on candidate if viewed as an appointment, and was made with no legislative appropriation of state funds.

OVERVIEW: Defendant made statements relative to three different murders at the same time. People v. Laws


No. 73306


Supreme Court of Illinois


155 Ill. 2d 208; 613 N.E.2d 747; 1993 Ill. LEXIS 32; 184 Ill. Dec. 430



April 15, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Richard E. Neville, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged an order of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed a trial court's dismissal of charges of conspiracy to keep a house of prostitution under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 8 -- 2, 11 -- 17(a)(1) and conspiracy in connection with pimping, soliciting for a prostitute, and pandering under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 8 -- 2, 11 -- 19(a), 11 -- 15(a)(2), 11 -- 15(a)(3), 11 -- 16(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: The intermediate court reversed a dismissal of the charges of violating Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 8 -- 2, 11 -- 17(a)(1) by conspiring to keep a house of prostitution and violating Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 8 -- 2, 11 -- 19(a), 11 -- 15(a)(2), 11 -- 15(a)(3), 11 -- 16(a)(2) as to conspiracies that related to pimping, soliciting for a prostitute, and pandering that were filed against appellants. The court partially affirmed and partially reversed the lower courts' judgments and remanded the case on appeal. The court reasoned that Wharton's Rule did not bar the prosecution of the conspiracies because the cooperative conduct that was contemplated by the substantive crimes was distinguishable from the complex agreements that supported the conspiracy charges because each of the conspiracies exceeded the simple cooperative conduct that was contemplated in the commission of the substantive crimes. The court also determined that the misdemeanor limitations period applied to the charge of conspiracy to keep a place of prostitution because punishment as either a Class 3 felony or a Class A misdemeanor was possible.


OUTCOME: The court partially reversed and partially affirmed the lower courts' rulings in a case in which an intermediate court reversed a dismissal of the conspiracy charges as to prostitution-related offenses against defendants, and remanded the case. The court held that Wharton's Rule did not bar the conspiracy prosecutions because each conspiracy exceeded the cooperative conduct that was contemplated in the substantive crimes' commission.

Dunaway v. Fellous


No. 73293


Supreme Court of Illinois

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) held that it did not have jurisdiction over the persons of defendants, a tavern keeper and its landlord, under the Illinois Dram Shop Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 43, para. 135 (1989). Plaintiff injured person appealed.


OVERVIEW: The injured person was struck by a driver who had been drinking at the tavern, which was located 30 miles inside Missouri, the next state. The Act provided for jurisdiction over sellers of alcoholic liquor, whether or not they were residents of the state. The trial court did not specify the basis on which it found lack of personal jurisdiction over the tavern keeper and the landlord, but the court affirmed and held that the Act did not apply at all to the landlord, an owner of out-of-state real estate, but only to the tavern keeper. The court noted that there was no evidence that the tavern keeper solicited business from Illinois residents. The fact that an individual consumed alcohol at the tavern and then drove 30 miles to Illinois did not demonstrate sufficient minimum contacts with Illinois to make it proper for an Illinois court to exercise jurisdiction over the Missouri tavern keeper. The requirement that a party must have purposefully availed itself of the privilege of conducting activities within Illinois was not met. That it was foreseeable that a tavern patron might cause injury in another state was not a sufficient basis upon which to predicate personal jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which held that it did not have jurisdiction over the persons of the tavern keeper and its landlord.

Collins v. Board of Trustees of Firemen's Annuity & Benefit Fund


No. 73460


Supreme Court of Illinois


155 Ill. 2d 103; 610 N.E.2d 1250; 1993 Ill. LEXIS 17; 183 Ill. Dec. 6



March 18, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Monica D. Reynolds, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pension board challenged the order of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed an order of the trial court dismissing appellee fire paramedics' suit that sought a declaration that § 6-210.1, article 6 of the Illinois Pension Code, 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/6-210.1 (West 1992), unconstitutionally diminished appellees' vested pension rights in violation of Ill. Const. 1970, art. XIII, § 5.


OVERVIEW: Appellee fire paramedics sought a declaration that § 6-210.1 of article 6 of the Illinois Pension Code, 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/6-210.1 (West 1992), unconstitutionally diminished their vested pension rights in violation of Ill. Const. 1970, art. XIII, § 5. The trial court granted appellant pension board's motion to dismiss, holding that § 6-210.1 was not unconstitutional. The lower appellate court reversed. However, the court reversed the lower appellate court's ruling. It found that the absence of acceptance of the Reciprocal Act of the Illinois Pension Code (Code), 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/20-101 (West 1992), in the enabling legislation for the police and firefighters retirement funds indicated that those systems were closed for purposes of service credits to employees transferring from other public employment. The court ruled that retirement service credits were intended to be conditioned upon payment of contributions. The court held that appellees could not receive service credits for purposes of computation of retirement annuity benefits for periods during which they performed the duties of their positions prior to 1983 and for which they made no corresponding contribution.


OUTCOME: The court held that amendments to the Illinois Pension Code did not unconstitutionally diminish appellee fire paramedics' rights in violation of the Illinois Constitution. The court reversed the order of the appellate court that had reversed the order of the trial court that granted appellant pension board's motion to dismiss appellees' complaint for declaratory judgment.

People v. Peeples

People v. Schaefer

Supreme Court of Illinois

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]

No. 72946. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County, the Hon. John P. Freese, Judge, presiding.

No. 72996. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County, the Hon. Vicki R. Wright, Judge, presiding.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent state sought to revoke driver's licenses of petitioner motorists. The Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) reversed the trial court's order dismissing one of the revocation proceedings. The Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois) affirmed the trial court's order denying one of the motorist's motions to rescind. The Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois) affirmed the trial court's order of rescission.


OVERVIEW: The motorists claimed that they had petitioned the trial courts for reinstatement of their driver's licenses and the trials were not held in a timely manner. The state claimed that the delay in the trial was not a jurisdictional issue and that the trial courts had the authority to refuse to reinstate the motorists' licenses so long as there was a reasonable excuse for the delay. In a consolidated appeal, the court held that the trial court was required to reinstate the motorists' licenses if the delays in holding hearings on the requests for reinstatement were not caused by the motorists and the state was responsible for the delays. The court further held that under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501 (1989) the driver's licenses were properly suspended if the motorists failed to timely request, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 2-118.1(b) (1989), a rescission of the automatic suspension that was based on the motorist driving while under the influence of alcohol in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501 (1989).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the third district appellate court's judgment, which affirmed the order of rescission of the motorist's suspension. The court reversed the fourth district appellate court's judgment, which affirmed the trial court's denial of the motorist's motion for rescission. The court affirmed the first district appellate court's judgment, which reversed the order dismissing the revocation proceedings against one motorist.

People v. Johnson


No. 72097


Supreme Court of Illinois


154 Ill. 2d 356; 609 N.E.2d 294; 1993 Ill. LEXIS 1; 181 Ill. Dec. 926



January 28, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 29, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Montgomery County, the Hon. E.C. Eberspacher, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Convictions Affirmed in Part and Vacated in Part; Death Sentence Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the convictions rendered by the Circuit Court of Montgomery County (Illinois). Defendant had pleaded guilty to murder, home invasion, and aggravated sexual assault. On appeal, defendant challenged the denial of a motion to withdraw his guilty plea, imposition of the death penalty sentence, denial of his right to effective counsel, and use of his home invasion charge for the imposition of the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to death after waiving his right to a jury trial and pleading guilty to murder, home invasion, and aggravated criminal sexual assault. Defendant contended that his motion to withdraw his guilty pleas was wrongfully denied because his confession was the result of misunderstanding his attorney's advice and he was unaware of the consequences. The court found that there was no objective proof to show that defendant was reasonably justified in his alleged mistake, so there was no abuse of discretion in the denial of his plea withdrawal motion. There was ample support for the trial court's conclusion that the murder was brutal or heinous as indicative of wanton cruelty to satisfy death penalty sentencing requirements. The court found that defendant's assertion that his counsel was ineffective because of testimony given by psychiatric witnesses examined by counsel did not render the attorney's services constitutionally deficient. The circuit court erred by not viewing the home invasion charge as a lesser included offense of the murder charge, but vacation of the death sentence was not required as the trial court had not used home invasion as an aggravating factor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court in all aspects except the home invasion conviction, which it vacated because the home invasion charge was a lesser included offense of the murder charge. The court also vacated the corresponding 60-year sentence. The court directed the court's clerk to enter an order for the execution of the death sentence.

King v. Ryan


No. 72392.


Supreme Court of Illinois


153 Ill. 2d 449; 607 N.E.2d 154; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 198; 180 Ill. Dec. 260



December 4, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Albert Green, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Secretary of State appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted plaintiff driver's request for a declaration that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501.6 (1989) was unconstitutional and enjoined the enforcement of its summary suspension provisions against any driver in the state.


OVERVIEW: A driver involved in an accident passed a field sobriety test, refused to take a breath test, and was released without citation. The Secretary of State (Secretary) suspended the driver's license for six months. The driver filed, as an amendment to his injunction request, a complaint for administrative review. The circuit court granted the driver's request for a declaratory judgment that § 11-501.6 was unconstitutional and enjoined the Secretary from enforcing the summary suspension provisions against any driver in the state. The Secretary appealed. The court held that the driver's amended complaint vested the circuit court with subject matter jurisdiction. The court held that the driver's refusal could not result in suspension because the test was authorized under § 11-501.6, which violated U.S. Const. amend. IV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 6. The court held that § 11-501.6 unconstitutionally authorized a search and seizure of an individual not charged with any offense without requiring probable cause of intoxication and did not fall within the special needs exception because it was furthered the gathering of evidence for use in a criminal proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment enjoining the Secretary of State from suspending the driver's license for refusing to submit to chemical testing under an unconstitutional vehicle statute.

Ardt v. Illinois Dep't of Professional Regulation


No. 72440


Supreme Court of Illinois


154 Ill. 2d 138; 607 N.E.2d 1226; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 199; 180 Ill. Dec. 713



December 4, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Thomas O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Illinois Department of Professional Regulation (department) found that appellee dentist violated the advertising provisions of the Illinois Dental Practice Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 2301 et seq. (1987). The Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) affirmed the department's determination, but also held that § 32 of the act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch.111, para. 2332 (1987), was unconstitutional. The department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The department argued that the trial court did not have the authority to enter a stay of the department's sanction. On appeal, the court held that § 32, which required that the sanction remain intact during the pendency and hearing of the judicial proceedings, was unconstitutional. The trial court had the inherent equitable power to issue the stay, and to the extent that § 32 restricted the inherent power of the court, it was unconstitutional as a violation of separation of powers. Section 45 (Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 2345(h) (1987)) of the Illinois Dental Practice Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 2301 et seq., prohibited the use of the terms "family dentistry" and "family practice." The court found that total ban was unconstitutional because the terms could have applied to the dentist's client base rather than to a dental specialty. However, two other terms that the dentist used were misleading. Section 45's use of "false," "fraudulent," and "deceptive" were readily understandable by a person of ordinary intelligence and, thus, § 45 was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

256 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Reed v. Kusper


No. 70833


Supreme Court of Illinois


154 Ill. 2d 77; 607 N.E.2d 1198; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 208; 180 Ill. Dec. 685



December 4, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Eugene L. Wachowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Supreme Court remanded a matter in which appellee objectors filed objections to appellee new political party's actions to place their candidates' names on a ballot. Appellant county electoral board ruled on the objections, holding that the party's candidates were entitled to appear on the ballot, with the exception of two candidates, for which the party had failed to gather the necessary number of petition signatures.


OVERVIEW: The new party fielded candidates for all nonjudicial, countywide offices. The objectors argued that the party's petitions lacked the required number of signatures and did not meet other requirements of the Election Code (code), Ill Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 1-1 et seq. (1989). On appeal from the board's ruling on the objections, the trial court held that the signature shortfall and the party's failure to present judicial candidates resulted in a failure by the party to submit a "complete slate" of candidates as required by § 10-2 of the code and, therefore, all the candidates were ineligible for the ballot. The United States Supreme Court, granting certiorari, made a variety of rulings, but remanded on the issue of whether the lack of a judicial slate of candidates provided a ground for invalidating the new party's entire slate, as was held by the trial court. Upon remand, the court reversed the trial court's judgment on the issue. The court held that the judicial offices at issue were not offices of the political subdivision in which the new party was fielding candidates, and as such, there was not violation of § 10-2 due to the failure to field judicial candidates.


OUTCOME: The court on remand reversed the trial court's decision and held that the lack of judicial candidates on the new party's slate did not invalidate the party's entire slate.

People v. Todd


No. 70470


Supreme Court of Illinois


154 Ill. 2d 57; 607 N.E.2d 1189; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 210; 180 Ill. Dec. 676



December 4, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Clinton County, the Hon. Dennis Huber, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Circuit Court of Clinton County (Illinois) found that aggravating factors outweighed mitigating factors and sentenced defendant to death, defendant took a direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder, and found eligible for the death penalty as a result of attempted robbery and sexual assault. In affirming the conviction, the court held that the failure to object to testimony of a jailhouse informant did not show incompetence of counsel when there was no showing of a probability that, but for the errors, the result would have been different. While there was not a sufficient foundation that a scientific test was generally accepted as reliable, its admission was harmless and not prejudicial in the presence of other strong, physical evidence. The court's failure to specifically inform defendant that the vote of one juror would be sufficient to prevent imposition of the death sentence was not error, when defendant was informed that the jury would have to decide unanimously. In establishing eligibility for the death penalty the state did not have to prove that criminal intent for the other crime was formed before the murder. The court was free in the second phase of the sentencing hearing to consider any relevant and reliable evidence in aggravation and mitigation, including the brutal and heinous manner of the crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence of death, as defendant was eligible for the death penalty and the court weighed all relevant factors.

People ex rel. Hartigan v. E & E Hauling, Inc.

Supreme Court of Illinois


153 Ill. 2d 473; 607 N.E.2d 165; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 212; 180 Ill. Dec. 271



December 4, 1992, Filed

DISPOSITION: Appellate Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part; Circuit Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part; Cause Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff attorney general filed a complaint against defendant contractors alleging fraud and unjust enrichment claims arising under a construction contract with a governmental unit. The Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) reversed portions of the trial court decision granting the contractors' motions to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The contractors challenged the attorney general's standing under his common law powers and the court found that there was standing under Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 121/1-2 (1987) of the Consumer Fraud Act even though the allegedly defrauded parties were governmental units. The court found no allegations in the complaint supporting claims of common law fraud alleging that the representation contained in waivers submitted by the contractors were fraudulent or that injury resulted from reliance on them from the complaint or all reasonable inferences therefrom. The court found that claims of misrepresentation were stated with sufficient particularity and should not have been dismissed, but that only one of the claims under the Consumer Fraud Act was sufficiently pleaded. The court found that the unjust enrichment claim was properly dismissed because such a claim was only applicable in implied contract cases and could not have stood where there was an express contract between parties.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed in part and reversed in part, the judgment of the circuit court was affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the cause was remanded to the circuit court.

People v. Patterson


No. 70985


Supreme Court of Illinois


154 Ill. 2d 414; 610 N.E.2d 16; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 214; 182 Ill. Dec. 592



December 4, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 29, 1993. As Corrected March 31, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. John E. Morrissey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, following a double jury trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), of murders occurring during the commission of a forcible felony, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a)(3) (1985). The trial court sentenced defendant to death, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stabbed an elderly couple to death while committing a robbery at their residence with his co-defendant. Although there was no direct evidence linking defendant to the murders, the jury convicted him based upon, inter alia, a corroborated confession to police and assistant prosecutors. The trial court had denied defendant's motion to suppress his confession. Noting that only a preponderance of the evidence was necessary to show the voluntariness of a confession, the court held that the trial court's findings of voluntariness were not against the manifest weight of the evidence where one prosecutor testified that defendant indicated that he was treated fine and given food. Defendant's own testimony also revealed that he was given Miranda warnings at the time of his arrest, and there was conflicting testimony as to whether he had asked for an attorney. The court also ruled that the trial court did not err in admitting evidence of defendant's gang membership where it tended to establish motive and was not unduly prejudicial. It also ruled that a brief commentary on defendant's post-arrest silence was harmless error given the adequacy of a curative instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence.

People v. Sutherland

Supreme Court of Illinois

Post-conviction relief granted at, Cause remanded by People v. Sutherland, 194 Ill. 2d 289, 742 N.E.2d 306, 2000 Ill. LEXIS 1696, 252 Ill. Dec. 56 (2000)

People v. Cruz


Docket No. 70407


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


1992 Ill. LEXIS 221



December 4, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Petition for Rehearing Allowed May 28, 1993.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An appellate court reversed and remanded defendant's convictions for murder, deviate sexual assault, aggravated indecent liberties, aggravated kidnapping, and residential burglary because two codefendants had been tried with defendant and statements of the three codefendants were insufficiently redacted. Defendant was tried again, convicted, and sentenced to death in an Illinois trial court. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the State failed to tender to him material exculpatory evidence, that the State knowingly used perjured testimony, and that another suspect had committed the murder. The court affirmed the convictions. Because the evidence in the form of a scientific analysis of a piece of physical evidence did not exist until after the trial, there was no violation of the State's obligation to provide it to defendant. There was no basis in the record for finding that the State suborned perjury, or otherwise knowingly used false testimony because nothing in the record indicated that the statement was false at the time it was made or that the State had any reason to think that it was. Notwithstanding the extensive cross-examination and massive impeachment efforts, the jury concluded that defendant's guilt had been proved beyond a reasonable doubt. A rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt. There was sufficient evidence in the record which made defendant statutorily eligible for the death penalty and there was no constitutional impediment to imposition of the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder, deviate sexual assault, aggravated indecent liberties, aggravated kidnapping, and residential burglary and his death sentence.

People v. Flores


No. 70205


Supreme Court of Illinois


153 Ill. 2d 264; 606 N.E.2d 1078; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 185; 180 Ill. Dec. 1



November 19, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 1, 1993.
Writ of certiorari denied Flores v. Illinois, 510 U.S. 831, 114 S. Ct. 102, 126 L. Ed. 2d 68, 1993 U.S. LEXIS 5188 (1993)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. James M. Bailey, Judge, presiding.
People v. Flores, 128 Ill. 2d 66, 538 N.E.2d 481, 1989 Ill. LEXIS 38, 131 Ill. Dec. 106 (1989)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of armed robbery and murder. Defendant was sentenced to death. The court dismissed defendant's petition and subsequent petition for post-conviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he was denied effective assistance of counsel on direct appeal and in his first post-conviction proceeding. Defendant argued that counsel failed to recognize and assert an error in the State's closing argument to the jury and that counsel failed to assert as error the disparate sentencing between defendant and his co-defendant. The court affirmed. Though the comments were potentially misleading, they were not clear or focused in attempting to shift the sentencing responsibility. The prosecutor's argument did not improperly diminish the jury's sense of responsibility to impose the death penalty. Although defendant's prior juvenile conduct was of a less serious nature than his co-defendant's prior criminal conduct, the mitigation was not sufficient to preclude imposition of the death penalty. Defendant's death sentence was not improperly disparate. Defendant was not prejudiced by prior appellate counsel's performance.

Geja's Cafe v. Metropolitan Pier & Exposition Authority


Nos. 73986, 74045 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


153 Ill. 2d 239; 606 N.E.2d 1212; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 177; 180 Ill. Dec. 135



November 19, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, restaurant owners and patrons, filed an action against defendant Metropolitan Pier and Exposition Authority (Authority), challenging the constitutionality of an amendment to the Metropolitan Pier and Exposition Authority Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 1221 et seq. (1991). The Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) affirmed judgments in favor of the Authority. The restaurant owners and patrons appealed.


OVERVIEW: The restaurant owners and patrons asserted several constitutional challenges to the validity of Ill. Pub. Act 87-733 (act), as well as a tax that was imposed pursuant to the act on certain types of food and beverage sales. The court held that (1) the tax did not violate the Uniformity Clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2 (1970), which encompassed the equal protection clause of the United States Constitution and added even more limitations on government, because there was a real and substantial difference between those taxed and those not taxed and the tax was reasonably related to the increased benefits received by the restaurant owners within the taxing district; (2) the tax did not violate the Interstate Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, because the tax had a substantial nexus to the state, was fairly apportioned, did not discriminate against interstate commerce, and was fairly related to the services provided by the state; and (3) the act complied with the single subject requirement of the state constitution even though it may have implicated statutes already in effect, and may have even added a second subject to those statutes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to death for murder, attempted murder, aggravated arson, and two counts of armed robbery. The court found that the addition of different allegations of counsel's incompetence did not allow the relitigation of the issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of defendants' post-conviction petition and directed the clerk to fix the date of execution.

People v. Ward


No. 68274


Supreme Court of Illinois


154 Ill. 2d 272; 609 N.E.2d 252; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 186; 181 Ill. Dec. 884



November 19, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 16, 1992. Rehearing Denied March 29, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Richard E. Neville, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of murdering two people, armed robbery, and possession of a stolen motor vehicle. After a jury trial, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) found defendant eligible for the death penalty. The death sentence was stayed pending defendant's appeal of his convictions and the sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant beat one of his victims to death, shot her boyfriend, and stole their car. Defendant argued that numerous errors were committed by the court during his trial and the sentencing phase. The court found that 1) the testimony of a police officer that when he arrested defendant, defendant had brain matter on his face and clothing, was not offered as an expert opinion, but the officer permissibly made that conclusion based on his prior experience; 2) the police's failure to preserve the "white fleshy matter" was at most negligent, and defendant failed to show that the police did not preserve the evidence due to bad faith; 3) references to the victims' familial relationships were not so prejudicial as to deprive defendant of a fair trial; 4) placement of an alternate on the jury resulted did not result in a deprivation of due process, because defendant did not have a right to a jury of his choosing; 5) defendant was less than diligent in trying to locate his witnesses only one day prior to their scheduled testimony, not granting a continuance was proper; and finally 6) the death sentence was not be vacated because the aggravating factor was supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence for murder, armed robbery, and possession of a stolen vehicle.

People v. Shephard


No. 72085


Supreme Court of Illinois


152 Ill. 2d 489; 605 N.E.2d 518; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 157; 178 Ill. Dec. 724



October 22, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]

Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Ronald Himel, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with possession of narcotics with intent to deliver pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401(a)(1)(A), (c)(2) (1989). The state sought to enhance the penalty pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1407(b) (1989) because the acts occurred within 1,000 feet of public housing. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) ruled that § 1407(b) was unconstitutional. The state sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possession of heroin and cocaine with intent to deliver within 1,000 feet of public housing. The circuit court ruled that the penalty enhancement of the statute under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1407(b) was unconstitutional as applied to residents of public housing and dismissed the enhancement charge. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the conflict between amendments to the statute was resolved by 1991 Ill. Laws 3943, and defendant was properly charged with a violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1407(b) (1989), as well as Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401(c)(2) (1989); (2) personal liberty when deprived by lawful incarceration was not a fundamental right for purposes of equal protection analysis; (3) Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1407(b) was subject to rational basis review; and (4) § 1407(b) as applied to public housing did not deny drug offenders the equal protection of the laws.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which held that the enhancement of the penalty for possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance within 1,000 of public housing was unconstitutional. The court remanded the cause for further proceedings.

State Farm Fire & Casualty Co. v. Yapejian


No. 72486


Supreme Court of Illinois


152 Ill. 2d 533; 605 N.E.2d 539; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 158; 178 Ill. Dec. 745



October 22, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]

Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. John W. Darrah, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of the decision from the Appellate Court for the Second District, which affirmed the decision of the circuit court, which granted appellee insureds' motion for dismissal of the insurer's complaint. The court allowed the insurer's petition for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Insurer brought an action, which sought a declaration of its obligations under an automobile insurance policy issued to the insureds. On appeal, the insurer argued that the statutory language required arbitration with respect to questions of damages and liability only. The insureds argued that section 143a(1) of the Insurance Code, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 73, para. 755a(1), required that all disputes relating to uninsured motorist coverage be determined through arbitration. The court held that the language of §143a, which required the arbitration of any dispute with respect to such coverage, was ambiguous. The court concluded, after having applied appropriate tools of statutory construction, that the legislature intended a narrower reading of the statute. The court held that because of the far-reaching consequences of such a rule, the court would expect an explicit statement of legislative intent before concluding that the general assembly sought to transfer from the courts responsibility for resolving the vast array of issues that can arise with respect to uninsured motorist coverage.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate and circuit courts and remanded the case to the circuit court for further proceedings.

Rehg v. Illinois Dep't of Revenue


No. 72374


Supreme Court of Illinois


152 Ill. 2d 504; 605 N.E.2d 525; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 164; 178 Ill. Dec. 731



October 22, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]

Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County, the Hon. Harold L. Jensen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state revenue department and officials sought review of the order of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which held that the Cannabis and Controlled Substances Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 2151 et seq. (1989), was unconstitutional on its face and as applied and quashed the jeopardy assessment against the appellee inmate as a second punishment after the inmate's prior drug offense conviction.


OVERVIEW: The inmate convicted of drug offenses brought an action for declaratory relief, challenging the revenue department's jeopardy assessment of tax and penalties under the Cannabis and Controlled Substances Tax Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 2151 et seq.(1989). The trial court held that the Act was unconstitutional on its face and as applied and quashed the jeopardy assessment against the appellee inmate as a second punishment after the inmate's prior drug offense conviction. On appeal, the department argued that the Act's provisions were not criminal in nature. The court reversed and remanded, holding that the substantial tax and penalty imposed upon "dealers" under the Act were civil in nature, and the Act was not unconstitutional on its face for failing to provide such "dealers" with the constitutional safeguards which ordinarily accompany a criminal trial. However, the court remanded for a hearing on whether the civil penalty imposed on the inmate subsequent to his criminal conviction was so disproportionately large as to have constituted "punishment" within double jeopardy's multiple-punishment prohibition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's ruling that a tax on illegal drugs was unconstitutional on its face. The court remanded for a hearing as to its application to the inmate convicted of criminal drug offenses in order to determine whether the tax and penalty were remedial in character or so disproportionately large as to constitute only a second punishment.

Supreme Court of Illinois

DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged the decision of the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which reversed defendant's conviction and sentence for 97 counts of obscenity charges.


OVERVIEW: Police secured a warrant to seize from a bookstore magazines containing depictions of certain sexual acts and records pertaining to the same. Warrant returns indicated that multiple copies of magazines had been taken. Defendant was found guilty of 97 counts of obscenity, and the circuit court entered a judgment of conviction on each count. The appellate court reversed the judgment entered against defendant and remanded the cause for a new trial, concluding that the complaint was duplicitous, that magazines seized from a delivery man were improperly admitted into evidence, and that only one judgment of conviction could be entered and only one sentence imposed. The court agreed that the charging complaint was duplicitous and affirmed the appellate court's reversal of the circuit court conviction. The court reversed the appellate court's decision to remand to the circuit court for further proceedings, but noted that the state could file a new complaint against defendant. The court further held that seizure of all available copies of pornographic magazines without a prior judicial determination on the obscenity issue was an unconstitutional prior restraint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment reversing defendant's conviction on obscenity charges and reversed the appellate court's judgment remanding to the circuit court for further proceedings.

People v. Smith


No. 68474


Supreme Court of Illinois


152 Ill. 2d 229; 604 N.E.2d 858; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 143; 178 Ill. Dec. 335



October 15, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied November 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Themis N. Karnezis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed; death sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered convictions of murder, aggravated sexual assault, and home invasion, and also sentenced defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions were before the court on direct appeal of his death sentence. He had been convicted of sexual assault and the murder of the babysitter of a four-year-old child who was present during the crimes. The court held that: (1) neither the Fourth Amendment or the Illinois Constitution were violated when police officers listened to a conversation from outside defendant's apartment door in which he confessed to the murder; (2) even if it constituted an in-home seizure defendant's warrantless arrest was reasonable because of exigent circumstances; (3) defendant's girlfriend gave valid, voluntary consents on two occasions to the search of defendant's apartment; (4) defendant's in-custody confession was voluntary and given after a knowing and intelligent waiver of his Fifth Amendment rights; (5) the child's identification of the defendant was admissible as an excited utterance and the child's competency was not an issue in that situation; (6) submission of a life photograph of the victim was proper as part of the corpus delicti; and, (7) the trial court's refusal to "life-qualify" potential jurors violated defendant's constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's convictions for murder, aggravated sexual assault, and home invasion, but vacated his death sentence and remanded for a new sentencing hearing.

People v. Mitchell


No. 70247


Supreme Court of Illinois


152 Ill. 2d 274; 604 N.E.2d 877; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 152; 178 Ill. Dec. 354



October 15, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied November 30, 1992. As Corrected November 5, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County, the Hon. Lloyd A. Karmeier, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, St. Clair County (Illinois), convicting him of first degree murder and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder, and he was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed, arguing that the state violated his right to equal protection of the laws under the Fourteenth Amendment when the prosecutor engaged in purposeful racial discrimination by employing three peremptory challenges to exclude three black venirepersons from the jury. The court ruled that the equal protection clause of the Fourteenth Amendment forbade prosecutors from using peremptory challenges to strike potential jurors solely on the basis of their race. The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant, holding that the trial court's decision concerning the prosecutor's reasons for challenging the jurors was entitled to great deference on appeal and that a trial court's decision was only reversed if it was against the manifest weight of the evidence. The court concluded that the trial court's decision was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant and sentencing him to death was affirmed.

People v. DiGuida


No. 72272


Supreme Court of Illinois


152 Ill. 2d 104; 604 N.E.2d 336; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 135; 178 Ill. Dec. 80



October 1, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied November 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Michael S. Jordan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the decision from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed defendant's conviction for criminal trespass to real property under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 21-3(a) after defendant refused to leave the premises of a grocery store where he had been soliciting signatures for a political petition.


OVERVIEW: The state appealed the appeals court's reversal of defendant's conviction for criminal trespass to real property under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 21-3(a). Defendant was standing inside the grocery store gathering signatures on a nominating petition for a political candidate. The store manager asked defendant to leave. Defendant refused and the police arrested him and charged him with a misdemeanor complaint with criminal trespass to land. The trial court found defendant guilty. Defendant appealed his conviction, which was reversed by the appeals court. On further appeal, the court found that the evidence was insufficient to conclude that the store had presented itself as a forum for free expression and that its exclusion of defendant did not violate the constitution. The court reversed the judgment of the appeals court, and affirmed defendant's conviction.

People v. Ramey


No. 69889


Supreme Court of Illinois


152 Ill. 2d 41; 604 N.E.2d 275; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 121; 178 Ill. Dec. 19



September 24, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied November 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. John E. Morrissey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed; death sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought reversal of his murder conviction and death sentence contending that he was found eligible for a death sentence in violation of the Ex Post Facto Clause. He also claimed that his waiver of a sentencing jury was involuntary and that his confrontation rights were violated. The court affirmed the conviction, but vacated the death sentence and remanded the case for resentencing. Because the prohibition against ex post facto laws applied to new judicial interpretations of statutory law, the trial court erred in applying a decision on the mental state that rendered a defendant eligible for the death penalty to acts committed before the date of that decision. Defendant's constitutional right of confrontation under U.S. Const. amends. VI and XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 8 were denied where he was not permitted to question a witness concerning his motive to testify falsely. Under Illinois law, a defendant did not have to be expressly advised of the nonunanimity rule, whereby a single juror's vote would preclude imposition of the death penalty, for waiver of a jury at a capital sentencing hearing to be knowing, intelligent and voluntary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the murder conviction, but vacated the death sentence and remanded the case for a new sentencing hearing.

People v. Adams


Docket No. 69278


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


149 Ill. 2d 331; 597 N.E.2d 574; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 107; 173 Ill. Dec. 600; 61 U.S.L.W. 2128



July 30, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Patrick J. Morse, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted of prostitution, and under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3(g) (1989), were ordered to undergo medical testing to determine whether they were carriers of the human immunodeficiency virus (HIV), the cause of acquired immunodeficiency syndrome (AIDS). Defendants filed motions challenging § 5-5-3(g)'s constitutionality, and the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) held it was unconstitutional. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants' causes were consolidated. The trial court determined that § 5-5-3(g)'s testing procedure represented an illegal search and seizure and denied defendants equal protection. The court held that: (1) The challenged statute was not an unreasonable search and seizure under the provisions of the United States and Illinois Constitutions because it served a preventative purpose. The test required by § 5-5-3(g) represented only a minimal intrusion on the person tested, who by reason of his status as a convicted offender could claim only a diminished expectation of privacy; (2) The testing provision, as applied to defendants, did not deny them equal protection of the laws because the evidence indicated that sexual activity was one of the primary means by which HIV was transmitted from one person to another. It was then appropriate for the legislature to include prostitution among the criminal offenses for which testing would be required. Such a requirement bore a rational relationship to the state interest in combating the spread of AIDS; and (3) The governmental reports and professional studies cited in the parties' briefs were matters that could be considered by the court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court, which held the testing statute unconstitutional, and remanded the consolidated causes for further proceedings.

In re A Minor


Docket No. 71270


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


149 Ill. 2d 247; 595 N.E.2d 1052; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 101; 172 Ill. Dec. 382; 60 U.S.L.W. 2025; 20 Media L. Rep. 1372



June 25, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Ford County, the Hon. William M. Roberts, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appellate court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois) affirmed a trial court's decision to prohibit appellant newspaper from reporting the names of the juveniles in a court proceeding. The newspaper appealed.


OVERVIEW: Prior to the commencement of juvenile proceedings, a reporter from the newspaper wanted to gain admission to the proceedings. The trial court would not admit the reporter until he signed a pledge not to reveal the identity of the juvenile victims. The reporter was admitted on the condition that the identity of the minors would not be revealed. The newspaper appealed. The appellate court held that the trial court order erred to the extent that it prohibited the newspaper from reporting the names of the juveniles. However, the appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision to the extent that it prohibited the newspaper from reporting the names of the juveniles if the source of the identity was the attendance at the juvenile proceedings. On appeal, the newspaper acknowledged that it did not know the identities of the minors. The newspaper stood to gain knowledge of the minors' identities solely through attending the juvenile court proceedings. The court found that the minor victims did nothing to limit or diminish their constitutional right to be free from governmental and nongovernmental invasions of their privacy. Therefore, the appellate court's decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's decision, which affirmed a decision to prohibit the newspaper from reporting the names of juveniles, was affirmed.

Opyt's Amoco, Inc. v. South Holland


Docket No. 71580


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


149 Ill. 2d 265; 595 N.E.2d 1060; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 103; 172 Ill. Dec. 390



June 25, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Lawrence Carroll, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff merchants challenged an order of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which affirmed judgments that denied the merchants' cross-motion for summary judgment and granted defendant village's cross-motion for summary judgment. The merchants challenged the constitutionality of the village's Sunday Closing Ordinance, and defendant was convicted of violating that ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court affirmed a denial of the merchants' cross-motion for summary judgment and a grant of the village's cross-motion for summary judgment in an action in which the merchants challenged the constitutionality of the village's Sunday Closing Ordinance, and affirmed a defendant's conviction for violating that ordinance in a consolidated case. The court affirmed that judgment on appeal. The court reasoned that South Holland, Ill., Code art. I, § 9-3 was a commodity-type ordinance that was similar to an ordinance that precedent upheld, and that the record showed that the ordinance was a reasonable exercise of the village's police powers despite the exceptions that it contained. The court also held that the ordinance met the equal protection and due process requirements of the federal and the state constitutions by promoting a legitimate governmental interest, and by striking a reasonable balance between the public benefits of peace and quiet and the ability to purchase necessities. The court further concluded that a review of the ordinance's text revealed that it was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that affirmed the judgments in a consolidated case in which the merchants' cross-motion for summary judgment in their action against the village as to the constitutionality of a Sunday Closing Ordinance was denied and the village's cross-motion for summary judgment was granted, and in which defendant was convicted of violating that ordinance.

People v. Johnson


Docket No. 66545


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


149 Ill. 2d 118; 594 N.E.2d 253; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 104; 171 Ill. Dec. 401



June 25, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Johnson, 183 Ill. 2d 176, 700 N.E.2d 996, 1998 Ill. LEXIS 905, 233 Ill. Dec. 288 (1998)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Opinion of April 16, 1992, Previously Reported at: 1992 Ill. LEXIS 68.
People v. Sanders, 168 Ill. App. 3d 295, 522 N.E.2d 715, 1988 Ill. App. LEXIS 368, 119 Ill. Dec. 53 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1988)
People v. Johnson, 1992 Ill. LEXIS 68 (Ill., Apr. 16, 1992)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in an Illinois trial court of murder, attempted murder, and armed robbery. Defendant was sentenced to death for the murder and to 30 years of imprisonment each for two attempted murders, to be served consecutively to the death sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the procedure of a simultaneous jury trial deprived him of a fair trial, that evidence concerning the victim's family was inadmissible, that the trial judge failed to take into account any mitigating factors, and that the trial judge improperly imposed the death sentence based upon a belief that defendant would escape from prison and kill again. The court affirmed. The State's occurrence witnesses were subject to cross-examination before defendant's jury. The record was overwhelming as to defendant's presence and participation in the crimes such that it negated his defense of misidentification and his alibi. The testimony of the victim's brothers concerning the family was relevant and properly presented at trial. The evidence was incidental to other relevant testimony of the victim's brothers and it was not presented in such a manner as to cause the jury to believe it was material. The sentencing judge did not fail to take note of the mitigating factors. Rather, he took them into account and found them insufficient to preclude the sentence of death. Defendant failed to prove any link between the alleged improper statements and the trial judge's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder, attempted murder, and armed robbery and the sentence of death.

 

286 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hamm


Docket Nos. 72034, 72035, 72036 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


149 Ill. 2d 201; 595 N.E.2d 540; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 94; 172 Ill. Dec. 179



June 9, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Schuyler County, the Hon. Carson D. Klitz, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgments affirmed in part and reversed in part; causes remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, the state challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Schuyler County (Illinois), which declared unconstitutional certain sections of The Fish Code of 1971, Ill. Rev. Stat. 56/2.4(a) (1989), in connection with a complaint alleging that each defendant had knowingly possessed and captured or killed aquatic life of species protected by the statute for commercial purposes.


OVERVIEW: The state charged defendants with knowingly possessing and capturing or killing aquatic life of species protected by the Fish Code of 1971 (Code), Ill. Rev. Stat. 56/2.4(a) (1989), for commercial purposes. Defendants filed motions to dismiss the felony counts, arguing that the Code was impermissibly vague, denied equal protection of the law, and provided a penalty disproportionate to the crimes. The trial court, dismissing defendants' charges, ruled that although the Code was not constitutionally vague, it violated equal protection because it treated a person fishing commercially differently than a person fishing for his own use. The state appealed. On appeal, the court held that those who fish for profit have a stronger motive, monetary gain, than a sport fisherman to illegally take as many fish as possible, and, therefore, the Code properly attacked the problem of commercial fishing when it provided the Class 3 felony in para. 2.4. The court held that the Code was not vague but reversed the trial court's decision with respect to equal protection, concluding that para. 2.4(a) of the Code did not violate equal protection under either the U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Ill Const. art. I.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision, finding that the Fish Code was not vague and held that those who fish commercially and for profit have a stronger motive of monetary gain to illegally take as many fish as possible. The court, however, reversed the trial court's decision with respect to equal protection and concluded that the Fish Code did not violate equal protection under either the U.S Constitution or under Illinois Constitution.

Central City Educ. Ass'n v. Illinois Educational Labor Relations Bd.


Docket Nos. 70425, 70584, 70609 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


149 Ill. 2d 496; 599 N.E.2d 892; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 97; 174 Ill. Dec. 808



June 9, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied October 5, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 70425. - Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on a petition for review of an order of the Illinois Educational Labor Relations Board.

Nos. 70584, 70609. - Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on a petition for review of an order of the Illinois Educational Labor Relations Board.



DISPOSITION: No. 70425--Affirmed; cause remanded. Nos. 70584 & 70609--Appellate court judgment reversed; IELRB decision set aside; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Teacher's unions filed complaints with appellant, the Illinois Educational Labor Relations Board (IELRB), against appellee school districts for failure to bargain regarding a reduction in force (RIF) and a teachers' evaluation plan. The IELRB held that the school districts must bargain about the evaluation plan, but not the RIF. The Appellate Courts for the First and Fourth Districts (Illinois) reversed. The appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: The school districts argued that their right not to bargain over the evaluation plans was resolved in negotiations and that the RIF was a matter of inherent managerial policy. The court reversed and remanded the order regarding the evaluation plans and affirmed but remanded the RIF case. In determining that the RIF was not a subject for mandatory bargaining, the IELRB did not use the three-part test. Because the application of the mandatory bargaining test required a detailed factual analysis that the IELRB was particularly well suited to examine, the court remanded the RIF cases to the IELRB for further proceedings. The IELRB found that the bargaining history of the parties overcame the school district's allegations that the "zipper clause" constituted a clear and unmistakable waiver of the right to bargain teacher evaluation plans. The extrinsic evidence showed that the parties could not have intended to allow the "zipper clause" to preclude bargaining over a subject which would violate the law if not resolved. The school district did not make any arguments that warranted reversing the IELRB's decision that the evaluation plans must be bargained over.


OUTCOME: The order that an RIF for economic reasons was a mandatory subject of bargaining was affirmed and remanded to the IELRB for further proceedings. The order that the teachers' evaluations plan was not subject to bargaining due to the "zipper clause" was reversed and remanded to the IELRB for further proceedings.

People v. Hampton


Docket No. 70758


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


149 Ill. 2d 71; 594 N.E.2d 291; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 93; 171 Ill. Dec. 439



May 21, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] etition for Rehearing Denied June 25, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County, the Hon. A.A. Matoesian, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to three counts of first degree murder and waived his right to have a jury at his death penalty hearing. The trial judge found that defendant was eligible for the death penalty and that there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude a sentence of death. The judge entered an order sentencing defendant to death, and defendant appealed. The death sentence was stayed pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed sentence of death imposed after he pled guilty. Defendant did not contest the validity of his guilty pleas and did not challenge his guilt on the three murder counts. Rather, defendant's contentions of error were directed exclusively toward his sentencing hearing and the propriety of his death sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that defendant's eligibility for the death penalty was proved beyond a reasonable doubt. The court opined that defendant's presentence interview did not violate his right to the assistance of counsel. The court found that there was no indication that defendant was deprived of the meaningful advice of his counsel prior to the interview or that he was forced to proceed with the interview after requesting and being denied counsel. The court held that defendant was not denied the effective assistance of counsel. The court articulated that it found no constitutional infirmity in the mandate of the state's death penalty statute that death be imposed if the sentencer determined that there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude that sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court.

People v. Easley


Docket No. 69387


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


148 Ill. 2d 281; 592 N.E.2d 1036; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 72; 170 Ill. Dec. 356



April 16, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied June 1, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Livingston County, the Hon. Charles E. Glennon, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a prison inmate, was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois) of first degree murder of a prison guard. The jury concluded that there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude imposition of the death penalty, and the trial judge sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed and the death sentence was stayed pending direct review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the police engaged in coercive behavior and overreaching in order to obtain an inculpatory statement from him and that gang-related evidence was improperly introduced at trial and in the State's closing argument. The State argued that defendant was not in custody during the second interrogation. The court affirmed the conviction. Defendant was in custody and was entitled to Miranda warnings because he was not free to leave. A deputy advised him that he could be subject to the death penalty and defendant made an inculpatory statement. Although the propriety of the deputy's statement was questionable, it was not the "functional equivalent" of interrogation. The gang-related evidence was improperly admitted at trial and the statements the State made during closing argument were improper. However, when considering the impact of the evidence under all the attendant circumstances, defendant was not denied a fair and impartial trial despite the erroneous admission of the evidence. The State's comments in closing, although inflammatory, did not amount to substantial prejudice because there was overwhelming evidence in support of defendant's guilt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree murder and the sentence of death.

People v. Reed


Docket No. 71707


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


148 Ill. 2d 1; 591 N.E.2d 455; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 73; 169 Ill. Dec. 282



April 16, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County, the Hon. David W. Watt, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with two counts of aggravated criminal sexual abuse, contrary to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-16(d) (1987). The Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois) granted defendant's motion to dismiss and held that the statute violated equal protection. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with aggravated criminal sexual abuse at times when he was 19 and 20 years of age. The state alleged that defendant, on two occasions, once when he was 19 years old and once when he was 20, knowingly engaged in acts of sexual penetration with a 13-year-old victim. The statute provided that if the accused was less than five years older than the victim, the offense was criminal sexual abuse, and if the accused was five or more years older than the victim, the offense was aggravated criminal sexual abuse. Defendant argued that the interplay of the sections violated equal protection guarantees of the Federal and State Constitutions. The court reversed the lower court and held that what could have been considered sexual experimentation by a 15-year-old girl and 18-year-old boyfriend, could have been sexual exploitation between a 15-year-old girl and a 19 or 20 year old man. The court held that the purpose of the statute was to protect children from sexual exploitation by adults that were five or more years older than the victim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the dismissal of the case for violation of equal protection.

People v. Anderson


Docket Nos. 71877, 71878, 71879, 71880, 71881, 71882, 71883, 71884, 71885, 71886, 71887, 71888 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


148 Ill. 2d 15; 591 N.E.2d 461; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 75; 169 Ill. Dec. 288; 30 A.L.R.5th 840



April 16, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McDonough County, the Hon. Ronald C. Tenold, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the judgments of the Circuit Court of McDonough County (Illinois), which ruled that the hazing statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1989, ch. 144, pars. 221 and 222, was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague as applied to defendants, university students.


OVERVIEW: University students, were charged with the violation of the hazing statute, which resulted in the death of an initiate from alcohol poisoning. The trial court dismissed the hazing charges on the grounds it was unconstitutional. The court held the statute was not facially overbroad. The court determined that the hazing statute reached only conduct which recklessly, knowingly, or intentionally resulted in the bodily injury of a person. Next, the court held that the hazing statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to university students' conduct. The court determined that university students were given fair warning of the statute's proscriptions and the statute did not promote arbitrary enforcement. Finally, the court held that the hazing statute did not violate equal protection and the limitation of special legislation. The court concluded that there was a rational basis for limiting the reach of the hazing statute to educational institutions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the trial court and remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Burrows


Docket No. 69161


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


148 Ill. 2d 196; 592 N.E.2d 997; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 58; 170 Ill. Dec. 317



March 26, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied June 1, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Iroquios County, the Hon. John F. Michela, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by a jury of the Circuit Court of Iroquois County (Illinois) for murder and armed robbery. Defendant was sentenced to death, and his sentence was stayed pending direct review by the state supreme court. A previous trial resulted in a mistrial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of the murder and armed robbery of an 88 year-old man. Defendant's first trial resulted in a mistrial. On appeal, defendant raised a number of issues relating to the pretrial phase of the trial, the guilt phase, sentencing, and the constitutionality of the Illinois death penalty statute. Defendant contended that double jeopardy prohibited a death penalty hearing in his second trial because his first trial resulted in a mistrial due to the jury's inability to reach a verdict. Therefore, defendant argued that the jury in the first trial, which could have been the sentencing jury, implicitly acquitted him of the death penalty when at least one of its members voted to acquit. The state maintained that the jury in the first trial failed to reach a verdict and that consequently no sentencing jury acquitted the defendant of the death penalty. In affirming defendant's sentence, the court found that because no sentencing hearing took place at the conclusion of his first trial, there was no death penalty acquittal, and the state was not barred from seeking the death penalty in the second trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder and armed robbery convictions and his sentence of death. The court held that there was no death-penalty acquittal, and that double jeopardy did not preclude imposition of the death penalty.

People v. Ganus


Docket No. 70147


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


148 Ill. 2d 466; 594 N.E.2d 211; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 61; 171 Ill. Dec. 359



March 26, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal fromthe Circuit Court of Randolph County, the Hon. Jerry D. Flynn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Randolph County (Illinois), which convicted him for three counts of murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after he made an oral statement in which he described the killing of an inmate. Defense counsel established through cross-examination of a state witness that the victim had raped someone who might have been associated with a gang, defendant's position in the gang was such that he was subject to orders from others in the gang, disobeying such an order could lead to being killed, and most prison killings were gang-related. Defendant was convicted for murder and sentenced to death. On appeal, defendant argued, inter alia, that he was denied effective assistance of counsel. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence, holding that: (1) in terms of defense-strategy, the gang-activity evidence was legitimate even though defendant was not entitled to a compulsion defense where the evidence was relevant as mitigation and its use as mitigating evidence was defense counsel's principle reason for eliciting it; (2) defendant's conviction was the result of a highly corroborated confession rather than the inflammatory gang evidence; and (3) a weak or insufficient defense did not indicate ineffectiveness of counsel where defendant had no defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for three counts of murder and the imposition of the death sentence.
