SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) ordering him to receive a capital sentence after his convictions for murder and attempted armed robbery. Appellant asserted that certain evidence ought to have been suppressed at the trial, that the charges were issued improperly, that he received ineffective assistance of counsel, and that the sentencing judge did not consider mitigating evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant defendant was convicted of murder and armed robbery and sentenced to death, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 9-1 (1985). XIV, having informed him of the charges against him, Ill. Const. art. I §§ 2, 7, 8, and were sufficiently related to his indictment so as to have afforded him the opportunity to prepare a defense. Similarly, the court found that appellant had not been denied effective assistance of counsel because his attorney had performed reasonably. The court also found that the sentencing judge had considered the mitigating evidence and upheld the validity of the death penalty statute, ch. 38, par 9-1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, finding that appellant defendant's confessions and other evidence had been properly admitted. The court found that jury instructions were properly issued, that the indictment had not been misleading, and that defendant's counsel had performed reasonably and was not ineffective. Also, the court found the judge had properly considered mitigating evidence and upheld the validity of the death penalty.

Mizell v. Passo


No. 69766


Supreme Court of Illinois


147 Ill. 2d 420; 590 N.E.2d 449; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 42; 168 Ill. Dec. 812

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Vermilion County, the Hon. Rita B. Garman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former patient sought review of the order of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which vacated the trial court's order that granted his motion for voluntary dismissal in favor of the defendant doctor.


OVERVIEW: The former patient filed a healing art malpractice action against the doctor. Attached to the complaint was an affidavit of his attorney that stated that he had been unable to obtain the written report of a reviewing health professional, as required by Ill. Code Civ. P. 2-622(a)(1), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-622(a)(1) (1987). The former patient later filed a motion to waive the Code's requirement. The doctor then filed a motion for a protective order, requesting that the trial court stay discovery until the former patient complied with the Code. The doctor subsequently filed a motion for judgment, and the former patient later filed a motion for voluntary dismissal. The trial court allowed the former patient's motion and the appellate court later vacated this decision. The court reversed the order of the appellate court by holding that the trial court properly exercised its discretion by hearing and ruling upon the former patient's motion to voluntarily dismiss the complaint before it reached the doctor's motion for judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order, which vacated the trial court's order that granted the former patient's motion for voluntary dismissal in favor of the doctor because the trial court properly exercised its discretion by hearing and ruling upon the former patient's motion to voluntarily dismiss the complaint before it reached the doctor's motion for judgment.

People v. Hope


No. 58037


Supreme Court of Illinois


147 Ill. 2d 315; 589 N.E.2d 503; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 34; 168 Ill. Dec. 103



March 12, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Remand from the United States Supreme Court pursuant to petition for certiorari.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's murder conviction was vacated and remanded by the United States Supreme Court, which granted his petition for certiorari after the court affirmed his convictions and rejected his claim that the state had unconstitutionally discriminated on the basis of race through peremptory challenges during voir dire. The court had also vacated the death sentence, finding that victim impact statements were inadmissible at the sentencing hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried for the murder of a police officer. During jury selection, the state exercised peremptory challenges against five black perspective jurors, which effectively excluded all black venire members. Defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. At the sentencing hearing, the trial court allowed the victim's mother and sister to testify as to the impact the murder had on their lives. On appeal, the court remanded for a Batson hearing to determine whether the state had discriminated on the basis of race by its peremptory challenges. The trial court held that there was no evidence of racial discrimination. On remand from the Supreme Court, the court vacated defendant's conviction, finding that the state's explanations for the peremptory challenges were pretexts for racial discrimination because they relied upon the demeanor of jurors and there were inconsistencies in that young blacks were excused while young whites served, and unemployed blacks were excused, but not unemployed whites. The court also held that the victim impact statements were admissible at the sentencing phase under the Illinois Bill of Rights for Victims and Witnesses of Violent Crimes Act.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's murder conviction and remanded to the trial court.

People v. Griffin


Docket Nos. 62397, 69286 cons.


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


148 Ill. 2d 45; 592 N.E.2d 930; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 37; 170 Ill. Dec. 250



March 12, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied June 1, 1992.
Writ of certiorari denied Griffin v. Illinois, 507 U.S. 924, 113 S. Ct. 1293, 122 L. Ed. 2d 684, 1993 U.S. LEXIS 1320 (1993)
Writ of habeas corpus denied United States ex rel. Griffin v. Mathy, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 67350 (N.D. Ill., July 29, 2009)
Related proceeding at People v. Griffin, 2014 IL App (1st) 120999-U, 2014 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 995 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Earl E. Strayhorn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was convicted of murder, solicitation to commit murder, and conspiracy to commit murder. The defendant was sentenced to death. The Illinois Circuit Court of Cook County granted the state's motion to dismiss the defendant's petition for post-conviction relief. The defendant sought review of the judgment of dismissal.


OVERVIEW: The victim was a member of a prominent drug operation. Another member of the drug operation contacted the police and told them that he had information regarding the murder. The informant indicated that the defendant was responsible for the victim's murder and testified to those facts at the defendant's trial. On appeal, the defendant contended that substantial perjury was employed to convict him and that the state's attorney's office knew or should have known of the perjured evidence. The defendant's petition for post-conviction relief specifically stated that the informant was paid by the state's attorney's office to lie at the defendant's trial. Upon review, the supreme court affirmed the dismissal of the defendant's petition. The supreme court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in ruling on the allegations of the defendant's petition without conducting an evidentiary hearing. The state established a proper foundation for the admittance of a tape-recorded telephone conversation between the defendant and the informant. The defendant failed to provide sufficient evidence to support his claim for ineffective assistance of trial counsel.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the defendant's petition for post-conviction relief was affirmed.

DeLuna v. St. Elizabeth's Hosp.


Nos. 68937, 68952


Supreme Court of Illinois


147 Ill. 2d 57; 588 N.E.2d 1139; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 27; 167 Ill. Dec. 1009; 60 U.S.L.W. 2551



February 20, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 30, 1992.
Rehearing denied by, 03/30/1992
Related proceeding at DeLuna v. Treister, 286 Ill. App. 3d 25, 676 N.E.2d 973, 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 886, 222 Ill. Dec. 9 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1996)
Related proceeding at DeLuna v. Burciaga, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 783 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Aug. 5, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Willard J. Lassers and Hon. Thomas R. Rakowski, Judges, presiding.
DeLuna v. St. Elizabeth's Hosp., 184 Ill. App. 3d 802, 540 N.E.2d 847, 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 858, 132 Ill. Dec. 925 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1989)



DISPOSITION: No. 68937 -- Judgment reversed. No. 68952 -- Judgment vacated; appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant filed a malpractice action against defendants, hospital and doctor, but failed to file an affidavit in compliance with Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-622 (1987) from a health professional declaring that the action had merit. The trial court dismissed the claimant's action but the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) declared para. 2-622 unconstitutional and reversed. The hospital and doctor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court declared Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-622 (1987) unconstitutional on the grounds that it violated the separation of powers clause of the Illinois Constitution. The court found that the statute did not violate separation of powers clause because it did not require the doctor who must be consulted to exercise a judicial function. The doctor merely certified that in his opinion the action had reasonable merit and this act was essentially no different from testifying at trial to the standard of care and its breach. The requirements also served the same end as Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 137, which required an attorney to certify that pleading were based on fact and made in good faith. The court also found that para. 2-622 was a legitimate procedural rule and did not infringe on the claimant's rights of access to the court's. Finally, where para. 2-622 was rationally related to the legitimate government interest of curtailing frivolous law suits it did not violate Due Process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court, which had found in favor of the claimant, vacated the judgment and dismissed the appeal.

McAlister v. Schick


No. 71157


Supreme Court of Illinois


147 Ill. 2d 84; 588 N.E.2d 1151; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 28; 167 Ill. Dec. 1021



February 20, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County, the Hon. Harris H. Agnew, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois) affirmed the dismissal of plaintiff patient's medical malpractice complaint against defendants, doctor and anesthesiologist group, for failure to comply with requirements of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 100, para. 2-622. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient was admitted to the hospital for treatment of a small bowel obstruction, and subsequently underwent surgery. The patient alleged that the doctor, who was a member of the anesthesiologist group, failed to inform him of the risks involved in the surgery, and failed to properly insert and monitor a catheter. The patient attached to his complaint an affidavit stating that he had been unable to obtain a consultation with a health professional, and could not obtain one before the expiration of the statute of limitations. The issue on appeal was whether § 2-622, which required that the patient attach to the complaint an affidavit certifying that he had consulted and reviewed the facts of the case with a health professional who had determined in an attached report that there was a reasonable and meritorious malpractice cause for filing the complaint, was unconstitutional. The court held that § 2-622 did not deprive the patient of a constitutionally guaranteed remedy, and thus was not unconstitutional. The legislature, in enacting § 2-622, did not encroach on judicial power and the health care professional did not exercise judicial power.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the patient's complaint was affirmed.

People v. St. Pierre


No. 69238


Supreme Court of Illinois


146 Ill. 2d 494; 588 N.E.2d 1159; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 29; 167 Ill. Dec. 1029



February 20, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Richard E. Neville, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part and Vacated in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted and sentenced defendant for murder.


OVERVIEW: On remand from a previously overturned conviction by a jury for murder and other charges, defendant pleaded guilty to the trial court for murder, armed robbery, conspiracy to commit murder, and concealment of a homicidal death. Defendant also agreed to sentencing by the trial court. On appeal, defendant claimed he pleaded guilty because of dangerous conditions at the jail. The court affirmed the conviction and sentencing to death by the trial court. After reviewing the record, the court concluded that defendant knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily entered his guilty plea, and that the trial judge repeatedly and thoroughly advised defendant of his rights and the attendant consequences of entering a guilty plea. The court also found that defendant knowingly and intelligently waived his right to a jury for sentencing. The court noted that defendant was aware that a sentencing jury had to agree unanimously as to the death sentence. Further, the court held that the fact that defendant was not admonished that a sentencing jury would be unaware of his prior death sentence did not invalidate his otherwise valid waiver and his sentence was not disproportionate to his crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence of death, but vacated defendant's conviction and sentence of imprisonment for conspiracy to commit murder.

Department of Public Aid ex rel. Cox v. Miller


No. 71687


Supreme Court of Illinois


146 Ill. 2d 399; 586 N.E.2d 1251; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 10; 166 Ill. Dec. 922; 60 U.S.L.W. 2519



January 30, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County, the Hon. Arthur H. Gross, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate Court Reversed; Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Illinois Department of Public Aid, sought review of an order entered in the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois) that reversed an order denying a motion filed by respondent, a putative father, to dismiss a paternity action filed on behalf of a minor.


OVERVIEW: The Illinois Department of Public Aid filed an action on behalf of a minor to establish a putative father's paternity, for reimbursement of public aid provided to the minor and her mother, and for future support for the minor. The putative father filed a motion to dismiss based on a settlement agreement entered in an earlier paternity action filed against him by the mother. The court determined that the settlement order and dismissal entered in the earlier paternity action did not bar the subsequent action, and held that equal protection of the law would be violated if a right to seek support from their parents was denied to nonmarital children where no marital child was barred from seeking support by settlements existing between the parents. The court ruled that the Illinois Parentage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1451 et seq. (1989), specifically Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2512.1 (1989), allowed the child to bring an action seeking support from her parents.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's order reversing the denial of the putative father to dismiss the paternity action filed by the Illinois Department of Public Aid, ruling that a settlement in an earlier paternity suit filed by the mother did not bar the action. The court remanded the case to the trial court with directions to ascertain paternity.

Supreme Court of Illinois

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Effingham County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss in the state's criminal case charging defendant with operation of a motor vehicle while in possession of an intoxicating liquor and driving while under the influence of alcohol.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with operation of a motor vehicle while in possession of an intoxicating liquor and driving while under the influence of alcohol. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, holding that the state's charging of defendant under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 18b-108 clearly laid out the penalty and the prohibited conduct; thus, it was not vague.

People ex rel. Burris v. Ryan


No. 72662


Supreme Court of Illinois


147 Ill. 2d 270; 588 N.E.2d 1033; 1992 Ill. LEXIS 1; 167 Ill. Dec. 903



January 14, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  147 Ill. 2d 270 at 293.


PRIOR HISTORY: Map approved.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Map approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand to comply with directives of the Supreme Court of Illinois, defendant, the Legislative Redistricting Commission, held expedited hearings in regard to the redistricting map it had submitted and another proposed remedial redistricting plan submitted by certain intervenor-plaintiff voters. The maps were submitted for judicial approval.


OVERVIEW: The dispute arose out of the submission of the redistricting map by the Commission and another map submitted by certain voters. The court concluded that the Commission had complied with the procedural and substantive directives of its earlier opinion and Ill. Const. art. IV, § 3. The court found that the Commission had heard testimony by experts on behalf of the parties, and reviewed affidavits filed on behalf of the parties, as well as voluminous documents. The court held that after reviewing all of the evidence submitted, it found that both plans were similar regarding compactness. However, the Commission map met all of the requirements of the four-prong test and a map submitted by the constitutionally mandated Commission was valid unless it was against the manifest weight of the evidence. In finding the map valid, the court did not judge the credibility of each expert, but rather relied on the statistics provided.


OUTCOME: The court approved the map submitted by the Commission and ordered that the State Board of Elections establish the boundaries in accordance with the map.

SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS

DISPOSITION: Redistricting map approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State sought to have a redistricting map approved in its action against defendants, who submitted an alternative map.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the court's previous order, a legislative redistricting commission had hearings on the redistricting plans in compliance with Ill. Const. art. IV, § 3. Upon consideration, the court adopted the commission's plan submitted on behalf of the State. The court held that the map submitted by the constitutionally-mandated commission was valid pursuant to Ill. Const. art. IV, § 3(b), unless it was against the manifest weight of the evidence. Based on its review of four requirements for a valid redistricting, the court determined that both plans met the constitutional compactness requirement. However, the court found that only the commission's plan satisfied the other three requirements, which included substantially equal population in each district, provision of adequate representation of minorities and other special interests, and political fairness. The court noted that, in making its determination, it relied on the statistics provided rather that judging the credibility of the experts.


OUTCOME: The court adopted the State's redistricting plan.

The defendant raised a number of issues concerning the guilt-innocence phase of the proceedings, including insufficient evidence of the corpus delicti of the offense, that his statements were coerced and thus involuntary and inadmissible, challenged the jury selection, argued the prosecutor's comments were improper, asserted there were restrictions on cross-examination of the witness, stated the trial court erred in denying a request for mistrial due to a spectator's outburst, and challenged the prosecutor's closing argument. People v. Johnson


No. 67319


Supreme Court of Illinois


146 Ill. 2d 109; 585 N.E.2d 78; 1991 Ill. LEXIS 120; 165 Ill. Dec. 682



November 27, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 3, 1992. As Corrected February 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. James M. Bailey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9--1(a) (1985), and aggravated criminal sexual assault. The jury found that he was eligible for the death penalty under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9--1(b)(6) (1985), and further found that there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude a sentence of death. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) thus sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal the court rejected defendant's contentions 1) that the evidence established that he was legally insane; 2) that if not insane, he should have been found guilty but mentally ill; 3) that the prosecutor's improper jury argument required a reversal; and 4) that the prosecutor's reference to the likelihood that defendant would commit a future murder was not supported by the evidence. The evidence in the record supported the jury's finding that defendant failed to prove his insanity by a preponderance of the evidence because the sole psychiatric expert to testify at trial unequivocally stated that defendant was attempting to fake insanity. The evidence that defendant was a sadist and suffered from an antisocial personality disorder did not compel either an insanity or a mentally ill verdict. The prosecutor's statement to the jury that "you don't sentence him" was improper but when viewed in context did not diminish the jury's sense of responsibility in determining the appropriateness of defendant's death sentence. The psychiatric expert testified that defendant told him that his "purpose in life" was to kill and that, should he be released, he would kill again.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court that sentenced defendant to death. The court directed the clerk of the court to enter an order setting Tuesday, March 10, 1992, as the date on which the sentence of death entered by the circuit court was to be carried out.

People v. Simmons


No. 70542


Supreme Court of Illinois


145 Ill. 2d 264; 583 N.E.2d 484; 1991 Ill. LEXIS 117; 164 Ill. Dec. 568



November 21, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County, the Hon. Lehman Krause, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Jefferson County (Illinois), which held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, § 3 -- 707 (1989) violated appellee driver's right to equal protection of the laws. Appellee was issued a traffic citation charging him with operating an uninsured motor vehicle in violation of the statute.


OVERVIEW: The issue for the court was whether § 3 -- 707 of the vehicle code was constitutional. The driver argued that § 3 -- 707 violated the equal protection clause because it discriminated against the working poor, and violated the U.S. Const. amend. VIII because the $ 500 minimum fine for a violation was excessive. The court disagreed and found that § 3 -- 707 neither denied the driver equal protection of the laws, nor mandated an excessive fine. The statute did not violate the equal protection clause of either the United States Constitution or the State of Illinois Constitution because no classification was created based on wealth. There was no doubt that the $ 500 fine for violating the mandatory liability insurance requirement had a much greater financial impact on those persons who were the working poor, but this disparity in economic impact did not give rise to an equal protection violation. The $ 500 minimum fine set out in § 3 -- 707 was not cruel, degrading, or so wholly disproportionate to the offense committed as to shock the moral sense of the community.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the circuit court that held that the vehicle code was unconstitutional and remanded the case.

 

311 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. P.H.


No. 70875


Supreme Court of Illinois


145 Ill. 2d 209; 582 N.E.2d 700; 1991 Ill. LEXIS 105; 164 Ill. Dec. 137



October 31, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Harry B. Aron, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which held the gang-transfer provision, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 805-4(3.1) (1989), of the Juvenile Court Act of 1987, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 801-1 et seq. (1989), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the gang-transfer provision, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 805-4(3.1) (1989), of the Juvenile Court Act of 1987, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 801-1 et seq. (1989), plaintiff state moved to prosecute defendant minor under the criminal laws. When the circuit court found para. 805-4(3.1) unconstitutional, review was sought, and the court reversed. The court held para. 805-4(3.1) had not violated the separation of powers because it neither deprived the juvenile court of jurisdiction nor infringed on the judiciary's powers. The court also held para. 805-4(3.1) had not violated double jeopardy because a transfer hearing was not tantamount to an adjudication as findings made during the hearing were not dispositive of guilt. Furthermore, the court held para. 805-4(3.1) had not violated equal protection because its aim was at decreasing gang violence and thus, was reasonably related to a legitimate governmental interest. Finally, the court held para. 805-4(3.1) had not violated procedural due process because there was no risk of a deprivation of a minor's interest in avoiding prosecution as an adult through the use of para. 805-4(3.1)'s procedures.


OUTCOME: Court reversed a judgment finding the Juvenile Court Act of 1987's gang transfer provision was unconstitutional because the provision, which had not infringed on the judiciary, had not violated separation of powers, had not violated double jeopardy as a transfer hearing was not an adjudication, had not violated equal protection under the rational basis standard, and had not violated procedural due process as there was no interest deprivation.

People v. Adams


No. 70462


Supreme Court of Illinois


144 Ill. 2d 381; 581 N.E.2d 637; 1991 Ill. LEXIS 88; 163 Ill. Dec. 483



October 17, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. John J. Bowman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which affirmed the trial court's judgment that required defendant to register as a habitual child sex offender pursuant to the Habitual Child Sex Offender Registration Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 221 et seq. (1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of criminal sexual assault under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-13(a)(3). The lower court affirmed the trial court's decision that required defendant to register as a habitual child sex offender pursuant to the Habitual Child Sex Offender Registration Act (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 221 et seq. (1987). The court held that the act was not cruel and unusual punishment under U.S. Const. amend. VIII. It further held that the act did not deny defendant equal protection or due process in violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 11. The court found that the statutory duty to register was neither imprisonment nor a fine and did not impose any restraints on defendant's liberty or property. Thus, such a duty was not punishment. The court held that the act did not arbitrarily differentiate among various sex offenders because the legislature was concerned with the direct victimization of children not child pornographers or those who used children for prostitution. Finally, the court held that the omission of the certification order was merely an administrative oversight that had no effect on defendant's substantive rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision that defendant was properly required to register as a habitual child sex offender pursuant to the Habitual Child Sex Offender Registration Act (act). The court found that the act was designed to aid law enforcement agencies by requiring habitual child sex offenders to register with the local law enforcement authorities whenever such offenders moved.

People v. Williams


No. 65249


Supreme Court of Illinois


147 Ill. 2d 173; 588 N.E.2d 983; 1991 Ill. LEXIS 94; 167 Ill. Dec. 853



October 17, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 18, 1991. Rehearing Denied March 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Frank Meekins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's first conviction in the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, for murder, aggravated kidnapping, and rape was reversed after rehearing, based on ineffective assistance of counsel. He was convicted after a second jury trial and again sentenced to death, and the sentence was stayed pending his mandatory direct appeal to the Illinois Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with capital murder, and his conviction was reversed based on the ineffective assistance of counsel. His conviction and sentence after a second trial was automatically appealed. In affirming both the conviction and sentence, the court ruled that the death penalty statute and the procedure for determining eligibility for the sentence were constitutional. The prosecutor's discretion in seeking the death penalty was proper, as it was exercised dependent upon whether the requisite elements for death sentencing existed, and further guided because it was made at the conclusion of the trial. Tactics used by counsel, such as the waiving of an opening statement and an admission of the horrendous nature of the crimes, were legitimate strategy, and not ineffective assistance. The issue of discrimination against black jurors being excluded was determined by considering whether a prima facie case was established by a pattern of strikes against blacks, a disproportionate use of peremptory challenges, or whether excluded blacks were a heterogeneous group sharing race as their only common characteristic, as well as the composition of the venire and the race of the parties.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and death sentence were affirmed, as the death penalty was not unconstitutional, and represented an individualized determination on the basis of the character of the individual and the circumstances of the crime.

People v. Jackson


No. 68012


Supreme Court of Illinois


145 Ill. 2d 43; 582 N.E.2d 125; 1991 Ill. LEXIS 83; 163 Ill. Dec. 859



September 26, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 2, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Joseph Urso, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted him for murder and imposed a capital sentence. On appeal, raised several contentions, including a defense of voluntary intoxication and prosecution's alleged purposeful racial discrimination in jury selection.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, attempted murder, armed robber, residential burglary, and home invasion. He was sentenced to death in connection with the murder charge, 60 years' imprisonment on the attempted murder, 30 years' imprisonment for armed robbery and home invasion, and 15 years' imprisonment for residential burglary. On appeal, he raised several arguments including a defense of voluntary intoxication and prosecution's purposeful racial discrimination in the selection of jury members. The court concluded that defendant's defense of voluntary intoxication was wholly without merit in view of the evidence of his state of mind that was presented in the form of his own statements and the testimony of others. Defendant had also failed to make the prima facie case of purposeful racial discrimination on the part of prosecution that was required under Batson in order to challenge prosecution's use of peremptory challenges, so his Batson argument was determined to lack merit. The court further determined that all other errors asserted by defendant were harmless and did not compel reversal. Accordingly, the trial court's judgment of conviction and sentences were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment of conviction and capital sentence were affirmed. Defendant failed to establish a valid defense of voluntary intoxication to capital murder charges. Further, he failed to make a prima facie showing of purposeful racial discrimination by prosecution in its selection of jurors.

316 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jones


No. 70352


Supreme Court of Illinois


144 Ill. 2d 242; 579 N.E.2d 829; 1991 Ill. LEXIS 71; 162 Ill. Dec. 15



September 19, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County, the Hon. William B. Starnes, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which denied his second petition for post-conviction relief on the grounds of the ineffective assistance of both his trial and appellate counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted, pursuant to a plea of guilty, of three murders and was sentenced to death for each murder following a sentencing hearing before a jury. On direct appeal, this court affirmed all three of defendant's convictions and two of the death sentences. The death sentence for the third murder conviction was vacated and the cause remanded for imposition of a sentence other than death. Defendant's new counsel filed a second petition for post-conviction relief, which was the subject of this appeal. Defendant appealed, and the court held that defendant was not deprived of the effective assistance of counsel at the plea proceedings or at the capital sentencing proceedings. Because defendant's trial counsel was not constitutionally ineffective, defendant was not prejudiced by his appellate counsel's failure to challenge the competency of trial counsel on direct appeal. Even if defendant's appellate counsel had raised the ineffective-assistance issue on direct appeal, this court would have rejected the claim, as the post-conviction court did. Neither attorney's actions rose to the level of incompetence and prejudice necessary for defendant's requested relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court denying the defendant's petition for post-conviction relief, finding that neither defendant's trial or appellate counsel's conduct arose to the level of incompetence and prejudice necessary to prove a claim for ineffective assistance of counsel.

 

317 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Beverly Bank v. Illinois DOT


No. 70105


Supreme Court of Illinois


144 Ill. 2d 210; 579 N.E.2d 815; 1991 Ill. LEXIS 74; 162 Ill. Dec. 1



September 19, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Richard L. Curry, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee landowner filed an application for an extension of a construction contract. Appellant Department of Transportation (DOT) denied the application based upon recently enacted flood control legislation, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 19, para. 18g (1989). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) held that the flood control legislation was unconstitutional. The DOT challenged the circuit court's order.


OVERVIEW: The flood control legislation, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 19, para. 18g, prohibited all new residential construction in a 100-year floodway. The landowner argued that § 18g was unconstitutional as it applied to her properties and that the court had to balance the individual hardships imposed on her against the benefit to be gained by the public. The DOT counter argued that the landowner's challenge was a facial attack on § 18g and that no balancing of interests was required. The court agreed with the DOT and held that the prohibition under § 18g was without exception and was applied in a completely nondiscriminatory manner. Further, the court found that § 18g was rationally related to several legitimate state interests and provided a reasonable basis for the prohibition of new residential construction in the 100-year floodway. The court found that in addition to the interest of reducing flood damage § 18g would: protect the health and welfare of those who would live in the new houses; reduce the expenditure of public funds; and limit the extent of emergency relief services required by the periodic inundation of flood waters.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that held that the flood control legislation was unconstitutional.

 

318 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Harris Trust & Sav. Bank v. Donovan


No. 71139


Supreme Court of Illinois


145 Ill. 2d 166; 582 N.E.2d 120; 1991 Ill. LEXIS 75; 163 Ill. Dec. 854



September 19, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 2, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Monica Reynolds, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant child challenged the decision of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed the decision of the trial court and found that appellee illegitimate child was an heir to the decedent father's estate.


OVERVIEW: The decedent father failed to mention his illegitimate child in either his will or the trusts he established in conjunction with his will. Instead, the decedent used the phrase "lawful blood children" in the trust documents and named only his legitimate children in his will. The appellate court, finding that the trust documents were ambiguous, remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings. The court noted that both the decedent's will and the trust documents had to be construed together in order to effectuate the overall intent of the decedent and that the same rules of construction applicable to the interpretation of the decedent's will applied to the interpretation of the trust documents. The court observed that, in Illinois, the word "lawful" under these circumstances meant "legitimate." The court found that the plain and ordinary meaning of the words in the trust documents was consistent with the will, that the illegitimate child was disinherited by necessary implication, and that the illegitimate child was excluded from taking under the decedent's trust.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed and the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Gosier


No. 69277


Supreme Court of Illinois


145 Ill. 2d 127; 582 N.E.2d 89; 1991 Ill. LEXIS 80; 163 Ill. Dec. 823



September 19, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 2, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County, the Hon. Robert J. Steigmann, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment entered in the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) for murder and aggravated criminal sexual assault and sought review of the death sentence imposed by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with committing two murders and aggravated criminal sexual assaults. During his trial, defendant pled guilty to all charges. The trial court sentenced defendant to death for the murders and two consecutive 60-year sentences for the aggravated criminal sexual assaults. Defendant contended that his guilty plea was not knowing and voluntary because the trial court failed to admonish him that he could plead guilty but mentally ill. Defendant further contended that the trial court improperly denied his request to withdraw his guilt plea and to substitute a plea of guilty but mentally ill. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions and sentences and set a date for the death sentence to be carried out. The court held that the trial court's admonishments were proper. Defendant's opening statement indicated that he planned to deny that he committed the charged offenses and not that he planned on alleging the affirmative defense of insanity. Because defendant failed to properly raise the insanity defense, the trial court did not err in its failure to admonish defendant that he could plead guilty but mentally ill.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's convictions of defendant for murder and aggravated criminal sexual assault and affirmed the sentences imposed by the trial court. The court set a date for defendant's death sentence to be carried out. Because defendant failed to properly raise an insanity defense, the trial court did not err in its failure to admonish defendant that he could plead guilty but mentally ill.

People v. Williams


No. 70427


Supreme Court of Illinois


143 Ill. 2d 477; 577 N.E.2d 762; 1991 Ill. LEXIS 54; 160 Ill. Dec. 437



August 14, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Stephenson County, the Hon. Lawrence A. Smith, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought direct review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Stephenson County (Illinois), which declared § 110 -- 6.2(b) of the Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 110--6.2(b) (1989), concerning post-conviction detention, to be unconstitutional. Defendant, convicted of making unlawful deliveries of a controlled substance, remained free on bond pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: Following defendant's conviction and release on bond pending appeal, the state contended that § 110 -- 6.2(b) was constitutional because the legislature considered the issue of prison overcrowding when it passed the provision into law and because it did not infringe upon a defendant's right to appeal. The circuit court sua sponte declared the statute unconstitutional on grounds that it was not practical to house all those individuals appealing orders of conviction and sentences, and the statute violated due process. On appeal, the court affirmed, ruling that the statute was unconstitutional because there was a conflict between the requirements of the statute and the terms of Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 609(b), 134 Ill. 2d R. 609(b). In so holding, the court reasoned that the word "shall" as used in the statute to describe the court's duty with regard to bond of a person found guilty imposed a mandatory requirement upon the judiciary that irreconcilably conflicted with the permissive language contained in Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 609(b), which provided that persons "may" be admitted to bail at the discretion of a judge of the trial or reviewing court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment declaring unconstitutional the provision of the Code of Criminal Procedure entitled "Post-conviction Detention."

People v. Pecoraro


No. 67289


Supreme Court of Illinois


144 Ill. 2d 1; 578 N.E.2d 942; 1991 Ill. LEXIS 44; 161 Ill. Dec. 296



June 4, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 30, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Kenneth L. Gillis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of murder and sentenced to death following a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). The execution was stayed pending direct review pursuant to Ill. Const. art. VI, § 4(b) and 134 Ill. 2d R. 603, 609(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant agreed to answer questions posed by a police officer en route to the police station. The officer learned whom defendant killed and when the incident occurred. Defendant later refused to sign a written statement of his confession after initially agreeing to do so. Subsequent to his confession, he was arrested and charged with two counts of murder and one count of armed violence. The court affirmed the convictions, finding that the confession was corroborated by physical evidence of the corpus delicti, and by the testimony of the police officers. The trial court properly admitted into evidence defendant's written confession, which was found to have been made voluntarily and knowingly. The jury weighed all the evidence and found defendant guilty of murder. Defendant failed to establish that his attorney's representation was deficient and that he suffered substantial prejudice as a result of these deficiencies. Also, the record did not reflect that defendant requested other counsel to represent him. The prosecution's closing argument was not prejudicial, since the defendant's version of the occurrence differed considerably from that given by witnesses for the prosecution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence of death.

324 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gean


No. 70660


Supreme Court of Illinois


143 Ill. 2d 281; 573 N.E.2d 818; 1991 Ill. LEXIS 31; 158 Ill. Dec. 5



May 20, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 6, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jasper County, the Hon. James Harvey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Jasper County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss six counts of possession of salvage certificates without authority and three counts of possession of certificates of title without complete assignment on the basis that the penalty provision for the charges, Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-104(b)(1) (1987), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court granted defendant's motion to dismiss on the basis that § 4-104(b)(1) was unconstitutional because it created a felony offense with felony penalties without requiring any unlawful purpose, knowledge, or intent and thus violated his due process rights. On appeal, the court reversed, and held that § 4-104(b)(1) was not unconstitutional because it did not prescribe felony penalties for absolute liability offenses. The court found that due to the lack of a clear legislative intent and the severe penalties applicable to violators of the two charges, under para. 4--104(a)(1) and para. 4- 104(a)(2), were not absolute liability offenses, and that, according to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 4-3(b) (1987), when a statute neither prescribed a particular mental state nor created an absolute liability offense, then either intent, knowledge, or recklessness applied. The court ruled that knowledge was the appropriate mental element for the state to prove that defendant possessed the certificates knowing that he did not have authority or knowing it was without complete assignment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of charges against defendant for possession of salvage certificates without authority and possession of certificates of title without complete assignment on the basis that the penalty provision for the charges was unconstitutional.

People v. Nitz


No. 67911


Supreme Court of Illinois


143 Ill. 2d 82; 572 N.E.2d 895; 1991 Ill. LEXIS 23; 157 Ill. Dec. 431



March 28, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 3, 1991.
Writ of certiorari denied Nitz v. Illinois, 502 U.S. 927, 112 S. Ct. 344, 116 L. Ed. 2d 283, 1991 U.S. LEXIS 6204 (1991)
Related proceeding at People v. Nitz, 242 Ill. App. 3d 209, 610 N.E.2d 1289, 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 314, 183 Ill. Dec. 45 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., 1993)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Williamson County, the Hon. Donald Lowery, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Williamson County (Illinois) convicted defendant of murder. Defendant waived his right to a jury for the sentencing phase of the proceedings and was sentenced to death. The sentence was stayed pending the direct appeal to the court. While his conviction was awaiting review, defendant filed a post-sentencing motion in the circuit court that was denied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. On appeal, the court affirmed. Defendant argued that the state did not prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that the state presented sufficient evidence to support the verdict. Defendant argued that the state's repeated use of his post-arrest silence during its case in chief, on cross-examination of defendant, and during rebuttal violated the principle that a defendant's post-arrest silence will not be used to discredit an exculpatory story offered at trial. Defendant argued ineffective assistance of counsel on several issues. The court held that defendant was not sufficiently prejudiced by any actions or inactions by his counsel to support a claim of ineffective assistance of counsel. The court reaffirmed its prior holdings that the death penalty statute was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of murder and death sentence.

 

327 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Fabing


No. 70082


Supreme Court of Illinois


143 Ill. 2d 48; 570 N.E.2d 329; 1991 Ill. LEXIS 17; 155 Ill. Dec. 816



March 21, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Ann Houser, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Reversed; Cause Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed defendant's conviction on four counts of violating the Illinois Dangerous Animals Act (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 8, para. 240 et seq. (1987) on the grounds that the act was unconstitutionally vague on its face.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of unlawful possession of life-threatening reptiles in violation of the act. He had a 4-foot alligator, a 7-foot boa constrictor, and two 15-foot pythons. The appellate court reversed, holding that the act was unconstitutionally vague on its face. On appeal by the state, the court reversed. Although the act did not contain any criteria for determining which reptiles were life-threatening, the court held that the ambiguity did not render the act unconstitutional on its face. The term "life-threatening" was sufficiently clear to establish a standard of conduct. The court disagreed with defendant that the reptiles' individual temperaments should be considered. The determination of whether it was reasonably possible that an animal would attack humans had to be made on a species-wide basis. The court held that the trial testimony showed that the pythons were life-threatening. However, the act was too ambiguous to permit conviction for possession of the seven-foot boa constrictor. The act was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to possession of the alligator because the evidence showed that alligators as a species were life-threatening.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision reversing defendant's conviction for violating an act prohibiting the ownership or possession of dangerous animals and remanded for consideration of defendant's remaining claims.

People v. Steidl

Supreme Court of Illinois


142 Ill. 2d 204; 568 N.E.2d 837; 1991 Ill. LEXIS 3; 154 Ill. Dec. 616



January 24, 1991, Filed

DISPOSITION: No. 65714 -- Affirmed. No. 70320 -- Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder by the Circuit Court of Edgar County (Illinois). While the original conviction was awaiting review, defendant filed a post-judgment petition, attacking his conviction and his death sentence. The circuit court denied the petition and defendant appealed. By order, the appeal of the post-judgment petition was consolidated with the pending direct appeal of defendant's conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a codefendant were indicted for murder. Defendant's motions for a change of venue and to sever his case were granted. The same jury that convicted defendant found that he was eligible for the death penalty and further found that there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude a sentence of death. Finally, because the state offered plausible explanations for all evidentiary inconsistencies and shortcomings, and because the jury was made aware of such infirmities, the court held that sufficient evidence was produced for a jury to hold defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction and sentence of death. The court also affirmed the circuit court's denial of defendant's petition for a new trial and directed the clerk of the court to enter an order setting the date on which the sentence of death was to be carried out.

DOT v. First Galesburg Nat'l Bank & Trust Co.


No. 69423


Supreme Court of Illinois


141 Ill. 2d 462; 566 N.E.2d 254; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 155; 152 Ill. Dec. 567



December 20, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 4, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Warren County, the Hon. Scott I. Klukos, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate Court Reversed; Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff department of transportation challenged the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), which reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had denied defendant landowners' motion to dismiss the department's eminent domain proceeding. The appellate court found that the department did not establish, by competent evidence, a prima facie right to take a fee simple interest in land using a quick-take procedure.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court approved the department's complaint for condemnation under the department's power of eminent domain and granted the department fee simple title to the existing Route 34 right-of-way and the fee simple title to strips of land adjacent to Route 34 so the highway could be widened. Defendants argued and the appellate court agreed that the department failed to prove a prima facie case giving it the right to obtain the underlying fee to Route 34 because no evidence was produced which showed that it was necessary to acquire the fee interest to that portion of the highway which had already been dedicated. On further appeal, the court reversed and reinstated the trial court's decision and held that the department satisfied its prima facie burden of proof when it introduced into evidence Ill. Rev. Stat. 1987, ch. 121, par. 4 -- 501, which specifically authorized the department to acquire the fee simple title to the disputed land. Because the legislature determined that the department could acquire the fee simple absolute, the court held that there was no showing the department manifestly abused its authority or its discretion by acquiring the underlying fee to Route 34.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court, denied defendant bank's petition for cross-relief, and affirmed the decision of the circuit court that had held that the department had made a prima facie showing of the necessity to take title to the disputed land in fee simple.

 

331 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Harlan v. Sweet


No. 69305


Supreme Court of Illinois


139 Ill. 2d 390; 564 N.E.2d 1192; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 128; 151 Ill. Dec. 530



November 30, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. Simon L. Friedman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county treasurers challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which held that the treasurers were not entitled to additional compensation during their term of office in the treasurers' action against defendant state director of revenue.


OVERVIEW: The county treasurers brought an action against the revenue director to compel him to pay a salary increase as mandated by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 36, para. 4.6 (1987). The law went into effect two days after the treasurers' election. The trial court found for the revenue director, holding that Ill. Const. art. VII, § 9(b) (1970) barred a mid-term increase in salary. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that although the statute used the term "stipend" and the constitutional provisions spoke only of "salaries," there was no difference between the two. The statute would have served to increase the treasurers' salaries during their elected terms of office, which the constitution forbade. The court also did not accept the treasurers' allegations that the raise was justified because additional duties were added to the treasurers' offices. No evidence was offered in support of the argument, and regardless, such a raise was still unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that the treasurers were not entitled to additional compensation in the middle of their term of office in their action against the state revenue director.

 

332 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


County of Bureau v. Thompson


No. 69130


Supreme Court of Illinois


139 Ill. 2d 323; 564 N.E.2d 1170; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 133; 151 Ill. Dec. 508



November 30, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Bureau County, the Hon. C. Howard Wampler, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the governor, state agencies, and state officials, appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Bureau County (Illinois), which held that § 4 of the Illinois and Mississippi Canal State Park Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 105, para. 482d (1987), violated Ill. Const. art. I, § 2; art. IV, § 13 (1970). The action by plaintiff local government entities sought relief from the obligation to maintain bridges under the Act.


OVERVIEW: When the state accepted title to the canal from the United States and created a park, it assumed responsibility for the bridges that connected with state highways and imposed responsibility for the remaining bridges on the local governments that were responsible for maintaining the roads that connected with those bridges. The local governments claimed that § 4 of the Act was unconstitutional. The circuit court ruled in favor of the local governments, and the court reversed on appeal. There was no equal protection violation because, while the local governments identified a class to which they alone belonged, there was a rational basis for the classification. As a result of the United States' assumption of bridge maintenance, plaintiffs for many years were not responsible for maintaining the bridges. There were no other governments situated similarly because no other governments had the United States unburden them of their bridge maintenance duties but later withdraw the benefit. Section 4 was a special and local law, not a general law, but it was constitutional where it did not have the effect of according a special privilege to some local governments that it denied to plaintiffs.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that held that a section of the Act that required the local governments to maintain bridges in the park was unconstitutional.

 

333 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Henderson


No. 65457


Supreme Court of Illinois


142 Ill. 2d 258; 568 N.E.2d 1234; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 138; 154 Ill. Dec. 785



November 30, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 1, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Richard E. Neville, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed, As Modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered judgment of his conviction for murder and other crimes and which sentenced defendant to imprisonment and, after a death penalty hearing before the trial judge, found defendant to be eligible for the death penalty and so sentenced defendant to death for the murder conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and other crimes. After a death penalty hearing before the trial judge, defendant was found eligible for the death penalty because he was 18 at the time of the murder and had committed the murder during the course of another felony. Defendant's post-trial motions were denied and his execution was stayed pending direct review by the court. The court affirmed. The court held that the trial court's finding that defendant failed to establish a prima facie case for his claim that the prosecution purposefully discriminated against black venire members was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. The court held that defendant's constitutional rights were not violated even though he was absent from the in-chambers voir dire of three venire members because the jury which tried defendant appeared to be impartial. The court held that defendant's waiver of his right to a jury during his death penalty sentencing hearing was knowing and intelligent because defendant consulted with his attorney, he said that he understood the consequences of the waiver, and his attorney said that he thought that defendant's decision was made knowingly and intelligently.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder and other crimes and his sentences of imprisonment and death because the finding that there was no purposeful racial discrimination by the prosecution during voir dire was not against the manifest weight of the evidence, the jury which tried him appeared to be impartial, and defendant knowingly and intelligently waived his right to a jury during his death penalty sentencing hearing.

 

334 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Rock v. Burris


No. 69821


Supreme Court of Illinois


139 Ill. 2d 494; 564 N.E.2d 1240; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 140; 151 Ill. Dec. 578



November 30, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original petition for writ of mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, members of the eighty-sixth general assembly, sought a writ of mandamus ordering defendants, state comptroller and state treasurer, to issue warrants for and dispense funds pursuant to their recent pay raise legislation, Public Act 86--27. Plaintiffs also sought that the court declare the legislation constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Public Act 86--27 raised the amounts that were paid annually for various leadership positions in the General Assembly. The increase was to be applied retrospectively to plaintiffs' current terms. Plaintiffs contended that the additional amounts paid to institutional officers of the General Assembly were not salary and could be increased without constitutional limitation. The court held that the legislation violated the provision in Ill. Const. art. IV, § 11, which prohibited a change in a legislator's salary during the term for which he was elected. The court held that the word "salary" encompassed all forms of compensation paid to public officials for performing the duties of office. The fact that institutional officers in the General Assembly were paid an additional amount above the base amount paid to all other legislators made it no less a salary. Though the court agreed with plaintiffs that members of the General Assembly could receive greater compensation because of additional duties, the pay increase was an additional remuneration for the additional duties assigned to legislators and was therefore, subject to the restrictions contained in art. IV, § 11.


OUTCOME: The court denied plaintiffs' petition for a writ of mandamus and dismissed the action.

The court held that under the circumstances, it could not accept the contentions of defendants and the holding of the trial court that the disputed system did not violate the one person, one vote constitutionally mandated by the Supreme Court. Therefore, the court reversed the decision of the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the circuit court which granted summary judgment for defendants and denied plaintiffs' motion to dismiss in an action concerning the constitutionality of the Chicago School Reform Act. People v. Pitsonbarger


No. 67879


Supreme Court of Illinois


142 Ill. 2d 353; 568 N.E.2d 783; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 139; 154 Ill. Dec. 562



November 30, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of Rehearing April 1, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County, the Hon. Calvin R. Stone, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed in Part and Vacated in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois) of two counts of intentional murder and four counts of felony murder based on the felonies of burglary and home invasion with respect to the murder of a husband and wife. In a bifurcated trial the jury sentenced defendant to death. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant broke into the victim's home and murdered the victims. Defendant stole the victims' truck when he left the scene and went on a two-state crime spree. Defendant was convicted by the trial judge of two counts of intentional murder and four counts of felony murder based on the burglary and home invasion with respect to each victim. The jury determined that defendant was eligible for the death penalty and, and considered the mitigating and aggravating evidence and sentenced defendant to death. On appeal, the court held that (1) the felony murder convictions were vacated because defendant could not be convicted of more than one murder from the same physical act, (2) prospective jurors were properly excused because their views on the death penalty would substantially impair the performance of their duties, (3) defendant's alcoholism, emotional problems, and disturbed childhood were relevant but did not require that the death sentence be reduced to imprisonment, and (4) the jury's weighing of the aggravating and mitigating factors did not assign the burden of proof to defendant or state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for intentional murder and sentence of death. The court vacated defendant's felony murder convictions.

People v. Holveck


Nos. 67290, 67443 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


141 Ill. 2d 84; 565 N.E.2d 919; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 127; 152 Ill. Dec. 237



November 21, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 4, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Nicholas Zagone and the Hon. Richard A. Kavitt, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with and found guilty of deviate sexual assault, aggravated indecent liberties with a child, and unlawful restraint. He filed a motion to quash his arrest and to suppress evidence arising from two separate incidents of sexual assault on minors, which was denied by the trial court. The Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) reversed the judgment and remanded the case for a new trial, and the state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state offered testimony that the defendant was given Miranda warnings before questioning, and approximately 10 minutes later, had made an incriminating statement regarding an assault of a minor boy. Based on that testimony, the detective considered there was probable cause to arrest the defendant. The state contended that after the defendant was given his Miranda warnings a second time, he made incriminating statements concerning another sexual attack on minors. The state contended that the subsequent statement given by the defendant was voluntary when, after being given Miranda warnings and without being subjected to the procedures of arrest, the defendant made incriminating statements. The court found that the defendant was arrested without probable cause upon the stopping of his car and the attendant events. The evidence showed that the officer told the defendant that he would have to go to the station to retrieve his license; and he felt compelled to go. He was not told that he was under arrest. The court further concluded that the giving of Miranda warnings alone was not sufficient to purge the taint of an illegal arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment that the defendant was arrested without probable cause and was seized in violation of rights under the U.S. Const. amend. IV.

People v. Christy

Supreme Court of Illinois


139 Ill. 2d 172; 564 N.E.2d 770; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 125; 151 Ill. Dec. 315

The supreme court held that the penalties for aggravated kidnapping and armed violence were unconstitutionally disproportionate because each offense required proof of the same elements, yet armed violence was punished more severely than aggravated kidnapping.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the intermediate appellate court vacating defendant's conviction and sentence for armed violence, reducing defendant's sentence for kidnapping, and remanding for sentencing on the offense of aggravated kidnapping.

Williams v. Illinois State Scholarship Com.


No. 68869


Supreme Court of Illinois


139 Ill. 2d 24; 563 N.E.2d 465; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 117; 150 Ill. Dec. 578



October 18, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 14, 1990. Rehearing Denied November 30, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County, the Hon. Jonathan Isbell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Illinois State Scholarship Commission sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) granting summary judgment to appellee loan defaultees on their action challenging appellants' collection of loans exclusively from one county and requirement that borrowers execute contracts containing venue waiver clauses. Appellees also asserted Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 30--15.12 (1988) was unconstitutional.

341 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Taylor


No. 69599


Supreme Court of Illinois


138 Ill. 2d 204; 561 N.E.2d 667; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 101; 149 Ill. Dec. 297



September 26, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County, the Hon. David Watt, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with unlawful possession of protected animals, operating as a taxidermist without a valid license, and possession of mammal parts not bearing coded origin tags. The Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois) found that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 61, para. 3.21 (1987) was unconstitutionally vague, and the state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found probable cause to believe that defendant had committed the offenses with which he was charged, but determined that para. 3.21 was unconstitutionally vague because the term "engaging in the business of taxidermy" was capable of several meaning. The trial court dismissed all three counts of the information, noting that the unlawful possession of protected animals offense alleged in count I of the information was predicated on a violation of para. 3.21, and that the remaining two counts also alleged a violation of that provision. The state appealed. In reversing the trial court, the court observed that in the absence of a statutory definition indicating a different legislative intention, the court would assume that statutory words had their ordinary and popularly understood meanings. To sustain a facial challenge the challenger had to demonstrate that the law was impermissibly vague in all of its applications. The court then concluded that the statute provided an individual with ample notice that any conduct which fell within the range of activity under the commonly understood meaning of taxidermy must be performed pursuant to the dictates of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, holding that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.

Tiller v. Klincar


No. 68877


Supreme Court of Illinois


138 Ill. 2d 1; 561 N.E.2d 576; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 88; 149 Ill. Dec. 206



September 19, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Tiller v. Klincar, 498 U.S. 1031, 111 S. Ct. 688, 112 L. Ed. 2d 679, 1991 U.S. LEXIS 283 (1991)
Remanded by Tiller v. Ill. Prisoner Review Bd., 2013 IL App (5th) 120389-U, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 965 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Johnson County, the Hon. James Williamson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, members of the Illinois Prisoner Review Board, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Johnson County (Illinois), which granted appellee inmate a writ of mandamus; found Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1003-3-5(f) (1988 Supp.), a statutory amendment eliminating annual parole hearings, to be unconstitutional as applied to the inmate; and ordered the board to grant the inmate a new parole hearing within 60 days.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of murder and became eligible for parole. For four years, the inmate received annual parole hearings; however, after an amendment to para. 1003-3-5(f), the board scheduled the next parole hearing date in three years, based upon a finding that it was not reasonable to expect that the inmate would be granted parole at an earlier date. The court affirmed the finding of unconstitutionality of the amended statute because of its ex post facto application. The court found that the inmate suffered a disadvantage by the termination of annual parole hearings. Moreover, the fact that the amended statute required special findings and that Ill. Admin. Code tit. 20, § 1610.100(a)(2) (1985) permitted an interim hearing did not sustain application of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1003-3-5(f) (1988 Supp.) The court reversed the granting of a new parole hearing because the board's reason satisfied the inmate's due process rights. The court found the reason for denial of parole was sufficient because the board specifically considered the inmate's conduct and not merely the statutory offense for which he was convicted. Thus, an immediate parole hearing was not required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the judgment of mandamus finding the statutory amendment governing parole hearings to be unconstitutional. The court reversed that portion ordering a new parole hearing for the inmate.

 

343 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Chicago Bar Ass'n v. Illinois State Bd. of Elections


Docket No. 69823


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


1990 Ill. LEXIS 84



August 22, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Original Opinion of July 3, 1990, Reported at 1990 Ill. LEXIS 73 



DISPOSITION: Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner bar association (bar) sought a writ of mandamus or a writ of prohibition asking the court to declare null and void the results of an election with respect to certain circuit judges on the grounds that the elections were in violation of Public Act 86-786 (amendatory Act).


OVERVIEW: The amendatory Act, among other things, divided the First Judicial District into five subdistricts and provided that certain circuit court vacancies be filled by appointment. The bar claimed that certain vacancies should not have been placed on the ballot. The court refused to issue the writ, holding that the amendatory Act's subdivision of the First Judicial District for purposes of electing appellate judges was unconstitutional. Although the Illinois constitution provided for subdivision of circuit courts and was silent as to subdivision of appellate courts, the court found that the history of the constitution's judicial article indicated that the First Judicial District was to remain a single, undivided district for the selection of both supreme and appellate judges. The provisions of the amendatory Act with respect to the First Judicial District as to both appellate and circuit court judges were a result of compromise and, thus, intertwined so that the provisions could not be severed. The court held that the challenged elections were proper, except for that of an additional circuit court judgeship created by the amendatory Act, which was held null and void.


OUTCOME: The court denied the bar's petition for writ of mandamus.

Batteast v. Wyeth Laboratories, Inc.


No. 67590


Supreme Court of Illinois


137 Ill. 2d 175; 560 N.E.2d 315; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 72; 148 Ill. Dec. 13; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P12,510



July 3, 1990, Filed
