CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant drug manufacturer challenged an order of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) that affirmed an award of compensatory and punitive damages in favor of appellee minor, including an award of medical expenses in favor of the minor's parents, in a product liability action based on strict liability, negligence, and willful and wanton misconduct. The drug manufacturer raised several issues on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The minor suffered brain damage and epilepsy from an overdose of theophylline. In a separate action filed against his physicians and the hospital, the parties reached settlement agreements prior to a jury verdict. The drug manufacturer contended that the settlements constituted a release that discharged all remaining defendants. In addition, the drug manufacturer charged that there was no evidence of proximate cause, the damages awarded were excessive, and there were several grounds for reversible error. The court held that (1) it was clear the settlement agreement with one of the physicians was intended to be a covenant not to sue and did not release other tortfeasors, (2) the drug manufacturer was improperly denied cross-examination of the other physician whose testimony on proximate cause was essential to the case, and he may have been potentially biased by the terms of his settlement agreement, (3) the issue of proximate cause based on the drug manufacturer's failure to warn was properly submitted to the jury, and (4) the drug manufacturer's failure to comply with FDA regulations was improperly submitted and considered by the jury in reference to punitive damages.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the appellate court and trial court were reversed and the cause was remanded for a new trial.

People ex rel. Chicago Bar Ass'n v. State Bd. of Elections


No. 69823


Supreme Court of Illinois


136 Ill. 2d 513; 558 N.E.2d 89; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 73; 146 Ill. Dec. 126



July 3, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of Rehearing August 22, 1990, Reported at 1990 Ill. LEXIS 84.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original petition for writ of mandamus, prohibition or supervisory order.



DISPOSITION: Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the Chicago Bar Association (CBA), petitioned for a writ of mandamus regarding the election of respondent judicial candidates to five resident circuit court judge vacancies. The CBA sought to enjoin the primary election results with respect to the existing vacancies and to fill said vacancies for terms to expire concurrently with the upcoming general election, pursuant to Public Act of Sept. 6, 1989, 86--786, §§ 1-3.


OVERVIEW: Public Act of Sept. 6, 1989 (Act), 86--786, §§ 1-3, amended prior law by creating two appellate judgeships in the Third Judicial District, dividing the First Judicial District for the election of some appellate judges, and dividing the Cook County circuit for the election of resident circuit judges. The court held that the provisions of the Act that pertained to the First Judicial District of the appellate court were unconstitutional. Applicable legislative history indicated that Cook County was to remain a single, undivided district for the selection of both supreme and appellate judges so that inadequate representation of Republicans and minorities in the First Judicial District appellate and circuit courts could be rectified. The invalid First Judicial District provisions were therefore not severable from the provisions pertaining to the Cook County circuit court. The Act's provisions regarding the Third Judicial District were severable and therefore valid because they were enacted to alleviate heavy caseload problems and were entirely unrelated to the First Judicial District provisions.


OUTCOME: The CBA's petition for a writ of mandamus was denied because the legislative provisions upon which the petition was based were declared unconstitutional. The court declined to enjoin the judicial candidates' elections and begin appointing judges to fill the resident circuit court vacancies based upon the unconstitutional statute relied upon by the CBA.

347 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Hayes v. Mercy Hosp. & Medical Ctr.


Nos. 68500, 68501 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


136 Ill. 2d 450; 557 N.E.2d 873; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 80; 145 Ill. Dec. 894; 88 A.L.R.4th 321



July 3, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Dean J. Sodaro, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Third-party plaintiff city and trucking company brought a third-party complaint for contribution against third-party defendant physician that alleged negligence in his treatment of the deceased plaintiff in an underlying tort action. The city and trucking company sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals for the First District (Illinois) that affirmed the trial court's grant of the physician's motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The physician argued that the contribution action was barred by the statute of repose in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13-212(a) because it was filed more than four years after the underlying negligent acts occurred. The city and trucking company argued that the statute of repose did not apply to contribution actions and that a contribution claim could be commenced any time during the pendency of the underlying case. The court held that the contribution action against the physician was time-barred by the medical malpractice statute of repose. An "action for damages" under the medical malpractice statute of repose was not limited to actions at law. The statute encompassed contribution actions against physicians for patient care because the basis for contribution rested on the contributor's liability in tort to the injured party, regardless of whether that theory of liability was asserted by the injured party. In addition, the insurer was exposed to the same liability in contribution as it had in a direct suit. The procedural requirement that contribution actions be brought within the pendency of an underlying suit did not mean that a suit brought within that period was timely.


OUTCOME: The judgment that upheld the order granting the physician's motion to dismiss the contribution action brought against him by the city and trucking company was affirmed. The contribution action was untimely because it was not filed within four-years of the time that the alleged negligent acts took place as required by the medical malpractice statute of repose.

Mutual Life Ins. Co. v. Washburn


No. 68884


Supreme Court of Illinois


137 Ill. 2d 312; 561 N.E.2d 29; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 77; 148 Ill. Dec. 723



July 3, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 1, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. C. Joseph Cavanagh, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state department of insurance and director of insurance, challenged the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (New York), which reversed the circuit court's grant of summary judgment for the department and held that a retaliatory tax assessment was valid. Appellee insurance company had filed an action challenging the assessment of a retaliatory tax under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 73, para. 1056 (1987).


OVERVIEW: Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 73, para. 1021 (1987) imposed a two percent tax of net taxable premium on foreign insurers, which were potentially subject under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 73, § 444, para. 1056 (1987) to a retaliatory tax. The company was organized in New York, which imposed a premium tax on all insurers of one percent on gross premiums and a "franchise" tax. The department assessed a net retaliatory tax based on the total New York tax the company would have had to pay if it were a foreign insurer in New York. The company sought a declaration that the tax was unwarranted. On appeal, the court reversed the appellate court's judgment, held that the retaliatory tax was authorized under § 444, and found that: (1) the department was not required to show, as a predicate, that New York taxes paid by Illinois insurers were "invariably, or even generally" more onerous than Illinois tax on New York insurers; (2) it was required to examine the Illinois business experience of each New York insurer and apply New York's tax scheme when assessing a retaliatory tax; and (3) the retaliatory tax was rationally related to deterring other states from enacting discriminatory taxes on Illinois insurers.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and affirmed the circuit court's judgment granting summary judgment in favor of the department and the director and holding that the retaliatory tax assessment was valid, in the company's action challenging the retaliatory tax assessment.

People v. Murray


No. 69335


Supreme Court of Illinois


137 Ill. 2d 382; 560 N.E.2d 309; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 65; 148 Ill. Dec. 7



May 30, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 14, 1990. Rehearing Denied October 1, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Matthew J. Moran, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the judgment of the Illinois Appellate Court for the First District that reversed defendant's conviction for unlawful use of a weapon by a felon upon ruling that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence that a gun was found in his parked car after police approached him and asked for identification.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with unlawful use of a weapon by a felon. At the hearing on his motion to suppress, evidence was presented that defendant was slumped over the steering wheel of his parked car when police approached, believing him to be sleeping or in distress. After knocking on the window, the officers asked for his license. The officers testified that when defendant exited the vehicle, a gun could be seen in plain view through the open door. Defendant disputed this and testified that his door was closed and the gun found during a nonconsensual search. The motion was denied and he was convicted, but the appellate court reversed, ruling that defendant was unlawfully seized in violation of the Fourth Amendment and the gun should have been suppressed. On further appeal, the supreme court ruled that the trial court's findings that defendant had not been seized and the officers were performing a community caretaking function were not manifestly erroneous. The mere approaching and questioning of defendant did not constitute a seizure, but was a consensual encounter.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed and the trial court's denial of the suppression motion was affirmed.

People v. West


No. 65382


Supreme Court of Illinois


137 Ill. 2d 558; 560 N.E.2d 594; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 67; 148 Ill. Dec. 196



May 30, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 1, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Francis Mahon, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After new trial, defendant was again found guilty of murder by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). The trial court sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed, and the death sentence was stayed pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of murder of a three-month old infant. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that defendant's statements were voluntary and that the trial court's finding thereon was not contrary to the manifest weight of the evidence. The court found that the extent and nature of the infant's injuries, as well as defendant's own statement and testimony from the infant's mother, were sufficient to find defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court opined that defendant was not denied assistance of counsel by the trial court's refusal to allow a continuance once defendant's retained counsel entered his appearance. The trial court properly admitted the testimony of an examining psychiatrist at the sentencing hearing because defense counsel requested both psychiatric examinations and defense counsel's representations during opening statement warranted the admission of the testimony in rebuttal. The prosecutor's statement in closing argument that defendant had raped a girl for whose murder he had been previously convicted was not improper given the evidence of rape. Finally, the court concluded that the state's death penalty statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People ex rel. Baricevic v. Wharton


No. 69245


Supreme Court of Illinois


136 Ill. 2d 423; 556 N.E.2d 253; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 69; 144 Ill. Dec. 786



May 30, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action for supervisory order.



DISPOSITION: Supervisory order entered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state filed a motion for a supervisory order to transfer six criminal cases of respondent trial judge to a different judge pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 114-5(c) (1987).


OVERVIEW: The state filed a motion for a supervisory order directing the trial judge to grant its Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 114--5(c) (1987) motions. The court denied the motion for a supervisory order, but did enter a supervisory order directing that the § 114--5(c) motions be transferred to another judge for a hearing. The court found that there was evidence in the record that suggested that the state filed the § 114 -- 5(c) motions in the six criminal proceedings before the trial judge in an attempt to coerce the chief judge of the circuit court to reassign the trial judge from the felony division of the circuit court to the juvenile division. The court also found that the state's blanket use of substitution motions in all felony proceedings before the trial judge, when viewed in conjunction with its earlier attempts at having the trial judge reassigned, posed a substantial threat to the dignity and independence of the judiciary. The court determined that although trial judges could not assess the allegations of prejudice in § 114--5(c), the trial judges could where there was prima facie evidence of unconstitutional conduct.


OUTCOME: The court denied the state's motion for a supervisory order directing the judge to transfer the six criminal cases to another judge. But the court entered a supervisory order directing that the chief judge of the circuit assign a another judge to conduct a hearing to allow the state to explain its basis for its claims of prejudice.

Davis v. Chicago Housing Authority


No. 68104


Supreme Court of Illinois


136 Ill. 2d 296; 555 N.E.2d 343; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 54; 144 Ill. Dec. 224



May 23, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Myron T. Gomberg, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, minor's mother, appealed an order from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed the trial court's holding that § 3-106 of the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act (Tort Immunity Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 1-101 et seq. (1985) did not apply to defendant municipal corporation.


OVERVIEW: A minor was injured while playing in a playground, which was owned, operated, maintained, and controlled by the municipal corporation. The playground was for the exclusive use of the municipal corporation's tenants, residents, and their guests. Subsequently, the minor's mother filed suit, alleging that the municipal corporation was careless and negligent in the maintenance and operation of the playground. The trial court granted the municipal corporation's motion to certify the question of whether the Tort Immunity Act was applicable to the municipal corporation, and the appellate court granted the municipal corporation's leave for appeal. Thereafter, the appellate court reversed the trial court's order and held that the Tort Immunity Act applied to the municipal corporation. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the powers conferred on the municipal corporation were public objects and governmental functions essential to the public interests. Thus, there was no question that the providing of a playground was a governmental activity. In addition, the court did not find any injury or wrong to be redressed under Ill. Const. art. I, § 12.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's order, holding that the Tort Immunity Act applied to the municipal corporation in a negligence action.

People v. Capitol News, Inc.


Nos. 67480, 67481, 67482, 67483 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


137 Ill. 2d 162; 560 N.E.2d 303; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 52; 148 Ill. Dec. 1; 13 A.L.R.5th 1029



May 23, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing October 1, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Circuit Court of McLean County, the Hon. Joseph P. Kelly, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed; causes remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In this consolidated case, the state appealed judgments of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which dismissed the indictments against defendants because of its ruling that the obscenity statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20 (1987), under which they were charged, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with the sale or delivery of materials in violation of the obscenity statute. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss because it held that the affirmative defense exempting dissemination to scientific institutions, established by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20(f)(2) (1987), was unconstitutionally vague. The trial court rejected defendants' argument that the indictments were duplicitous. The state appealed the dismissal of the indictments. The court reversed the judgments. Defendants lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the affirmative defense portion of the statute as there was no evidence that they intended to rely on that defense at trial. Because no justiciable controversy was raised, the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. The court did address the issue of constitutionality and concluded that the statute was constitutional. It found that the scientific exemption was not overly vague. The court also considered the indictments void for duplicity because they charged sale or delivery, which were alternate and disparate acts, the performance of either of which constituted an offense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgments dismissing defendants' indictments because the obscenity statute was unconstitutional and remanded the causes to the trial court. The court also found that the indictments were void for duplicity.

Supreme Court of Illinois

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's murder conviction and death penalty sentence were on direct appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted as the killer in a murder-for-hire scheme. He was sentenced to death under after the jury determined that there were two aggravating factors and no mitigating factors to support imposition of the sentence. The court held that: (1) the trial court's use of in camera interviews of potential jurors without defendant's waiver of his presence during those interviews was improper, (2) the interviews did not constitute plain error because the procedure had not affected the impartiality of the jury, (3) the trial court's in camera inspection of the privileged mental health records of one witness with disclosure of material information to defendant was the proper procedure and did not deny defendant his Sixth Amendment right of confrontation, (4) the failure to admonish prior to recess between guilt and penalty stages was not error in light of defendant's failure to show any prejudice, (5) the jury was properly allowed to consider as aggravating factors that the murder was for pecuniary gain and that it was committed during an armed robbery, and (6) the jury was not precluded from considering defendant's background as mitigation.

355 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Morris


No. 68646


Supreme Court of Illinois


135 Ill. 2d 540; 554 N.E.2d 150; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 45; 143 Ill. Dec. 215



April 18, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of La Salle County, the Hon. Fred Wagner, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois) reversed a trial court ruling, which convicted defendant on three counts of criminal sexual abuse in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12 --15(a)(1) (1984). The appellate court reversed on statute of limitations grounds. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with four counts of sexual misconduct, all of which stemmed from the same incident on the same date. The three charges at issue were not added to the indictment until after the expiration of the three-year limitation period. The court found, however, that an exception to the limitations period would have generally applied under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 3 -- 7 (1987) because the timely count (the count not at issue here) was pending against defendant for the same conduct that gave rise to the remaining counts when the latter counts were filed. The court refused to allow this statutory exception to toll the limitations period. However, because the court found the state was required to not only set forth circumstances which, in and of themselves, provided a basis for tolling a limitation period, but the state was also required to make clear that those circumstances were in fact the basis upon which the state sought to toll the limitation period. The indictment at bar contained no language specifying that the limitation period should have been tolled because a prosecution was pending against defendant for the same conduct involved in the counts at issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court ruling because the state failed to make clear the circumstances which were the basis upon which the state sought to toll the limitation period for the three counts at issue. The court remanded the case, however, for the appellate court to address defendant's contention that the evidence in support of his conviction was insufficient.

Condon v. American Tel. & Tel. Co.

Supreme Court of Illinois

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employee sought review, by direct appeal, of a decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which entered a directed verdict in favor of defendant employer in the former employee's action alleging that the employer wrongfully demoted and dismissed him because management employees failed to adhere to the employer's policy directives, and failed to award termination pay.


OVERVIEW: The trial court, in denying rehearing on its decision not to permit the testimony of the former employee's damages expert because the expert's identity had not been disclosed, stated that if Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-1003 were in conflict with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 220(b), 107 Ill. 2d R. 220(b), the statute was unconstitutional. The trial court then granted the directed verdict on the issue of contract liability. The court vacated the trial court's order and transferred the cause to an intermediate appellate court. The court stated that because the trial court had directed a verdict in the employer's favor on the issue of whether the personnel guide was an implied contract, no contract existed as a matter of law, and any issue regarding damages stemming from a breach of the alleged contract was moot. The court noted that the only contention in the former employee's case that could have invoked the jurisdiction of the court for the purpose of direct appeal was the issue of the unconstitutionality of a statute, and stated that the issue was moot.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order on the constitutionality issue, and transferred the former employee's appeal to an intermediate appellate court for review of the remaining issues.

People v. Morris


No. 68971


Supreme Court of Illinois


136 Ill. 2d 157; 554 N.E.2d 235; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 37; 143 Ill. Dec. 300



April 18, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Ronald B. Mehling, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty by the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) of the offense of possession of an altered temporary registration permit in violation Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-104(a)(3). The circuit court held the penalty provided by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95, para. 4-104 (b)(2) unconstitutional in that the penalty was disproportionate to the offense, and the state appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had altered the temporary registration permit for his automobile in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-104(a)(3), which was a Class 2 felony. In affirming, the court concluded the circuit court was correct in holding unconstitutional the penalty of a Class 2 felony for the alteration by an owner of an automobile of the temporary registration permit for that automobile. A Class 2 penalty for a person who altered a temporary registration permit for a vehicle which he or she owned or to which he or she was legally entitled was not reasonably designed to protect automobile owners against theft, nor was it reasonably designed to protect the general public against the commission of crimes involving stolen motor vehicles. Such a penalty was violative of the Due Process Clause of the United States Constitution, and could not stand. The court found that the penalty of a Class 2 felony for altering the temporary registration permit for a vehicle which one owned or to which one was legally entitled violated the guarantee of proportionate penalties in the Illinois Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court that the felony penalty for alteration, by an owner, of an automobile of a temporary registration permit was unconstitutional as applied.

Carpentersville v. Pollution Control Bd.


No. 68074


Supreme Court of Illinois


135 Ill. 2d 463; 553 N.E.2d 362; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 32; 142 Ill. Dec. 848



March 29, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on petition for review of an order of the Pollution Control Board.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant polluter sought review after the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois) reversed appellee Illinois Pollution Control Board's determination, which held that the Environmental Protection Act (the Act), Ill. Rev. Stat., ch. 111 1/2, par. 1001 et seq. (1987), preempted a height restriction in appellee village's zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: After numerous complaints about noxious odors, the polluter sought a permit to modify its plant. The Environmental Protection Agency issued a permit to make the modifications, but imposed several special conditions, one of which was a requirement that the incinerator discharge stack be 100 feet above grade. The village refused to grant a variance. A village zoning ordinance limited the height of structures to 35 feet. The polluter appealed to the board. The board held that the Act preempted the village's zoning ordinance. The village appealed to the appellate court and the appellate court reversed. The court affirmed and held that the Act did not preempt local zoning ordinances. Section 39(c) of the Environmental Protection Act provided that an applicant had to meet and secure all necessary zoning approvals from the unit of government having zoning jurisdiction over the proposed facility. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, par. 1039(c) (1987). The court's contrary holding, that the Act was intended to preempt non-home-rule regulations, was based on the court's interpretation of the Act before enactment of amendments to § 39(c).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Gersch


No. 68199


Supreme Court of Illinois


135 Ill. 2d 384; 553 N.E.2d 281; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 24; 142 Ill. Dec. 767; 58 U.S.L.W. 2650



March 22, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Michael J. Pope, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant appealed the judgment of conviction and the sentence imposed by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). The defendant waived his right to a jury but the state filed its jury demand under § 115-1 of the Illinois Criminal Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-1 (1987). The court accepted jurisdiction under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 302(b), Ill. 2d R. 302(b), because Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-1 (1987) was held unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The defendant waived his right to a jury trial and requested a bench trial on charges of murder and concealment of a homicide. The state invoked its statutory right to a jury, and after the jury trial, the defendant was convicted. While defendant's appeal was pending, the court held Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. § 115-1 to be unconstitutional and the court accepted jurisdiction under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 302(b), Ill. 2d R. 302(b), The court found that the 1987 and 1988 amendments to § 115-1 were held to be unconstitutional violations of a defendant's right to waive trial by jury, and that the Illinois constitution and common law provided for a defendant's waiver to be free from interference by the state. The court held that a denial of retrospective application of the finding of unconstitutionality ignored the ab initio rule of statutory invalidation, that the effect of enacting an unconstitutional amendment was to leave the law in force as it was before the adoption of the amendment, and that the proper remedy was a reversal of the conviction and a remand for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The judgments of conviction and sentence were reversed, and the case against the defendant was remanded for a new trial.

People v. Williams


No. 68487


Supreme Court of Illinois


133 Ill. 2d 449; 551 N.E.2d 631; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 21; 141 Ill. Dec. 444



February 16, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County, the Hon. W. Charles Witte, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) with child abduction,(Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10-5(b)(10)(1961)(law). The trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss on the ground that the law was impermissibly vague. Because the trial court held invalid a statute of the state, the state appealed directly to the court, 107 Ill. 2d R. 603.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the vagueness of the law violated defendant's due process rights, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 (1970). The law stated that a person committed child abduction when he intentionally lured or attempted to lure a child under 16 years of age into a vehicle without the parent's consent for other than a lawful purpose. Defendant on five consecutive days slowly drove his car past a 12-year old girl walking home from school, trying to converse with her and telling her "come on." Defendant argued that the law impaired his free speech rights. The court held that due process required that a criminal statute be clearly defined and provide definite warning as to the proscribed conduct. The law's phrase "for other than a lawful purpose" was not unconstitutionally vague. That phrase implied any action that violated the state's criminal code, not violations of administrative regulations of city ordinances. Attempts using speech to lure children into cars for a criminal purpose was not protected by the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

People v. Fields


Nos. 64276, 64277 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


135 Ill. 2d 18; 552 N.E.2d 791; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 19; 142 Ill. Dec. 200



February 16, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 9, 1990.
Writ of certiorari denied Fields v. Illinois, 498 U.S. 881, 111 S. Ct. 227, 111 S. Ct. 228, 112 L. Ed. 2d 182, 1990 U.S. LEXIS 4709, 59 U.S.L.W. 3250 (1990)
Post-conviction proceeding at People v. Hawkins, 181 Ill. 2d 41, 690 N.E.2d 999, 1998 Ill. LEXIS 7, 228 Ill. Dec. 924 (1998)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Fields v. City of Chicago, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 36410 (N.D. Ill., Apr. 4, 2011)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by People v. Fields, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1066 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Thomas J. Maloney, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted of murder and sentenced to death by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). The defendants' sentences were then stayed pending direct review.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of murder, and their death sentences were stayed pending direct appeal. The court affirmed the judgments and held that the evidence, including three eyewitness accounts, was sufficient to prove defendants guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The trial court did not erred in accepting witness testimony and rejecting subsequent recantation. The court would not substitute its judgment for that of the trier of fact on questions involving the weight of the evidence or the credibility of witnesses. While discrepancies existed, the court could not say that the trial court's conclusion was so unreasonable, improbable, or unsatisfactory as to have raised a reasonable doubt as to defendants' guilt. The record did not support defendants' claim that a joint death penalty hearing made it impossible for the jury to render an individualized sentencing decision. The trial court instructed the jury to give separate consideration to each defendant; therefore, the jury was informed that each defendant was entitled to have his case decided only on the evidence and law applicable to him. The death penalty statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for murder and their death sentences.

People v. Franklin


No. 64838


Supreme Court of Illinois


135 Ill. 2d 78; 552 N.E.2d 743; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 17; 142 Ill. Dec. 152



January 24, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 9, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Frank W. Meekins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, which convicted him of murder pursuant to 1979 Ill. Comp. Stat. 38/9-1(a)(1), (a)(2), and sentenced him to death after a jury concluded that he was eligible for the death penalty, finding there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude such a sentence.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of murder and subsequently found him eligible for the death penalty. Defendant appealed based on various assertions of error regarding the trial and sentencing phases. The court found that the police records did not qualify as evidence under Brady, because they did not contain any information that was either favorable or unfavorable to the defendant. Therefore, there was no due process violation. The circuit court did not abuse its discretion in limiting recross-examination to the scope of the redirect examination nor did it abuse its discretion in allowing a witness to testify about the results of the probable-cause hearing. Defendant waived numerous objections due to procedural default. Defendant was eligible for the death penalty under 1975 Ill. Comp. Stat. 38/9-1(b)(3) regardless of whether he was convicted under § 9-1(a)(1) or § 9-1(a)(2). Finally, the court concluded that while it may not have been necessary to admit all seven photographs into evidence, it could not be said that the admission of each was an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

365 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Healy v. Vaupel


No. 67122


Supreme Court of Illinois


133 Ill. 2d 295; 549 N.E.2d 1240; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 3; 140 Ill. Dec. 368



January 17, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of De Kalb County, the Hon. Rex F. Meilinger, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state employees sought review of a decision of the Appellate Court for the Second District of Illinois upholding a trial court's decision refusing to dismiss appellee victim's personal injury complaint under 107 Ill. 2d R. 315(a). Appellants asserted that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the action and that only the Court of Claims (Illinois) had jurisdiction for an action against state employees.


OVERVIEW: Appellee victim brought an action against appellants state employees based on alleged personal injuries. An appellate court refused to dismiss appellee's complaint under 107 Ill. 2d R. 315(a). The court remanded appellee's action for dismissal of her complaint, finding that the court in which appellee had brought her action lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the matter. Under the Court of Claims Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1987, ch. 37, par. 439.1 - 439.24, the court noted, the Court of Claims (Illinois) had exclusive jurisdiction over matters brought against the State of Illinois in tort. Although appellee's action was technically filed against state employees, the court noted that there had been no allegations they acted beyond the scope of their authority, that the allegedly breached duty was not one owed to the public generally independent of their state employment, and that the alleged actions were within appellants' normal duties. The court, therefore, found the action had effectively been brought against Illinois. The court also found that it had jurisdiction to hear this matter and to grant required relief under 107 Ill. 2d R. 366(a)(5).


OUTCOME: The court remanded appellee victim's action to the lower court for dismissal of her complaint, finding that her action was effectively one brought against a state because it involved activities of state employees acting within the ordinary course of employment. As such, the court found that only the Court of Claims could exercise jurisdiction over this matter. The court noted that it had jurisdiction over the appeal.

People v. Sandoval


No. 68286


Supreme Court of Illinois


135 Ill. 2d 159; 552 N.E.2d 726; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 1; 142 Ill. Dec. 135



January 17, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 9, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. Jack Hoogasian, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court judgment reversed; circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which reversed defendant's conviction for two counts of criminal sexual assault and one count of battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of criminal sexual assault and battery related to his sexual assault of the victim, his former girlfriend. The appellate court reversed the convictions on the grounds that the trial court, under the rape shield statute, improperly excluded evidence of the victim's past sexual activities because the victim waived the statute's protection and that it was error not to allow defendant to impeach the victim's testimony that she had not dated since the incident in order to test her credibility. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the rape shield statute, Ill. Comp. Stat. § 38/115-7, was clear and unambiguous and left no room for introduction of reputation or specific-act evidence from any party. The court held that defendant's right to confrontation was not violated by the exclusion of such testimony because testimony regarding the victim's prior sexual history was not relevant to the matter being tried, which was defendant's alleged sexual assault on victim. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in limiting defendant's impeachment of the victim's testimony because the testimony related to a collateral matter.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which convicted defendant.

Santiago v. Kusper


No. 67704


Supreme Court of Illinois


133 Ill. 2d 318; 549 N.E.2d 1251; 1990 Ill. LEXIS 8; 140 Ill. Dec. 379



January 17, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. George M. Marovich, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered; appellate court judgment vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner filed a claim against defendants, county officials, as a class action in equity for a declaratory judgment finding that the county officials had, for several years, required payment of unlawful taxes described as costs. The Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) reversed the trial court's order that denied the county officials motion to dismiss. The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowner owned a parcel of real estate and failed to pay the general real estate taxes assessed on the land in for 1984. After his failure to make payment on the due date of the second installment, he received notice that he had to pay the taxes due, plus accrued interest and costs, in order to avoid legal action. Upon his failure to respond to the notice, the landowner's name was included among a list of landowners that had failed to remit their 1984 real estate taxes. A judgment and order of sale against those properties on the application list was entered. On January 31, 1986, pursuant to the judgment, the landowner's taxes were sold for a sum, which included an assessment of $ 10 for "costs." The landowner redeemed the property from the tax sale for a price, which included the $ 10 charge, and filed a protest against the fee. He also filed this class action. The court held that the county officials had the discretion to determine the cost incurred when providing the landowner notice of delinquency by certified mail prior to the tax date.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the appellate court and remanded the case.

People ex rel. Braver v. Wash.


1-97-4693


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


311 Ill. App. 3d 179; 724 N.E.2d 68; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 953; 243 Ill. Dec. 759



December 30, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 25, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Thomas R. Fitzgerald, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal challenging an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), granting appellee's petition for "writ" of mandamus, seeking an award of meritorious good time credits by appellant sufficient to result in appellee's immediate release from prison, and denying appellant's motion to vacate the granting order.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was convicted of unlawfully using weapons and sentenced to a State prison term. Unable to make bail, appellee served 217 days in county jail prior to sentencing. Upon transfer to the State penitentiary, appellee was required to serve a total of 276 days in jail, which exceeded his 270-day sentence. Appellee argued the State's policy of requiring each inmate to serve at least 61 days in the State penitentiary, regardless of the amount of jail time the inmate had spent in a county jail, violated an inmate's rights to equal protection and due process. The trial court agreed and ordered the State to release appellant immediately. On appeal, the court reversed, holding the trial court's judgment was against the manifest weight of the evidence because the award of meritorious good time credit was not automatic but was given to eligible inmates, based upon appellant's discretion after considering numerous factors.


OUTCOME: Order of mandamus was reversed; the lower court improperly usurped appellant's authority by exercising the discretion that the legislature had given solely to appellant to determine whether to award meritorious good time to inmates, reducing their prison sentences.

Board of Educ. v. Brown


No. 1-98-1169 (Consolidated with Case Nos. 1-98-1748 and 1-98-2221)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


311 Ill. App. 3d 478; 724 N.E.2d 956; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 957; 244 Ill. Dec. 68



December 30, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 29, 2000. Released for Publication March 14, 2000. Certiorari Denied October 30, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 7068.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 95 CH 9540. Honorable John K. Madden, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendants' petition to detach their small residential real estate development from one township and annex to another township pursuant to 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7-2b.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, residents of a small residential real estate development and subdivision, sought to detach the development from one township and annex to another township pursuant to 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7-2b. Plaintiffs, the first township and the former president of that township's board of education, objected to the detachment on constitutional grounds. The Joint Board denied detachment, but the circuit court reversed. On appeal, plaintiffs argued defendants' petitions were invalid because certain signers failed to include a proper statement of their addresses. The court found that the identity of each and every individual could be readily determined by the name and street address when read in conjunction with the remaining contents of the petition and therefore it held the signatures to be valid. Further, the signatures were collected and timely filed in accordance with 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7-1. The signatures were not stale and defendants' petition was sufficient as a matter of law. As to the constitutional claims, the court remanded for further hearings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and vacated in part. The cause was remanded to determine constitutional issues. The signatures on defendants' petition to detach were valid because the identity of each individual could be determined in conjunction with the other contents of the petition.

People v. Brown

371 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Hartmarx Corp. v. Bower


No. 1-98-2309


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


309 Ill. App. 3d 959; 723 N.E.2d 820; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 907; 243 Ill. Dec. 517



December 23, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 19, 2000. Released for Publication February 15, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE JOANNE L. LANIGAN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed an order of the circuit court of Cook County (Illinois) affirming the decision that sales shipped from Illinois by a member of plaintiff's unitary business group to purchasers located outside Illinois should be "thrown back" to Illinois for inclusion in a combined Illinois sales factor, and assessed penalties.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff Delaware corporation with a principal place of business in Illinois was part of a nationwide unitary business group. Defendant ruled that the "throwback rule" applied to sales of goods by member of plaintiff's unitary business group that were shipped from Illinois to customers in other states where such members were not subject to taxation, but where other members of the group were subject to taxation. Defendant also assessed penalties for failure to include such sales in taxable income. The appellate court reversed as to assessed penalties for one tax year. The court otherwise affirmed the ruling, concluding that if the economic activity of plaintiff was not taxable in the destination states, it was taxable in the shipping State of Illinois using the throwback rule; 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 502(e) did not require a unitary business group to be treated as a single "person"; apportionment focused on "business activity," and shipping was included in such activity.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed as to penalties imposed for one tax year. The judgment was otherwise affirmed. The "throwback rule" applied to plaintiff's economic activity, which included its shipping activity; if the activity was not taxable in the states to where its products were shipped, then the activity was taxable in the shipping state of Illinois.

People v. Campbell


NO. 4-98-0532


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


309 Ill. App. 3d 423; 721 N.E.2d 1225; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 875; 242 Ill. Dec. 694


July 29, 1999, Submitted  
December 16, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 14, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 97CF495. Honorable Sue E. Myerscough, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), in which a jury convicted defendant of attempt (armed robbery), 720 Ill Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/8-4, 18-2(a) (West 1998), and two counts of first degree murder, 720 Ill Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-1(a) (1) , (a) (2) (West 1998).


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of attempt (armed robbery) and two counts of first degree murder. On appeal, defendant raised several issues, but the court affirmed the conviction, finding no reversible error. The trial court did not commit prejudicial error by allowing the appellee state to refer to him by his nickname, "Psycho," because it was introduced only for the relevant purpose of establishing defendant's identity. The law enacting the residual hearsay statute, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-10.2, did not violate the single subject rule of Ill. Const. 1970, art. IV, § 8(d), and was not unconstitutional, so the statute itself was constitutional. The statement admitted into evidence under that statute contained sufficient guarantees of trustworthiness to satisfy the statute and U.S. Const. amend. VI, considering the totality of circumstances. Defendant claimed appellee violated the notice requirements, but failed to show he was unfairly prejudiced.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed; statement admitted into evidence under the residual hearsay statute, which was found to be constitutional, contained sufficient guarantees of trustworthiness under the totality of circumstances; defendant's nickname was used to establish identity, so was not prejudicial error.

OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sued the owner of Wrigley Field, Chicago National League Ball Club (the Cubs), after he was struck by a foul ball during a baseball game. McCann v. Presswood


No. 4-99-0423


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


308 Ill. App. 3d 1068; 721 N.E.2d 811; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 843; 242 Ill. Dec. 532



December 8, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 6, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Logan County. No. 98L22. Honorable Stephen R. Pacey, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action against defendant alleging two counts of common-law negligence and two counts of intentional misconduct, plaintiff appealed the judgment of the Logan County Circuit Court (Illinois) that dismissed plaintiff's intentional misconduct counts with prejudice.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed an amended complaint against defendant for property damage. Counts II and IV of plaintiff's amended complaint were supposedly based on an intentional misconduct theory rather than negligence. Plaintiff requested punitive damages in counts II and IV of the amended complaint. The trial court dismissed counts II and IV with prejudice, finding that plaintiff violated § 2-604.1 of the Code of Civil Procedure, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. § 5/2-604.1 (West 1994), by requesting punitive damages in his amended complaint. The court affirmed, holding that § 2-604.1 precluded plaintiff from requesting punitive damages on the face of any complaint based, even in part, on a negligence theory. The court found no abuse of discretion by the trial court in dismissing counts II and IV, considering plaintiff's repeated disregard of § 2-604.1 and his refusal of the trial court's offer to conduct a hearing to determine whether sufficient facts existed to support a punitive damages claim.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. The Code of Civil Procedure precluded plaintiff from requesting punitive damages on the face of any complaint based, even in part, on a negligence theory.

People v. Noble


No. 3-98-0785


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT

December 1, 1999, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois. No. 97-CF-767. Honorable Robert A. Barnes Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois, which found him guilty, but mentally ill, of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for killing his wife by forcing her head under water in a marsh. Defendant was assessed as mentally ill but not insane, since his mental illness did not affect him to the extent he was unable to appreciate the wrongfulness of his behavior. Around the time of defendant's psychiatric evaluations, Public Act 89--404 was declared unconstitutional. Prior to that, defendant merely had the burden of proving his insanity by a preponderance of the evidence. The new legislation had the effect of increasing defendant's burden of proof to a clear and convincing evidence standard. The court reversed and remanded, holding that under the circumstances, defendant did not have a fair opportunity to weigh his option of raising an insanity defense under the statute applicable to his offense.


OUTCOME: Conviction reversed and remanded; the court held that under the circumstances, defendant did not have a fair opportunity to weigh his option of raising an insanity defense under the statute applicable to his offense.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Stephenson County (Illinois), which convicted and sentenced him for aggravated battery, home invasion, and aggravated arson.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of aggravated battery, for which he was sentenced to five years' imprisonment; home invasion, for which he was sentenced to 30 years imprisonment; and aggravated arson, for which he was sentenced to 25 years imprisonment, to be served consecutively. DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Coles County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder, finding that defendant knew his acts would create a strong probability of death and that defendant killed while committing a forcible felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with several counts of first-degree murder for a drowning death. After trial, the jury acquitted defendant of one count, but found defendant guilty of two others. The trial court entered a conviction, and defendant appealed, raising issues concerning speedy trial, ineffective assistance of counsel, jury instructions, and good-time credit concerning his sentence. The court held that because defendant's right to a speedy trial was tolled, had his attorney moved to dismiss the charges on speedy trial grounds, the motion would have been denied. Therefore, defendant failed to establish the prejudice prong under Strickland and his ineffective assistance of counsel claim failed. The court also held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing an instruction on second-degree murder, or on involuntary manslaughter, but that defendant was entitled to calculation of day-for-day credit, as it existed prior to any truth-in-sentencing amendments.


OUTCOME: Affirmed and remanded with directions; defendant's right to speedy trial was tolled, had his attorney moved to dismiss on speedy trial grounds, it would have been denied, thus he failed to establish prejudice prong of his ineffective assistance of counsel claim.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from the conviction entered in the Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois) for burglary and theft of property having a value less than $ 300. Appellant was sentenced to 10 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of burglary and theft, and he was later sentenced to 10 years in prison. Appellant contested, arguing that (1) Ill. Pub. Act 89-689 [Pub. Act 89-689, § 90, eff. Dec. 31, 1996 (1996 Ill. Laws 3775, 3792-93)], was unconstitutional because it violated the single subject rule of the Ill. Const. 1970, art. People v. Foster


Nos. 1-97-1556 & 1-97-2117 (consolidated)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


309 Ill. App. 3d 1; 722 N.E.2d 658; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 808; 242 Ill. Dec. 874; 242 Ill. Dec. 874



November 22, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 25, 2000.
Related proceeding at People v. Luckett, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 572 (Ill. App. Ct., May 9, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Stanley Sacks, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; sentence vacated and original sentence reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed the denial of his motion to suppress and trial court's resentencing of him, entered by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), in a case where he was charged with first-degree murder, three counts of attempted first-degree murder and three counts of aggravated discharge of a firearm.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant was charged with first-degree murder, three counts of attempted first-degree murder and three counts of aggravated discharge of a firearm. He was convicted on five of the counts. The trial court originally sentenced defendant to concurrent terms of 18, 17, 17, 10 and 10 years in prison. Defendant filed a notice of appeal. Plaintiff State filed a motion to reconsider. The trial court granted the plaintiff's motion, resentenced defendant to 35 years and concluded the sentences should run consecutively. Defendant appealed. The court vacated the trial court's resentencing order and ordered the original sentences reinstated. The court held once the notice of appeal was filed, the trial court lacked jurisdiction to enter its resentencing order. The court also held the original sentences were proper because the crimes were not committed as part of a single course of conduct, as required by the consecutive sentencing statute.


OUTCOME: Ruling denying criminal defendant's motion to suppress affirmed and convictions affirmed, but resentencing order imposing consecutive sentences vacated and original valid order sentencing defendant to concurrent terms reinstated because trial court did not have jurisdiction to enter resentencing order since defendant filed valid notice of appeal that preceded the order.

Johnson v. Illinois Dep't of Prof'l Regulation

November 8, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 7, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County Nos. 98MR66, 98MR67. Honorable Luther H. Dearborn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), affirming the decision of defendant, Illinois Department of Professional Regulation, which rejected plaintiffs' applications for licensing as private detectives because plaintiffs failed to satisfy statutory qualifications required of private detectives.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs applied to defendant, Illinois Department of Professional Regulation, for licensing as private detectives. Defendant rejected the applications because plaintiffs failed to satisfy statutory qualifications required of private detectives. The circuit court affirmed the decision. On appeal, the court cited a two-part test to determine whether the apprenticeship provision of the Private Detective, Private Alarm, Private Security, and Locksmith Act of 1993 (Act), 225 Ill Comp. Stat. 446/75 (a) (6), was constitutionally valid. The act conferred a monopolistic right to instruct, and the apprenticeship was not calculated to enhance the expertise of prospective licensees. Thus, in applying the test, the court found the Act, as interpreted by defendant, to violate both prongs of the test, and was invalid.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded with directions. The court held that the statute, as interpreted by defendant, was invalid. The court reversed the decision of the circuit court, set aside the decision of defendant, and remanded cause to defendant with directions that plaintiffs shall be allowed to sit for the licensing examination.

 

381 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Gersch v. Ill. Dep't of Prof'l Regulation


No. 1-98-1291


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


308 Ill. App. 3d 649; 720 N.E.2d 672; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 770; 242 Ill. Dec. 51



November 5, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 97 CH 11748. Honorable Albert Green, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which affirmed a final administrative decision by the Illinois Department of Professional Regulation which ordered a non-disciplinary cancellation of the plaintiff's registration as a licensed clinical social worker.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a social worker since 1959, was classified as a certified social worker in 1969. In 1989, the state enacted legislation, without a grandfather clause, requiring advanced education for higher tiered "certified social workers." Defendant department discovered that plaintiff's higher tier license had been erroneously issued and filed an administrative complaint. Upon recommendation by the administrative law judge, defendant cancelled plaintiff's license and ordered a lower tier one. The lower court affirmed. On appeal, the court affirmed; pursuit of a profession was not a fundamental right so, under the rational basis test, the legislation's educational mandates bore a rational relationship to the legitimate purpose of protecting the public and were neither arbitrary nor discriminatory. The defendant had the authority to rescind or cancel plaintiff's license; given its wide latitude, defendant's decision was not against the manifest weight of the evidence; neither equitable estoppel or laches barred the decision.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; plaintiff's pursuit of his profession was not a fundamental right; higher educational mandates bore a rational relationship to the legitimate purpose of public protection and were not arbitrary or discriminatory. Evidence supported the decision, estoppel and laches were not applicable, defendant acted within its authority.

People v. Jaramillo


No. 2-97-0938


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 96--CF--71. Honorable Judith M. Brawka, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed from a denial of his motion to reduce sentence and his conviction pursuant to a guilty plea of one count of predatory criminal sexual assault entered by the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) in a case where defendant was sentenced to 20 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant was originally indicted for three counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault. The offenses leading to his conviction occurred between December 26, 1995 and January 10, 1996. He was indicted again in December of 1996 for predatory criminal sexual assault. Later, he plead guilty to one count of predatory criminal sexual assault. He was sentenced to 20 years in prison. The trial court denied his motion to reduce sentence. Defendant appealed. He argued his conviction had to be vacated because the offense of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child was unconstitutional. The court held the statute as applied was invalid. The court held the last act leading to defendant's conviction occurred in January of 1996, but the predatory criminal sexual assault statute did not go in effect until May of 1996. Since his conviction was reversed, the court held the issue regarding his sentence was moot.


OUTCOME: Judgment of conviction reversed and issue regarding sentence held to be moot because the offense for which criminal defendant was convicted was not in effect when defendant committed the assault.

People v. Daniels


No. 2-98-0589


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


307 Ill. App. 3d 917; 718 N.E.2d 1064; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 726; 241 Ill. Dec. 210


March 30, 1999, Assigned; April 6, 1999, Submitted  
October 13, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 12, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 97--CF--2622. Honorable Stephen E. Walter, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from conviction entered by Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) for the crime of unlawful delivery of less than one gram of cocaine within 1,000 feet of a church (Illinois Controlled Substances Act, 401 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/ 401(d) (1996)).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of unlawful delivery of less than one gram of a controlled substance on a public way within 1,000 feet of a church. On appeal, defendant argued that the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/407(b) (1996), violated the establishment clause of U.S. Const. amend. I, as well as Ill. Const. 1970, art. I § 3. The appellate court affirmed, and applied a test to determine the statute's constitutionality. The statute must have a secular legislative purpose; its main effect must be one that does not advance or inhibit religion; and it must not foster excessive entanglement with religion. It need contain only one of these defects to be unconstitutional. The appellate court held the statute was constitutional. Also, plaintiff was not required to prove that defendant knew that he committed the offense on a public way within 1,000 feet of a church.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the circuit court was affirmed. The statute governing unlawful delivery of less than one gram of a controlled substance on a public way within 1,000 feet of a church was not unconstitutional and did not violate the establishment clause.

People v. Kauffman


No. 1-97-1849


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


308 Ill. App. 3d 1; 719 N.E.2d 275; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 697; 241 Ill. Dec. 414



September 30, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 30, 1999. As Corrected October 14, 1999. Released for Publication November 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Gerald T. Rohrer, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her second degree murder conviction in Cook County Circuit Court, Illinois, and from her sentence to a five-year term of probation, claiming several errors in the jury instructions given and contesting the denial of her motion to admit into evidence information on the victim's propensity for violence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of second degree murder and appealed, alleging errors in the jury instructions given. The court found that the second degree murder instruction was properly given if the evidence presented at defendant's trial raised a factual issue as to that offense. The court further found that the jury was improperly instructed in receiving the wrong instruction which did not provide for a general "not guilty" verdict form. The jury received conflicting instructions due to the combination of instructions from series "A" and series "B" of the Illinois Pattern Jury Instructions. The court found that departure from the pattern instructions was not warranted and that the compound errors that occurred undermined the reliability of the verdict, denying defendant a fair trial. The court also held that because the victim's entry was not unlawful, the defense of defense of dwelling was unavailable to defendant.


OUTCOME: Remanded for new trial because departure from the pattern instructions was not warranted and the compound errors that occurred undermined the reliability of the verdict, denying defendant a fair trial.

Van Hattem v. Kmart Corp.


1-98-2423


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


308 Ill. App. 3d 121; 719 N.E.2d 212; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 704; 241 Ill. Dec. 351



September 30, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Donald J. O'Brien, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) ruling in plaintiff's favor in a case alleging that defendant pharmacy misfilled a prescription, resulting in a wrongful death. Defendant claimed error in court's denial of motion for mistrial and other errors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pharmacy appealed a judgment in plaintiff survivors' claims of wrongful death, contending that the trial court erred in failing to grant a mistrial due to prejudice from a television news story about pharmacy misfills which aired during the week of trial, refusing a special interrogatory regarding contributory negligence, admitting evidence without a chain of custody, and in allowing testimony from two expert witnesses. The court found that the television program was palpably prejudicial, particularly its timing, and was of such character and magnitude as to deprive defendant of a fair trial. The court also found that although the special interrogatory did not test the general verdict, it provided means by which the jury's award could be distributed consistent with its finding of contributory negligence. It was within the discretion of the circuit court to admit the disputed evidence. The testimony of the two experts was correctly allowed.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the circuit court reversed and cause remanded for new trial because television program was prejudicial and was of character and magnitude as to deprive defendant of fair trial.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County's (Illinois) grant of summary judgment against him and in favor of defendants, in an action regarding breach of fiduciary duties by an attorney.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was sued civilly and prosecuted criminally, and was convicted of various criminal charges. The court also refused to apply the actual innocence rule, and held that damages for emotional distress were recoverable.

People v. Rokicki


No. 2-98-0256


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


307 Ill. App. 3d 645; 718 N.E.2d 333; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 675; 240 Ill. Dec. 852


April 8, 1999, Assigned; April 27, 1999, Submitted  
September 28, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 29, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 95--CF--2295. Honorable James T. Doyle, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed Circuit Court of Kane County's (Illinois) conviction for a hate crime under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12--7.1 (West 1994) based on the predicate offense of disorderly conduct, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/26--1(a) (1) (West 1994).


OVERVIEW: Defendant yelled, pounded his fists on the counter, and called victim epithets at a restaurant where victim worked. Defendant was arrested for disorderly conduct and charged with a hate crime, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12--7.1 (West 1994). The court held that defendant remained free to believe what he wanted, but he could not force his opinions on others by shouting, pounding on a counter, and disrupting a lawful business. The court held that the hate crime statute required conduct beyond mere expression and that the statute constitutionally regulated conduct without infringing upon free speech. The court held that the hate crime statute was not facially unconstitutional when the predicate offense was disorderly conduct because the statute reached only conduct and did not punish speech itself; the statute did not impermissibly discriminate based on content; and the statute did not chill the exercise of U.S. Const. amend. I rights.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed; the hate crime statute was not facially unconstitutional when the predicate offense was disorderly conduct because (1) it reached only conduct and did not punish speech itself; (2) it did not impermissibly discriminate based on content; and (3) it did not chill the exercise of first amendment rights.

People v. Scales


NO. 5-97-0273


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


307 Ill. App. 3d 356; 718 N.E.2d 281; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 679; 240 Ill. Dec. 800



September 28, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rule 23 Order Redesignated Opinion and Ordered Published September 28, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County. No. 96-CF-266. Honorable Patrick J. Hitpas, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed from the Circuit Court of Marion County (Illinois) his convictions of residential burglary and armed violence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of residential burglary and armed violence and sentenced on both charges. He failed to show diligence in securing alibi witnesses for trial or to establish prejudice from denial of request for a continuance to secure alibi witnesses. The court concluded defendant was proved guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The penalty for armed violence based on residential burglary violated the proportionate-penalties provision contained in Ill. Const. art. I, § 11. Accordingly, the court vacated defendant's conviction for armed violence based on residential burglary. The sentencing court was not given the option of considering an extended-term sentence on defendant's residential burglary conviction. In light of the vacation of defendant's conviction for armed violence, the matter was remanded for resentencing so that the trial court could consider all permissible sentencing alternatives on the residential burglary conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence for armed violence vacated and conviction for residential burglary affirmed and remanded for resentencing on the residential burglary conviction. The sentencing court was not given the option of considering an extended-term sentence on defendant's residential burglary conviction.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. Nos. 97--CF--2078, 97--CF--2079. Honorable Rosemary Collins, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from his conviction and sentence by the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) under an invalidated truth-in-sentencing statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to two charges of criminal sexual assault. In exchange for defendant's guilty plea, the state dismissed other charges which could have imposed mandatory consecutive sentences. The trial court accepted the plea, imposed two consecutive terms, ordered defendant to serve 85% of his aggregate sentence pursuant to the truth-in-sentencing statute, and then told defendant that he had 30 days either to file a motion to withdraw his guilty plea or a motion requesting the court to reconsider his sentence. Because defendant did not file a motion to withdraw his guilty plea, the trial court denied defendant's motion to reconsider. Defendant appealed. The appellate court held that claims of an unconstitutional sentence were not waived, modified defendant's sentence in light of the invalidated statute and remanded the cause for the trial court to admonish defendant of his right to move to withdraw his guilty plea and vacate his sentence.


OUTCOME: Sentence affirmed as modified to reflect his eligibility for good-conduct credit while incarcerated under relevant statute; remanded with directions to the circuit court for new admonishments and assurances that defense counsel strictly comply with the new admonishments before the court would grant a hearing.

In re Marriage of Duffy


No. 2-98-1290


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT
