June 29, 1999, Assigned; August 4, 1999, Submitted  
September 16, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 21, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of De Kalb County. No. 98-D-261. Honorable Wiley W. Edmondson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of De Kalb County (Illinois), modifying the parties' joint parenting agreement in a divorce action.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner and respondent's joint parenting agreement provided that mediation of disputes regarding their child was encouraged but the parties could opt out of mediation provisions without cause. The trial court entered an order dissolving parties' marriage but modified the dispute resolution provision of the incorporated parenting agreement, ordering mediation of any future child custody disputes. Petitioner appealed, arguing the trial court abused its discretion because it lacked authority to modify the parties' agreement regarding custody. The court affirmed because the trial court was in the best position to determine the best interests of the child; requiring mediation preserved the resources of the parties, leaving them available to meet their child's needs, and did not pit the parties against one another. Thus, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in modifying the parties' parenting agreement.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because trial court was in best position to determine child's best interests and requiring mediation preserved the resources of the parties, leaving them available to meet their child's needs. Thus, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in modifying the parties' parenting agreement.

People v. Smith


No. 1-98-1323


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


307 Ill. App. 3d 414; 718 N.E.2d 640; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 633; 241 Ill. Dec. 69



September 7, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 27, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable James D. Egan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), arguing that charges of indecent solicitation of a child must be dismissed because statute was void and unconstitutional as it failed to include sentence for offense of indecent solicitation of a child based on predatory criminal sexual assault of a child.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff alleged that defendant solicited two children under age 13 to have sexual intercourse, an act which if completed would be predatory criminal sexual assault of a child. The trial court found defendant "not not guilty" and ordered that defendant be remanded to the department of mental health for treatment. On appeal, defendant argued that the statute was void and unconstitutional as it failed to include a sentence for the offense. On appeal, the court construed the indecent solicitation of a child statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-6 (West 1996), and concluded that the only logical reading of the statute was to classify the predicate act of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child as a class 4 felony. The legislative intent was clear from the statute and the penalty section of the statute should be read to include "predatory criminal sexual assault of a child."


OUTCOME: Affirmed. The legislature intended to classify indecent solicitation of a child based upon predatory criminal sexual assault of a child as a class 4 felony, and the court corrected the deficiency within the statute.

People v. Jaudon


Nos. 1-97-0046, 1-97-1125, 1-97-1192, 1-97-1193, 1-97-1748, 1-97-1776, 1-97-1777, 1-97-1914 (cons.)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


307 Ill. App. 3d 427; 718 N.E.2d 647; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 634; 241 Ill. Dec. 76



September 7, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 27, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Walter Williams, Judge Presiding. Honorable Clarence Bryant, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Nos. 1-97-0046, 1-97-1125, 1-97-1192, 1-97-1193, 1-97-1748, 1-97-1777, 1-97-1914, Orders vacated. No. 1-97-1776, Judgment reversed. As Corrected September 22, 1999.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which denied its motion to vacate a release order on defendant's impounded vehicle and held plaintiff's counsel in contempt for failing to release the impounded vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were arrested and charged in separate criminal cases with various weapons-related violations. The plaintiff city seized and impounded the vehicles defendants were driving. At the probable cause hearings the judges ordered the city to release the impounded vehicles. Plaintiff moved to vacate the release orders. The trial court denied or struck each motion to vacate and subsequently held the City's Law Department and the city's then Corporation Counsel individually in contempt for refusing to return one defendant's vehicle. On appeal, the court determined the home-rule municipal ordinance was constitutional; the trial court lacked authority to order release of the vehicles seized pursuant to that municipal ordinance; the trial courts lacked subject matter jurisdiction to order release of the vehicles because there was no exhaustion of the city's administrative adjudication process; and the civil contempt judgment was void. The court vacated the lower court's orders and reversed the judgment of contempt.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; home-rule municipal ordinance constitutional; court lacked authority to order release of vehicles seized pursuant to ordinance; court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to order release of the vehicles because there was no exhaustion of administrative process; civil contempt judgment was void.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent appealed from the order by the Circuit Court of Monroe County (Illinois) which granted petitioner's petition for election contest and declared petitioner to be the coroner of Monroe County.


OVERVIEW: After an election for county coroner in which he lost by two votes, petitioner filed a petition for election contest. Respondent, the winner, filed a motion to dismiss the petition, claiming that it was insufficient in law because it failed to include an assertion that a recount would change the results. The trial court gave petitioner time to amend his petition, which he did. After a hearing to recount the votes, the parties stipulated that many votes were uninitialed, and petitioner filed a motion for summary judgment arguing that those votes were not to be counted, which the court granted. On respondent's request for a recount, the trial court ordered that petitioner had won. On respondent's appeal, the court affirmed; it held that the amended petition related back to the original, so it was timely filed. More importantly, the law mandated that the uninitialed ballots could not be counted.


OUTCOME: Order declaring election result after recount was affirmed. Petitioner's amended, election petition related back to the original, so it was timely filed; case and statutory law mandated that uninitialed ballots could not be counted.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his sentencing by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), for attempted first degree murder and armed violence predicated upon the offense of aggravated battery causing permanent disability.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted first degree murder and armed violence predicated upon the offense of aggravated battery causing permanent disability. OUTCOME: Affirmed; attempted murder and aggravated battery were based on separate acts. Massie v. Minor

August 31, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 14, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County. No. 97-LM-213. Honorable David L. Sauer, Judge, presiding. Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County. No. 98-LM-29. Honorable David L. Sauer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 97-LM-213: Reversed. No. 98-LM-29: Reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants appealed from the refusal by the Circuit Court of Marion County (Illinois) to dismiss on the basis of res judicata a suit brought against appellant attorney in Illinois for money due on a written contract, and the refusal to register a Mississippi judgment obtained by appellant law firm.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was executor for the estate of an Illinois resident who sued appellant attorney in Illinois under a contract which provided that any legal action would be brought in Illinois. Appellant attorney's firm then sued in Mississippi for breach of contract and obtained a default judgment. Appellant attorney and law firm moved to dismiss the Illinois complaint on the basis of res judicata, and petitioned for registration of the Mississippi judgment pursuant to the Uniform Enforcement of Foreign Judgments Act, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-650 et seq. (West 1996). The trial court found that the Mississippi judgment had been procured by fraud, in part because the Mississippi court was informed neither of the contract's venue provision nor of the Illinois suit. The court reversed because the trial court's findings involved intrinsic rather than extrinsic fraud, and were not a proper basis for denying full faith and credit.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded; trial court's findings of fraud were insufficient to deny full faith and credit to Mississippi judgment, where all of the findings of fraud were matters that could have been raised in the Mississippi proceeding.

People v. Peterson


No. 2-97-0017


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


306 Ill. App. 3d 1091; 715 N.E.2d 1221; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 591; 240 Ill. Dec. 164


July 27, 1998, Assigned; September 10, 1998, Submitted  
August 19, 1999, Filed


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied April 17, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 2746. Released for Publication September 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, Illinois. Nos. 96--CF--552, 96--CF--553. Honorable J. Todd Kennedy, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed judgments of guilty but mentally ill in the Circuit Court of Lake County, Illinois, alleging numerous errors including insufficient evidence to support convictions under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-6 (1996), violation of constitutional rights to freedom of speech, religion, due process and a fair trial, and ineffective counsel.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendants husband and wife guilty but mentally ill (GBMI) of intimidation, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-6 (West 1996), and threatening public officials, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-9 (West 1996). The defendants were sentenced to concurrent five-year terms of imprisonment for intimidation, but the convictions for threatening a public official were vacated. The appellate court affirmed the convictions, holding that the letters which the defendants wrote provided sufficient evidence to support the conviction of intimidation beyond a reasonable doubt; that the application of the GBMI statute was constitutional; that the letters were threats designed to coerce the victims to comply with defendants' wishes and thus, not constitutionally protected speech or free exercise of religion under U.S. Const. amend. I. The appellate court further rejected the arguments that defense counsel was ineffective and victim testimony was improperly admitted, its relevance going directly to the letters' tendency to create apprehension.


OUTCOME: Convictions of threats and intimidation affirmed, because the letters that defendants themselves wrote provided sufficient evidence to support the judgment of guilty but mentally ill and threatening letters not constitutionally protected speech or protected as the free exercise of religion under U.S. Const. amend. I.

 

399 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Brown & Kerr v. American Stores Props.


No. 1-98-3749


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


306 Ill. App. 3d 1023; 715 N.E.2d 804; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 566; 240 Ill. Dec. 117



August 6, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released For Publication September 13, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Clifford L. Meacham, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a corporation and a construction company, challenged orders of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granting partial summary judgment to appellee subcontractor on appellee's breach of contract claim, denying appellants' motion for attorney fees, and denying appellants' motions to reconsider these rulings.


OVERVIEW: Appellee subcontractor brought suit against appellants, a corporation and a construction company, alleging that appellants breached a subcontract by failing to pay appellee for its subcontracting work. Appellee also requested judgment pursuant to the Mechanic Lien Act, 770 Ill. Comp. Stat. 60/28 (1996). Appellants counterclaimed, alleging that because appellee refused to provide guarantees, sworn statements, and a final lien waiver and release as required by the contract, it was not entitled to any further payment. The trial court granted appellee's motion for partial summary judgment as to the breach of contract claim. It granted appellants' motion for judgment on the pleadings as to the mechanics lien count. The court denied all requests for attorney fees, noting that both sides won and lost. The court denied the parties' motions for reconsideration. The appellate court affirmed, holding that the record demonstrated that appellee had a claim for breach of contract to the extent of the base contract. As to attorney fees, the appellate court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding that the case was a draw and, therefore, in not awarding fees.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed an order granting partial summary judgment to appellee subcontractor on appellee's breach of contract claim where it held that record demonstrated that appellee had a claim for breach of contract to the extent of the base contract. The court also affirmed the trial court's denial of appellants' motion for attorney fees where it found that case was a draw and therefore neither side was entitled to fees.

 

400 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Bus. Serv. Bureau v. Martin


NO. 4-98-0894


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


306 Ill. App. 3d 907; 715 N.E.2d 764; 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 557; 240 Ill. Dec. 77


June 22, 1999, Submitted  
August 5, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 3, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 97SC804. Honorable Donald R. Parkinson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which denied defendant's motion to vacate a job search order, made pursuant to Ill. Code Civ. P. § 2-1402, following a judgment against defendant for unpaid medical expenses.


OVERVIEW: A trial court entered a civil judgment for plaintiff against defendant for unpaid medical expenses plus costs and interest. Supplementary proceedings to discover assets followed, and the trial court ordered defendant to search for employment. Following a hearing, the trial court denied defendant's motion to vacate the job search order. On appeal, the court vacated the job search order because, under the clear and unambiguous language of Ill. Code Civ. P. § 2-1402(a), no provision for creating or ordering the creation of assets existed. Section 2-1402 did not by its terms provide for job search orders or otherwise imply that such orders were appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to vacate the trial court's job search order following a civil judgment against defendant for unpaid medical expenses because there was no authority for creating or ordering the creation of assets.
